# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 15

## 526

526

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, a man of fine character and accomplishments, whose work is the work of Hashem, etc., Rabbi Dovid, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification that you have rented an apartment in close proximity to the institution where you serve in holiness, to educate the children of Yisrael in the purity of holiness, through the study of Torah imbued with yiras shamayim and guidance in the fulfillment of mitzvos.

May it be Hashem’s will that the statement of our Sages, "A beautiful dwelling expands a person's mind," be fulfilled in this home—a "pure mind" in the language of the Rambam, and "higher consciousness" (da'as elyon) in the language of Chassidus. Through this, the saying of our Sages is fulfilled: "If you have acquired knowledge (da'as), what do you lack?"

For then, the vessels of the dwelling, all matters pertaining to the dwelling, and those who dwell within it, will be worthy of being a dwelling for the "Higher Man," as it were (see Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 6, 22b).

This is the task of every single man and woman of Yisrael: to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling in the lower worlds, as it is written, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell within them"—within each and every one of Yisrael.

And merit is brought about through meritorious days—the days of building a home in Yisrael, the days of your wedding, in a good and auspicious hour.

May the Creator of man establish your building as an everlasting edifice, founded upon Torah and mitzvos, imbued with the light and vitality of Chassidus.

With blessings of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov.

#### ***526***

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copies of the original correspondence. They are not marked with footnotes unless the source is different, or if they have already been printed in Likkutei Sichos.

**Rabbi Dovid:** Shochat, Toronto.

## 5227

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, engaged in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments, etc., R' Boruch, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I am in receipt of your letter, in which you write regarding your holy work in preparing for the publication of Maseches Pesachim, comparing the various versions from several manuscripts, accompanied by an extensive explanation of the words of the Rishonim, and including the commentaries of the Rishonim on this tractate with notes and emendations.

May it be the will of Hashem that what Hashem desires shall succeed in your hand, to uncover mysteries and hidden treasures in our Torah, especially in this tractate, as many of its matters touch upon practical halacha. Among them, in the language of the Alter Rebbe, is the severe Torah prohibition of chametz, regarding which the Torah was stringent concerning *bal yera'eh* and *bal yimatzei*, and regarding which many of the early books of the Rishonim, of blessed memory, have not yet been published, etc. See there. See also Iggeres HaKodesh by the Alter Rebbe, section 26 (144b), and the Kuntres Acharon there, s.v. *U'lehavin pirtei hahalachos*.

May you soon be able to celebrate the completion of your work and continue to go from strength to strength in such endeavors, with tranquility and expansion.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 15,828

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

Mr. Yitzchak, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you have succeeded in organizing some of your friends to study Torah together, but that you are not satisfied with their conduct in some matters. You should have consulted on this with the *rav pa’alim* [man of many deeds], the *chossid* R’ Azriel Haikin, may he live, who surely knows some of them and will therefore be able to gauge how it might be easier to influence them. It is possible that the *rav* of your camp could also speak, at the very least, with some of them regarding the aforementioned matter. In any case, one must not despair; one must strive time and again—two and three times, and so on—in the language of the verse, "You shall surely rebuke" (*Vayikra 19:17*), even up to one hundred times. It is a well-known saying of our Rebbes, the *Nesi’im* holy, that there is a *chazakah* [presumption/established power] for *ta’amulah* [outreach/propaganda] that it does not return empty. Certainly, as you increase your own good conduct with greater and greater perfection—for there is always room for addition and improvement in matters of *kedushah*, which are without boundaries—you will succeed more in your influence upon the aforementioned, as our Sages said, "Whoever possesses *yiras shamayim*, his words are heard." May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

Regarding what you wrote concerning an explanation of the concept of *sheviras hakeilim* [the shattering of the vessels]—this is explained in several places in the teachings of Chassidus, among them in *Torah Or* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, page 27c, and in *Toras Chayim* there, and elsewhere.

Likewise, regarding what you wrote concerning an explanation of the concept of Rachel and Leah as brought in Kabbalah, you should also examine this in the *sefer Torah Or* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, page 22d, and elsewhere.

Also, regarding what you ask about the nature of the names derived from *rashei teivos* [acronyms], this is explained according to what our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, beginning of Chapter 12.

It is understood that there is no room for a sufficient explanation of such matters in letters, and you should ask Rabbi Haikin, *shlita*, to study these aforementioned places with you, and he will explain them there.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

## 529

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Nach Yitzchok, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Sunday, in which you write that you have already purchased the house and are living in it.

It is appropriate that you hold a farbrengen in your new home, where words of Torah and words of hisorerus regarding yiras shamayim and ahavah of Hashem will be spoken, for this is the fitting education for the home of a Jewish man.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for good tidings and for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

## 530

B.H., 2 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the Avrech Menachem Ben Zion, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from the 23rd of Adar Sheini was received. Regarding your question as to how to influence a certain Avrech: it is understood that there are no fixed rules, as it depends on the character of the individual one wishes to influence. In any case, as we see tangibly in the vast majority of instances, the path of argumentation is not a method for exerting influence. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Whatever is simple is better." Even if the individual in question wishes to argue, you should explain to him that he can do so at a later time, and not necessarily at the very beginning of receiving the influence. The influence should come through the study of the teachings of Chassidus and the explanation of its concepts through conversation in the spirit of Chassidus. It would be appropriate to consult with others who know the individual and his character, for it has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

It is distressing to hear what you wrote—that sometimes when the esteemed Chassid, a man of many accomplishments, Rabbi A.Z. HaKohen, may he live, comes to his shiur, he finds only one or two listeners. Although it is understood that he must come nonetheless—for whoever sustains even one soul of Israel, it is as if he has sustained an entire world—it is clear that dissemination is achieved when the number of listeners increases, not only in quality but also in quantity. And this is obvious.

Regarding what you wrote about there being obstacles: it is a great wonder that you listen to the enticements of the Yetzer Hara that there are obstacles, at a time when the verdict from Above is known. Due to the mesiras nefesh of our Alter Rebbe for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be on top (printed in *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya*, end of page 122), and anything that stands to be nullified is considered as already nullified.

The recitation of *Lamnatzeiach Yaancha*... *Tefillah LeDavid*... according to the Chabad custom, depends on the recitation of *Tachanun*...

Surely you are preparing to utilize the days of the festival of Pesach for the dissemination of the wellsprings as well, in addition to the campaign of distributing *matzah shemurah* as in previous years, but with an increase.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5331

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Elazar Steinman, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’vracha!

In anticipation of the Festival of Matzos that is approaching us and all of Israel for good, I send to you and all those associated with you my blessing for a kosher and happy holiday. May it be the will [of Hashem] that our season of freedom brings true freedom—freedom, both physical and spiritual, from concealments and hiddenness, and from anything that distracts from the avodah of Hashem with joy, and may we draw from this joy for the entire year.

In connection with this, I am sending you a Haggadah of Pesach with a collection of customs and reasons, which we have just published in a third edition. I am certain you will find interest in it, and it is my hope that it reaches you in good time.

As I speak of this, and whenever I see your books or am reminded of them, I think of your greatest merit: that you have merited to spread the wellsprings outward into circles that, were it not for you, who knows when they would have reached them. It is clear to me that you, or your parents, must possess some special merit that caused this merit of the many to be brought about through you. And if one were to ask, what is the practical difference for me in knowing why he merited more than others? Firstly, it is known that knowledge regarding a person’s avodah can be beneficial to others, and perhaps to me as well. Furthermore, when one sees that a specific matter has led to such a reward, it provides additional strength for that type of avodah. It is human nature that when one knows a matter in its general sense, it does not have as much of an effect as when one knows the details. It is understood that it is not my place to inquire into the private matters of others, but since the merit of this dissemination is a matter of the many, surely there must have been here a merit of the many, measure for measure.

With respect and holiday blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***5331***

## H'Shlav

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, R' Eliezer, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I read your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Nissan, the month of miracles and redemption. In it, you outline the highlights of your holy work in drawing the hearts of our fellow Jews closer to our Father in Heaven. Fortunate is his portion that Divine Providence has placed him in this position. As is well known, the Baal Shem Tov taught that every single Jewish man and woman is dearer to our Father in Heaven than the dearness of an only child born to his parents in their old age. From this, one can also understand the magnitude of the reward—and the essential point that "a mitzvah draws another mitzvah," and "the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself"—in that one is granted the ability and the possibility to increase strength in these matters, in addition to fulfilling the personal needs of himself and his family, may they live.

I was pleased to read at the end of your letter regarding the appreciation for the Chabad movement. It is my firm hope and confidence that you will engage in its teachings and its affairs, one of the fundamentals of which is the dissemination of the wellsprings of this Torah until they reach the "outside." As per the statement of the Mishnah, "Give, and let others give," [one is then called] a **Chassid**, and similarly, "Benefit, and let others benefit." We have each already been promised in the Torah, "If you walk in My statutes," which Rashi explains, based on the Sifra, to mean that you should be toiling in Torah, etc., "then I will provide your rains," and all the matters mentioned in that portion.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

#### ***H'Shlav***

**R' Eliezer:** Spector, London. Another letter to him—see below, H'Ta'az.

**Baal Shem Tov’s teaching:** See also above, Vol. 8, letter B'Resz, and the references in the notes there. See below, H'Tav.

**Statement of the Mishnah:** Avos 5:13.

## 533

[3 Nissan, 5717]

...In response to your letter from Tuesday, in which you write regarding the marriage proposal with Ms....

The proposal is, of course, appropriate, provided that she takes upon herself to conduct their home in a Chassidic manner, wearing a sheitel, etc. May it be the will [of Hashem] that it be in a good and auspicious hour.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you to increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos, especially in connection with this new turning point in your life, and [the rest] is understood.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, as well as in your holy work of spreading the wellsprings outward.

## 534

B.H., 5 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, together with the *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zya*. Regarding the beginning of your letter, where you write that you have no good news to report, etc. — may it be Hashem’s will that, eventually, you too will see the good and begin to report as much, and through this, the revealed and manifest good will increase as well.

Regarding what you write concerning the yeshiva in..., the phrasing of your letter is surprising, as if you are standing on the sidelines, and the responsibility for establishing the yeshiva and its development rests upon a few of *anash*, and [you ask] what you are to do about it.

Now, from a distance, it is difficult to give instructions on many details. However, regarding one **fundamental and internal** point, it is incumbent upon you and all your colleagues, and it must be emphasized from here as well: this concerns the recruitment of students and holding onto them (*anhaltin*) within the walls of the yeshiva. This depends, first and foremost, on the *roshei yeshiva* and the *mashpiim*, and you are among them. It is understood and **obvious** that it is not at all sufficient to merely study a specific portion of Torah with the students at a set time, and that occasionally you may even hold a *farbrengen* with them. For the study of Torah is not like the study of any other wisdom; it must be "arranged in all things and kept," not only from the side of the student, but even more so from the side of the teacher, and in a manner appropriate to the nature and senses of the recipient—that is, the students. **If** the *roshei yeshiva* of the yeshiva in... had been teaching in the aforementioned manner throughout the... years you write about, **certainly** the name of the yeshiva would be famous throughout Eretz Yisrael, *tiv*, and primarily, the youth would be knocking on the doors of the yeshiva, asking to be accepted to hear *shiurim* that captivate the student and make him alive and warm with *chayus* and Chassidic warmth. It is also obvious that this is possible not only when studying a chapter of Tanya or a Chassidic concept, but even when teaching *aleph-beis* or Hebrew. It is painful to put my concern into writing: that the conduct of the *roshei yeshiva*, etc., on this point was **not** in the aforementioned manner. And regarding all the *mitzvos*, the command stands that they should not be "a commandment of men learned by rote," and *kal v'chomer*.

It is understood that the intention of all the above is not to preach, and certainly there is no intent here to refrain from *limud zechus*, but rather to point out the matters that are capable of rectifying the current situation of the yeshiva in...

And since we are approaching the festival of our freedom, freedom in body and soul, may it be His will that you and your family, *shichyu*, be liberated from all matters that distract from serving Hashem with true joy, peace of mind, and proper health.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

...It is obvious that I do not mean general and comprehensive matters that [would be discussed] at a general *farbrengen*, but rather in the manner of a merchant in his material livelihood, who is concerned that his place of business be well-known, that there be a large number of customers, etc.

#### ***534***

Following this — see letter 454.

## 535

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Adar II and the telegram that preceded it, in which you write regarding the matter of... [may she live].

As you describe the situation, you should have approached a Rav, a teacher of instruction in Israel, regarding such matters as soon as possible, and detailed before him the current situation and the sequence of events, so that he may rule according to the law as it conforms to the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life. Surely he will not delay the ruling, for just as peace is a great principle in general, and especially between a man and his wife, so too in certain cases, etc., and the Sages were diligent regarding the welfare of the daughters of Israel.

My letters in response to your previous correspondence surely arrived in due time.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**Regarding the matter of... [may she live]:** That her husband lacks the power of potency.

## 335

5 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Following a long hiatus, your letter written on 8 Adar II, along with its enclosure, has been received. Regarding your statement that the content of my letters is beyond your comprehension and that of everyone who has seen them, and that they have no knowledge of these matters...

Just as the Torah is meticulous in its choice of words—writing "not pure" when describing animals in order to maintain refined language—so too is the Torah meticulous in the laws of ritual impurity by explicitly using the word "impure." Similarly, just as there is the greatest obligation to judge every person favorably—and in the words of our Rebbe, "every person" literally, down to the lowest of the low—so too is there the obligation of "you shall surely rebuke" (*hochiach tochiach*), even toward others, in a situation where it is practically relevant and there is hope that by protesting the matter, something will be rectified. Since I have not yet entirely lost hope that the aforementioned will be rectified, I wrote to some of *anash*, and to you among them, and perhaps...

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter about the visits to various locations, etc., and that you witnessed terrible *avodah* there, etc.—this could certainly have been anticipated in advance. Therefore, you were surely prepared to utilize the visit for some rectification in the matter. As I wrote in my previous letter, even a small rescue is a rescue, especially in the areas of education and the actual fulfillment of *mitzvos*. Despair is forbidden, even if one fears—and believes the fear is well-founded—that the rectification will not hold for long. Especially in light of the wondrous words of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe (Tanya, Chapter 25), that this *yichud* above is eternal forever and ever. This applies even to the fulfillment of a single *mitzvah*, whether *d'oraisa* or *d'rabbanan*, even one time. How much more so, and with a *kal v'chomer*, if the thing is fulfilled several times, over a period of time, and by many people. Surely, for someone like you, elaboration on this is superfluous.

In connection with this, and as a continuation of this—and all these things, and much more, serve as a protest against your writing that you are broken and crushed upon seeing what was achieved—I recall the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Our *ziburis* (inferior grain) is better than their *id'is* (superior grain)." I am confident that one cannot fathom what was achieved in the aspect of "doing good," and even more so in the aspect of "turning away from evil," specifically through his entry into the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva. My hope is strong that here, too, elaboration for someone like you is superfluous.

Since we are approaching the time of our freedom, where—as with all matters—these days are "remembered and performed," as is well known from the Arizal’s interpretation of this, and since the freedom actually began in Tishrei, when the labor of our forefathers ceased, and there is an even closer beginning from Rosh Chodesh Nissan, "This month shall be for you" specifically, as our Sages have taught—may it be the will of Hashem that in all the aforementioned matters, there will be true freedom from all things that distract one from fulfilling the role of every member of the Jewish people: "I was created to serve my Maker." As is explained in the teachings of Chassidus, this means to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds. In a dwelling place, a person is found in his essence, and it is known that the essence is drawn down only through the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. May this be drawn down, as mentioned, below the ten *tefachim*, until it permeates daily life, and the results will be seen immediately in the strengthening and expansion of all Chabad activities in every place, and in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, obviously and simply. And may we soon merit, through the spreading of the wellsprings, that the Master, King Moshiach, will come.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and awaiting good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 537

[5 Nissan, 5717]

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos along with the enclosure, as well as your previous letters. It is surely superfluous to elaborate on the great *nachas ruach* derived from the activities about which you write. And surely our *Nesi’im*, our holy Rebbes—who sacrificed themselves for the matter of *ahavas kol echad mei-Yisrael* and spoke at length regarding the magnitude of this matter—will add to the *hisorerus* from Above in their place of holy service now, to increase abundant success in the aforementioned activities, and exceptional success, as well as blessing and success in the private matters of all those who are engaged in this. And surely, through this, they will increase these activities, for *mitzvah goreres mitzvah*.

And just as you have merited to inspire the idea of the visits, and have merited to see the actual results and good fruit from these activities, so too may you merit in the future to bring good tidings in this regard, that the activities continue to grow in both quantity and quality, until the prophecy is fulfilled: "And no longer shall they teach each man his neighbor... for they shall all know Me, from the smallest to the greatest."

#### ***537***

Published in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 535.

**The idea of the visits:** In the "Preface" to *Bit'on Chabad*, Issue 15: For about a year now, Tzeirei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) has been visiting, in pairs, various *moshavim* and *kibbutzim* of all factions and circles, bringing before their residents the word of Chassidus, its Torah, its guidance, and its customs, and they have succeeded in stirring strong waves of *teshuvah* to the source of Yiddishkeit. We are hereby transcribing the letter of the *Nasi* of our generation, the Rebbe shlita—dated 5 Nissan 5717—to one of *Anash* (may he live) who stands at the head of the organization of these activities.

See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 5133. Below, 5343, 5353.

## Letter 5,338

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Adar II and those preceding it.

Regarding what you write about the effects of drinking the four cups: one should consult a physician, who will surely instruct you on how to prepare the wine in a way that will not affect your health, and consequently, the effects you describe will be nullified.

Regarding what you write about the thoughts of your grandmother, she should live and be well, who envisions confused matters in her mind: the mezuzos in her room should be checked. Furthermore, she should set aside a few coins for tzedakah every morning. It is also appropriate for her situation that, before she goes to sleep, someone should read to her or tell her stories of our holy Nasi and stories of Chassidim in general. Surely, she recites Krias Shema Al HaMitah, at least the first paragraph and the blessing of Hamapil.

There is surely an organized plan for utilizing the upcoming days of the Pesach holiday for matters of Yiddishkeit in general, and for spreading the wellsprings outward in particular, and you are among those active in this, and you also encourage your friends to be active in this as well.

With the blessing that Hashem, may He be blessed, protect your parents, may they live and be well, wherever they may be, and may they emerge with kindness and mercy from distress to relief, and with a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach and for good tidings.

#### ***Letter 5,338***

**To check the mezuzos:** In continuation of this — see below, Letter 5,707.

## 539

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I confirm receipt of your letter from the 27th of Adar II, and surely in the meantime you have received my response to your previous letter. I find the conclusion of your letter—in which you ask to be relieved of your administrative duties, G-d forbid, etc.—to be a source of great wonder and astonishment, even as a mere passing thought. For while it is understandable if one occasionally thinks such things to oneself—which falls under the category of "one who injures himself," for which one is at least exempt from human judgment—it is quite another matter when I, as you suggest, would be the one to act upon it; that would fall under the category of "one who injures others."

Indeed, the Sages have stated that the poor person does more for the householder than the householder does for the poor person. This applies to every dynamic of *mashpia* and *mekabel*, including the affairs of the *yeshiva* which you manage and organize—namely, that they are in the position of *mekabel* and you are the *mashpia*. And even though this is through the power of our holy Rebbes, it does not diminish your exertion, and at times, your distress. "You have labored and you have found," and "according to the effort is the reward." If there is any basis for the complaints you write of (that you are not being considered, etc.), it is understood and obvious that this detail must be rectified, but not, G-d forbid, by touching the affairs of the *yeshiva*, nor by touching your own involvement.

Furthermore, it should be known that there is no perfection in the world. In the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his well-known *sicha*, there is no good without evil. From this, it is also understood that if one were to cancel every endeavor because some small amount of evil is found within it, it would result in the destruction and ruin of all things in the world.

The conclusion to be drawn from this is that Hashem should grant you success not only to continue in your holy work, but to increase it. May the negative matters steadily diminish. And if a little light pushes away much darkness, then how much more so does a great deal of light.

Especially as we are in the days that connect one redemption to another, and the precision of the phrase "as in the days of your exodus" (in the plural) is well known—that the Exodus from Egypt began on the 15th of Nissan in the year 2448 and continues every day until the coming of *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*. It is understood that every day adds to the one before it, for the Exodus from Egypt refers to an exodus from all *metzarim*—that is, the matters that limit and constrain—and it is a preparation for the giving and receiving of the Torah. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, you will divert your mind from all matters that distract from success in your holy work, for the consolidation and development of the camp of the good, and may you bring good tidings not only in general matters, but also in personal matters, for yourself and for each and every member of your household, may they live.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**M. Schneerson**

## 540

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

...It is somewhat surprising that, apparently, until now there were institutions in... that were run according to the personal opinions of an individual. It is understood that this has no place—not only according to Torah in general, but even according to simple logic. And who is greater than Moshe Rabbeinu? The words of our Sages are well known (Midrash Rabbah and Tanchuma, beginning of Parshas Pekudei; Rema and Bach in Yoreh Deah, siman 257; see there). Since I read in your letter that the matter has been rectified regarding the..., I have strong hope that the other matters will also be rectified as soon as possible. Certainly, this will result in an increase in the drawing together of hearts, an increase in blessing, etc.

#### ***540***

From a copy.

## 510

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Dovid Abba, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Many thanks for the good news regarding the arrival of his wife’s parents to the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. May it be the will of Hashem that they settle in the best possible manner, in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed.

And may the merit of your involvement in establishing the affairs of Kfar Chabad—and I have a strong hope that you will not be satisfied with the manner of your work as secretary of the village until now, but will add to it in the necessary fashion—stand for you and your entire family in your private matters as well. For this village, by its very function, is a vessel to receive the blessings of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, may their merit protect us, and it is also the conduit for their blessings for all of Anash throughout the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and through them, for the entirety of the Jewish people who are there. For regarding all of Israel it is said, "You are all standing today," as one complete entity, as explained in Likutei Torah at the beginning of Parshas Nitzavim.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for good news in both general and private matters.

#### 510

**Moreinu HaRav Dovid Abba, may he live:** Chen, Kfar Chabad.

## 5342

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Shlomo, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Nissan and the one preceding it, in which you write regarding the activities of organizing public lectures of *hisorerus*,

I am interested to know the points of the content of these lectures, for there are many types of *hisorerus* and many manners and ways to achieve it. It is understood that in these days, especially through *kiruv* and words of pleasantness, one accomplishes more than through the opposite—all the more so and *kal v’chomer* from the days of the Baal Shem Tov and his students, where even then there was a great difference, and that difference has grown over the passage of time.

Regarding what you wrote about printing a pamphlet concerning *emunah* and *hisorerus* regarding the observance of Torah and *mitzvos*—surely you will not include in this pamphlet matters of *vikuach* (debate) and the like. For every debate necessitates presenting the opinion of the opposing side, and the refutations of it are not always absorbed. The main point is that in our generation, there are many who do not know the whole matter—meaning, they do not even know the words of the opponent—and therefore, one must be careful about publishing views of *kefirah*.

Regarding what you wrote about the *Reshimas HaMaasar* (the Prison Diary), it is appropriate that you speak with the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in your vicinity and with the members of the editorial board of the publication.

It is my hope—even though you do not write explicitly—that you are making progress in holiness regarding the *kevius itim* (fixed times) for your study of *Chassidus*. For despite the magnitude of all the aforementioned matters, as I have written at length elsewhere, after the prophet marvels at the greatness of the activities, "Share your bread with the hungry," etc.—and in this, as per the interpretation of *Tanna D’Vei Eliyahu Rabbah*, this refers to those hungry and naked in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—nevertheless, "do not hide yourself from your own flesh." May it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach.

Regarding your question about the contradiction between *avodah* on oneself and *avodah* with others—*tzarich iyun*—I believe I have already written to you regarding this, that both are **essential**, from which it is understood that in essence, they do not contradict one another. The division of time between them varies according to the person and the place, and for the same person, from time to time. Regarding this, one should consult with those who are on-site and whose hearts are close to the distress of every individual of *Bnei Yisrael*. As is known, the ruling is that one does not seat in the Sanhedrin one who is extremely elderly, etc.

## 155

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

To each and every one in Kfar Chabad—founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—may Hashem watch over them and grant them life,

Peace and blessings!

Approaching the festival of Pesach, the season of our freedom, which is arriving for us and for all of Yisroel for the good, I hereby express to each and every one of you my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday, and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual anxieties, from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

May it be His will that you carry this freedom and joy throughout the entire year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, which is commanded to us in our Torah—the Torah of life—encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night.

As it is said, "In all your ways know Him," which is explained by the Rambam (Hilchos Deos, end of chapter 3) and cited as halacha in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, section 231.

And even more so in the Zohar: "In all a person’s deeds, he should intend that they all be for the sake of the Holy Name... to mention the Holy Name with his mouth regarding everything he does, for everything is for His service" (Vol. III, 51b; and see there 50a).

The purpose of this is explicitly stated in the verse: "Know Him." As it is written, "Know this day... know the G-d of your father," and as explained by the Rambam (Shemonah Perakim, chapter 5): "He should always place one goal before his eyes, which is the attainment of Hashem... and he should direct his actions... and all his words toward this goal."

It is my prayer that Hashem will help and grant success so that the actions of Kfar Chabad and all its affairs will be directed toward and lead to this goal—the matter of the *maayanos hachassidus*—in accordance with the will of its founder, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, from whom the springs shall spread outward.

Until the fulfillment of the promise, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," in the true and complete Geulah, speedily in our days, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach, with material and spiritual expansion, true freedom, and a healthy and happy summer.

I have entrusted the matzos-shmura to the esteemed and G-d-fearing Rabbi A. Dreizin, may he live, and I have requested that he distribute them equally among the residents of Kfar Chabad, through the Village Committee and the Spiritual Committee, under the leadership of the Rav, the Mara D'Asra, shlita.

May it be His will that they effect the result mentioned by our Sages, as "food of faith" and "food of healing," as explained by our Alter Rebbe regarding this (copied in *Hayom Yom*, 15 Nissan, 5703).

#### ***155***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 244, and in its entirety in *Bitaon Chabad*, Issue 14, p. 2.

## 5048

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the holy congregation "Shuva Yisrael" in Buenos Aires, led by the distinguished Rav, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and esteemed...
Rabbi Zev, shlita,
May Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

As we approach the festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, which is arriving for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

Avodah of Hashem encompasses the entire day and night and all of a person’s affairs, as it is written, "In all your ways know Him," which the Rambam explains at length (Hilchos Deios, end of chapter 3), and which is brought as halacha in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 231. See there.

May it be the will that they continue this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the year.

In accordance with the well-known language of the Zohar, that matzah is the "food of faith" and the "food of healing," I have requested that they send matzah shemurah from here in good time, in such a way that there will be at least two kezayis for each and every one of your holy congregation.

May it be the will that this fulfills the saying of our Rabbeinu HaZaken—the author of the Shulchan Aruch, who decides the revealed Torah, and the Tanya, who decides the hidden Torah—which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: The Alter Rebbe said: "Food of faith"—the first night; "food of healing"—the second night. If the healing brings the faith, then he says, "Thank You, G-d, for my healing," implying he was sick; but if the faith brings the healing, then one is, from the outset, not sick at all.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

## 5337

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your prompt letter was received. I feared that the haste was because it concerned a material matter, and to my regret, this was confirmed. It is your custom either not to write at all, or at the very least to do so very rarely, yet when matters related to the body in the literal sense arise, you immediately send an urgent letter with a request, expecting the response to be in the same vein. However, based on the interpretation of the Metzudas David on the verse "You open Your hand and satisfy the desire of every living thing," and especially in light of the well-known principle that "the material needs of another are my spiritual concern," I am fulfilling this desire of yours as well...

May it be Hashem's will that even as we approach the Yom Tov of haste—when our forefathers left Mitzrayim in a rush—we will also feel the virtue of "in stillness and trust shall be your strength," which is the preparation now, in the footsteps of Moshiach, for the future redemption, may it come speedily in our days. See the *Hemshech* "VeKacha"—the great one—at its beginning and its end.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 548

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday,

At an auspicious time, I will mention your father, *sheyichyeh*, at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zya*, for success in his affairs. Your father will surely serve as a conduit connecting to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who awakens Divine compassion in this regard, through the study of his Torah—namely, his *maamarim* of *Chassidus*—and by keeping the three *shiurim* accessible to every soul, as established by him: *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and the well-known *Tanya*.

Regarding what you wrote about your manner of study, and that at times you do not feel the momentum of *hasmadah* and *shekidah*—this has already been addressed in the *Tanya*. It is one of the tactics of the *yetzer hara* to incite a person by suggesting that he is not what he ought to be. Yet, at the very moment the *yetzer* incites him, the *nefesh elokis* that is within every single person remains faithful to him, and every Jew desires to fulfill the will of the Giver of the Torah and the *mitzvos*. As this is explained at length in *Tanya*, and briefly codified as *halacha* in the *Rambam* (Hilchos Geirushin, end of Chapter 2), it is understood that the matter depends solely on one’s will. The ability has been granted to you in full to study with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* that grow from time to time—especially as we approach the days of *Pesach*, the season of our freedom, and there is no "free man" from the *yetzer* except through the engagement in Torah.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for a kosher and happy *Pesach*.

## 5717

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter:

I am surprised by its content. You yourself write that I had asked you to write to me and let me know when things improved; yet you did not do so, and waited until after the improvement, when something became obstructed, and only then did you inform me.

It is well known, as explained in the holy seforim, that when one receives chassadim from Hashem Yisbarach, one must acknowledge them to the fullest extent and thank Him in an appropriate manner. This gratitude is expressed by adding to one’s involvement in Torah and mitzvos. When one acknowledges the good that Hashem Yisbarach provides, this sustains the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, and Hashem Yisbarach adds even more. However, if when the good arrives, one takes it for granted—and sometimes even as one’s own achievement, brought about by one’s own wisdom or the like—not only does this not lead to an increase in Torah and mitzvos, but at times it leads to the exact opposite. For when one feels secure in oneself, it is no wonder if things subsequently become obstructed.

It is understandable that my request for you to let me know about the improvement was intended to draw your attention to observing how Hashem Yisbarach conducts Himself with you in kindness and mercy, and through this, the good should be further strengthened.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you that, at the very least from now on, you should act as stated above, especially as we prepare for the Yom Tov of Pesach, the season of our freedom.

You do not mention in your letter the matter of a shidduch for your son, sheyichyeh. I assume that, as we discussed, this is being handled in an appropriate manner, and may Hashem Yisbarach help with success.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Yom Tov of Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe,

Secretary

## 550

B.H., 8 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

Your note, along with the enclosure, has reached me. At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need, as is appropriate to write.

One should endeavor—especially if it does not involve particular difficulties—to write the articles in such a way that they would be suitable for publication in print, should it be decided that there is a public benefit in doing so.

You are surely familiar with the saying we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the study of Torah: "You tell me that you are studying Torah, but what has the Torah taught you?" Yet, in your aforementioned note, you add details about what you are studying with others, but not about your own Torah study as it pertains to yourself.

May it be the will of Hashem that this omission exists only in your writing and reporting, but not in actual practice. Even then, an increase from time to time is necessary, in accordance with the commandment to "ascend in matters of holiness."

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and for a truly kosher and joyous Pesach.

## 5252

**Which I have reviewed:** See also above, Vol. 12, letter 3807.

 On the second day of Chanukah, the Kohen is called up for the second day [reading], "until 'full of incense'." The Levi, until "the son of Tzur." The Yisrael, "on the third day," etc. (and the same applies to all the days of Chanukah).

## 1553

1553

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, illustrious, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Mordechai, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you write the main points of your life story and continue regarding your connection to Chassidus and Chassidim.

It is already known what our Rebbes, the holy Nesi'im, have stated: "True hiskashrus is through the study of Torah. When one studies my maamarim of Chassidus, reads the sichos, connects with the friends of anash and the talmidei hatmimim—may they live—in their studies and farbrengens, and fulfills my request by reciting Tehillim and keeping to the study schedules—this is hiskashrus" (copied in Hayom Yom, 24 Sivan, 5743). Likewise, when each of us studies those same maamarim of Chassidus, strives to keep the takanos of our Rebbes, the holy Nesi'im, and—most importantly—engages in *hafotzas hamaayanos*, the wellsprings of the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, we are naturally connected together to the "Tree of Life" through our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, all the way up to the holy source: Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Maggid of Mezritch, the Baal Shem Tov, etc., of whom it is said, "I stand between Hashem and you," as the intermediary who connects us to the *Atzmus u'Mahus* of the Ein Sof, B"H.

In connection with this, it gave me pleasure to see in your letter that in addition to your sons—may they live—having been within the four cubits of the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim, you yourself have fixed times for the study of Chabad Chassidus, you review its maamarim in public, and you strive to spread the wellsprings outward by visiting settlements of Bnei Yisrael that are, for the time being, outside of the aforementioned. I am certain that through all this, your hiskashrus will be strengthened even further. The main thing is that it should have an effect on your daily life and in all matters, as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him." How wondrous are the words of the Rambam (Chapter 5 of the Rambam's Shemonah Perakim) that the goal of **all** human affairs is the attainment of knowledge of Hashem; see there.

We are now approaching the time of our freedom—freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem with joy and a glad heart, out of an abundance of everything.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you and your entire family—may they live—at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Your efforts in the aforementioned matters will surely stand for each of you to draw down blessings from the Giver of the Torah, the Life of all life, in whatever you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned, and for the continuation of your activities in *hafotzas hamaayanos* and an increase in this, in accordance with the directive to "increase in holiness," and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 554

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date of writing—in which you write that you are studying at the Yeshiva...

You write of certain ideas regarding your plans for the near future, and you ask for my opinion on which path you should choose.

Now, the study of Torah in our times in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established) within the framework of a Yeshiva, in addition to the general matter of Torah study, has a primary function and the greatest benefit: it establishes the student on a firm foundation so that he can stand before the trials of our current era. He will not be swayed by the strange winds blowing from all sides, which, unfortunately, are not only not diminishing but, on the contrary, are as our Sages of blessed memory said, "There is no day [whose curse is not greater than the day before it]..." From this, it is understood that it is not only one who chooses a career in the holy service—such as a Rav, Rosh Yeshiva, or Shochet—who must study for a few years in a Yeshiva. Rather, **every single one** of the youth who truly desires to live a life of Torah study and fulfilling mitzvos according to the will of the Creator of the world needs to live for several years within the aforementioned framework. On the contrary, since he is not choosing a career in the holy service, there is room to say that his trials will be even more difficult, and he is even more in need, during these years that shape his spiritual character, to remain within a Yeshiva framework without distracting himself with other studies and without being in a different atmosphere. And all of this is not a question of acquiring more knowledge in Torah and becoming more of a *lamdan*, but it also concerns the fulfillment of mitzvos in their literal sense.

Furthermore, it should be known that the statement of the Mishnah, "Do not believe in yourself," is simple and its power holds true even in our days. Especially regarding the youth who has not yet stepped outside the four cubits of his parents' home or outside the four cubits of Torah and tefillah, it is impossible for him to estimate in advance the intensity of the trial he will face after a few years, or to decide whether he is already as fortified as necessary to overcome all the concealments and hiddenness.

There are those who object to the above, arguing that the years in Yeshiva delay the start of establishing oneself in a livelihood. But ultimately, Hashem is the One who sustains and provides for all, and "man does not live by bread alone." One must, at the appropriate time, establish his spiritual standing and his peace of mind, ensuring they are founded as necessary. When the foundation is strong and firm, one can benefit from the building that rests upon this foundation, improving and perfecting it—which is not the case when the foundation is shaky, etc.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you decide what is truly good for you—that is to say, to dedicate a few years to holy studies and in a holy atmosphere and environment—and then you will succeed in the future, and in material matters as well.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5717

10 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, a man of many accomplishments and fine character,
R’ Alexander Zissel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of intervals, your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos was received. I was pleased to read in it the account of the daily schedule at the institution under your administration. Surely you are doing everything necessary regarding the fact that both boys and girls are being educated in the institution, especially since you mention that they stand separately during davening. It is understood that this is not yet sufficient.

Regarding the point in your letter where you write that you sometimes engage in self-reflection regarding your involvement in the education of others, while wondering what will become of your own situation and your own eyes, as day follows day, etc.

Surely you are aware that this dilemma and these inner struggles are ancient. They confuse all those who engage in communal needs in general, and in the field of communal activism—which occupies and encompasses the entire person—in particular. It is also understood that the solution to this dilemma and the answer to this fundamental question are not the same in all eras, nor for all individuals. A time of war is not like a time of peace; a time of emergency is not like years of normalcy. And it goes without saying that one who possesses a special talent for activism is not like one whose involvement in it is by way of *iskafya* (self-coercion). These matters are understood and are simple to one who contemplates, even for a short while, the worldview of our Torah—the Torah of life—which contains the great principle: "Love your fellow as yourself," and "Whoever sustains one soul of Yisrael is as if he sustained an entire world."

It is understood that in our generation—a generation of orphans, and on the other hand, the generation of *Ikvesa D’Meshicha*, the end of the *galus* and the immediate preparation for the beginning of the true *Geulah*—about which it is said that it will be a complete *Geulah* (meaning that not a single person of Yisrael will remain in *galus*, neither in *galus* of the body nor in *galus* of the spirit), the participation and effort of every individual is mandatory in gathering the souls of the children of Yisrael and bringing them closer to the Redeemer of Yisrael, the Holy One, blessed be He, the Giver of the Torah and the *mitzvos*. No one is exempt from this holy *avodah*. At the very least, a specific amount of time every day, week, and month must be dedicated to it. As the person’s talent for this *avodah* grows, so too must the amount of time he dedicates to it increase. From this, it is also understood that there are those whose primary *avodah* is specifically this, and all their other affairs are *hechsher mitzvah* (preparations for a mitzvah) for this *avodah* as well. In other words, this is the *mitzvah* regarding which "he was more careful" (see *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe HaZaken, end of Chapter 7, and in *Sefer HaSichos* Summer 5700, page 22, and the footnote there). All his other Torah and *mitzvos* ascend through this *mitzvah*, from below to above, and all his *hemshechos* and *hashpaos* (drawings down and influences) are drawn through this *mitzvah* from above to below.

However, it is also understood that in order to gather the sparks and to draw hearts closer, merely being "moist" is not enough; one must be "moist in order to moisten" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*). This is a matter left to the person to measure and allocate: each day and each period, how much time and energy he must dedicate to working on himself—*mit zich un in zich* (with himself and within himself)—even though the majority, if not all, of his efforts are dedicated to working with others. In order not to err in this measurement, one must remember well the well-known adage that we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: Just as it is forbidden to diminish one's own shortcomings, so too is it forbidden to diminish one's own virtues. On another occasion, he said that the prohibition against *lashon hara* applies not only to others, but it is also forbidden to speak *lashon hara* about oneself. Since the Holy One, blessed be He, demands the aforementioned *avodah*, it is certainly possible to fulfill it. One should not be discouraged if, at the beginning of these matters, one encounters difficulties—and furthermore, even if one occasionally stumbles. As our Sages of blessed memory have said, "A person does not stand on the words of Torah unless he has stumbled in them." There is no greater instruction than this, for it is in the laws of *pikuach nefesh*.

And to use the style of our Rebbe HaZaken (*Tanya*, Chapter 44):

Even though who is the one whose heart would dare to approach and grasp even one-thousandth of the level of a "shepherd of Yisrael," nevertheless, a small portion and a trace of this exists in every person of Yisrael, and especially in activists who work in the field of education—at the very least in potential and in power. Therefore, this is the place to contemplate the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on Shabbos Bereishis 5737, on the verse "Arise, shine" (*Kumi Ori*). This is the language of the notes of one of the listeners: "The *maamar* of the Baal Shem Tov was to the *Nesi'ei Yisrael* (leaders of Yisrael). He said to them: 'You, *Nesi'ei Yisrael*, who teach Yidden Torah and act for the benefit of the many—what will be with you yourselves?' To this, the answer is: 'Arise, shine'—with the light that is both particular and general—'for your light has come'..." [The note is incomplete].

Even though, due to the note being unfinished, the conclusion of the matter is not clear, the dilemma is clear, and it is also clear that the aforementioned individuals set aside their own Torah and *avodah* for the benefit of the many, and not only is this conduct of theirs approved, but they are also blessed with the light that is both particular and general.

To grasp the depth of the matter, one could elaborate at length and still not exhaust it. But since we are concerned with practical application, the criterion regarding practical conduct is well known. In the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), may his soul be bound in the bond of life: "Take this rule in your hand and remember it always: that any thing that is beneficial or leads to *avodah* in practice, any obstacle that may arise to this—even if the obstacle is from something most lofty—is only from the stratagems of the *nefesh habehamis* (animal soul)" (recorded in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan 5703).

If you will listen to me, you will increase your strength in your *avodah* of educating the sons and daughters of Yisrael, both through your influence on them in the institution and outside of it. You should view the matter as it is in its truth and in its inwardness: that you are dealing with those about whom it is said for each one, "You are children to Hashem your G-d." Every thing that brings them closer to our Father in Heaven, and every action in this regard, is eternal forever and ever and causes boundless *nachas ruach*. However, in order for the *avodah* to be successful, you and your home must be a living example for those you influence, in those very matters in which you influence them. That is to say, a living example of a Yiddishe man and woman according to the words of our holy Torah, and together with this, permeated with the "light of the Torah"—this is the Torah of Chassidus. This necessitates consistency in one's soul, as well as consistency in time, the study of Chassidus, and the observance of its guidance and conduct. Then, surely, the promise will also be fulfilled that "his mind and heart will become a thousand times purer"—and "a thousand times" here is not an exaggeration, as explained in many places. That is to say, through the study of one *sha'ar* (chapter/gate), one succeeds and absorbs in quantity and quality what another would need a thousand hours for. Then you will also proceed in your private life from level to level, from strength to strength.

It is understood that this is not an easy *avodah*, but where did the initial thought come from that a Yiddishe person should look for an easy *avodah*? Especially in our days, when the *Shechinah* is in *galus*, the darkness is double and redoubled, and all matters are laborious, etc. More than what is written here is found between the lines, and I hope that for one who contemplates, this too is sufficient. May it be the will of Hashem that we both aim for the same goal: to spread the wellsprings of Chassidus outward, conquering until we conquer all of our people, the House of Yisrael, until "no longer will one teach his neighbor... and the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem."

It is understood that in all of the above, there is no contradiction to what I wrote, I believe a few times, regarding your assistance to Kfar Chabad and its affairs. On the contrary, you are also assisting in this, and as the Mishnah promises, "a *mitzvah* leads to another *mitzvah*."

As we approach the *Chag HaMatzos*, the time of our freedom, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and happy holiday, and for true freedom—freedom from worries in material matters and worries in spiritual matters, from everything that hinders the *avodah* of Hashem with joy and a good heart. And may you continue this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the year, especially since the *avodah* of Hashem, as commanded to us in our Torah—the Torah of life—is in all of a person's affairs and throughout the entire day and night, as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him."

With the blessing of the holiday and for good news.

## 550

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Moshe, son of Nachum, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending me a report regarding the visit of the shluchim to Ayanot. I was happy to hear that the mutual impression was positive and good, to the extent that they requested to confirm the scheduling of Shabbos Parshas Shekalim as Chabad Shabbos in Ayanot.

However, according to the Chabad approach, one does not postpone a good thing for an entire year, especially in this era of *haras olam* (the world in labor), when twelve months in our time are worth many times more than in normal years. If this is true in general, it is all the more so when it concerns the welfare of youth at an age when their character is being formed; for what one does a year before that character is set is not comparable to the impact of many years thereafter.

In any case, it is my hope that this was a good beginning for drawing hearts closer on the foundation of our Torah, in which a great principle is "Love your fellow as yourself." This is emphasized at the beginning of the *Seder Pesach* as it is practiced, with the gathering of four sons—possessing viewpoints from one extreme to the other—around the father's table, who teaches them all, each according to what the Torah has spoken.

With respect and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 557

11 Nissan, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, and the activists of Chinuch in particular, in every place and location,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

Pesach begins with *Ki yishalcha bincha*—"When your son asks you," and *V’higadta l’vincha*—"You shall tell your son." There are various manners of asking and answering, corresponding to the four types of "sons": the *Chacham* (wise), the *Rasha* (wicked), the *Tam* (simple), and the *She’eino Yodei’a Lish’ol* (the one who does not know how to ask).

Along with the diversity of these four sons and their opposition to one another, they all share a common denominator: even the *Rasha* is present at the *avodah*-seder; he encounters it, lives together with, and takes an interest in those who are engaged in *avodah* and in a life of Torah and Mitzvos.

This provides hope—a very strong hope—that not only the *Tam* and the *She’eino Yodei’a Lish’ol*, but even the *Rasha*, will become *chachamim*, fully conscious Jews who are *shomrei Torah u’Mitzvos*.

Sadly, however, especially in our time of double and redoubled darkness, there exists another category of children: the child who is not present at the Seder at all. He asks no questions because he has nothing to do with Torah and Mitzvos, or with authentic Jewish laws and customs. He does not know that there is such a thing as "this *avodah*"—a Seder of Pesach, a *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, and *Kabbalas HaTorah*.

One must work with these children long before Pesach and the Seder night, and one must dedicate oneself to them with *mesiras nefesh* and *ahavas Yisrael*.

For one must not forget a single Jewish child, and all one’s strength must be applied to pull them out of their situation and bring them back to the Jewish Seder table.

***

As with all painful phenomena, where in order to rectify the situation one must first know the causes that led to it, so too is it in this case.

Regrettably, one must acknowledge that almost always, the blame for the situation of this category of children lies primarily with the parents.

Arriving in a new land, finding themselves in an environment where they are a small minority, and encountering difficulties—which are generally unavoidable in any migration from place to place—some parents convinced themselves that the only way to avoid these difficulties was to assimilate as quickly as possible in everything with the surrounding environment, by casting off the yoke of Torah and the observance of Mitzvos. Even if they themselves could not easily or fully achieve this, they decided that their children should not have to go through the struggle.

They convinced themselves, and influenced their children as well, that Yiddishkeit, Torah, and Mitzvos were not suited for contemporary life, especially in a new place. In the authentic Jewish way of life, they sought—and consequently, eventually "saw"—only flaws, while in the surrounding environment, they saw only virtues.

Through this approach, the aforementioned parents sought to secure the existence of their children in the new environment. In doing so, they forgot:

That a person cannot exist—as a person ought to exist—if he gives up his soul-life, his entire spirituality, for the sake of the body and physicality.

They also failed to take into account that any mere imitation is false and invites contempt, even from those whom one wishes to emulate and flatter;

And that if the environment and the majority are not founded on justice and righteousness, they will, in any case, oppress the weaker ones and the minority.

***

The same false approach—to solve the position of a minority in an unfriendly environment by dissolving oneself, which in essence means suicide, or at the very least self-mutilation—was adopted not only by individuals, but sadly, also by certain groups of Jews united by common circumstances. From this grew various movements that, openly or covertly, waged war against the Torah that Moshe commanded to us, which he received from the One Hashem for Jews who are one in the land—movements that, despite their wars among themselves, are all built on the same thought: "Let us be like the nations, like the families of the lands, to serve wood and stone" (Yechezkel 20:32).

***

The results of this thoroughly false approach have been that thousands upon thousands of souls have been torn away from their true life-source of Yiddishkeit and from the Jewish people, and have been spiritually murdered. Children have grown up—who are now fathers and grandfathers—who are not only not in the category of *Chacham*, *Tam*, or *She’eino Yodei’a Lish’ol*, but not even in the category of *Rasha*.

They have lost themselves, and are being lost, *chas v’shalom*, to the Jewish people and to authentic Yiddishkeit, which are one.

***

*Yetzias Mitzrayim* and the festival of Pesach come and teach us, among many other instructions for daily life, that the hope for *Geulah* and freedom does not lie in the attempt to imitate the environment, but quite the opposite.

The Jews in Mitzrayim were a small minority and lived in the worst conditions. Yet, as our Sages of blessed memory tell us, they separated themselves from the environment and proudly guarded their own way of life, traditions, and uniqueness (that the Jews were distinguished there by their dress, their food, and their language), and precisely through this, they secured their existence and also attained the true *Geulah*, physically and spiritually.

***

It is one of the life-essential tasks of our time to apply the greatest efforts to instill in the young generation—and even in those who are old in years but young and small in knowledge—the correct appreciation of authentic Yiddishkeit, Torah-true Yiddishkeit, not falsified or watered-down Yiddishkeit, and the recognition that the very existence of a Jew depends upon it—of **every** Jew—the existence also in this world, in every place and at every time.

Until they return to the tradition of our fathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and proudly establish and guard the Jewish way of life, living according to the instructions of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*.

A Jew must never despair; one must never give up on a Jew. And with the correct approach of *ahavas Yisrael*, one will also include the aforementioned category of children among the "four sons," and in time, bring them into the category of *Ben Chacham*.

***

May the Almighty help that all sons and daughters be gathered together at one table of "this *avodah*" and celebrate the Seder Pesach according to the law, to carry out the testimonies, the statutes, and the judgments that Hashem our G-d has commanded us.

And may the beginning of the *kibbutz galuyos*—gathering together at a Torah table even the wayward children—hasten, speedily in our days, the *aschalta d’Geulah* and bring the *Geulah HaAmitis V’HaShleima* through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With the blessing of a Kosher and Happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**
