## 5447

5447

B”H, 14 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, a branch of noble ancestors, a man of character, etc.,
R’ Chaim Shimon Zev, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After your silence, it was pleasant for me to receive your letter of the 5th of Iyar, and thank you for the good news regarding your health. Surely you are fulfilling the directive of our holy Torah, which informs us that it grants the physician permission to heal. In this context, "permission" also means "power," and the physician is merely a conduit through whom one receives the strength and added vitality for the body to be healthy and whole. This is one of the ways of Hashem, as explained in the Rambam, Hilchos De’os, beginning of chapter 4, and in many other places, as well as in the teachings of Chassidus in several maamarim.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the statement in the Zohar* that "the face of the Master, Hashem" refers to Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai: it is known that there are several worlds that have addressed this. I have already stated long ago that this matter is also found in the Nigleh (the revealed) Torah, in accordance with our Sages’ teaching, "Everything that exists on land exists in the sea,"** which is in the Yerushalmi, Bikkurim 3:3, and the matter is explained in Chassidus as well.

Since we are currently in the days between Pesach, the time of our freedom, and the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah—"engraved (charus) on the tablets; do not read it as 'engraved' (charus) but as 'freedom' (cheirus)"—may it be the will of Hashem that there be added to you, and to all those mentioned in your letter, freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem. This includes matters of physical health, as is also explained in the words of our Sages, that all of Yisroel were healthy and whole for the receiving of the Torah, even in their bodies and in their physicality. This is understood even more deeply according to what is explained in Tanya, chapter 49, regarding "And You have chosen us from among all nations and tongues," that the choice is revealed specifically in the material body, etc.; see there.

With blessings for good news and proper health.

## 5748

B"H, 14 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, Rabbi Dovid Tzvi, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 7 Iyar, in which you write that you are a maggid shiur at the Yeshiva in Be’er Sheva.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the demand of the hour: regardless of the context in which one engages with the sons and daughters of Yisrael, the central point must always be to instill in them a spirit of yiras shamayim and to make them recognize the absolute necessity of fulfilling mitzvos maasiyos. While the methods and forms of explanation naturally differ between lower and higher grades, the goal is one. With contemplation, one can find a way in any subject of study to integrate an expression of hisorerus in yiras shamayim and a conclusion regarding mitzvos maasiyos, as is evident in practice. Now, more than ever, the verse in our Torah is emphasized: "Fear G-d and keep His mitzvos, for this is the whole of man."

From the above, it is also understood that regarding what you conclude in your letter—that you are distressed over the bitul Torah caused by your transition to giving shiurim—this is not bitul Torah, but on the contrary, it is the fulfillment of Torah. Especially in a place like Be’er Sheva, where the halachic ruling is established and clear: a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others takes precedence over bitul Torah, as Rashi states: "Cease your Torah study and engage in the mitzvah" (Moed Katan 9b).

I have requested that the secretariat send you the publications from Kehot as per your request, and I am sure you will confirm receipt.

With a blessing for success in bringing the hearts of the children of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven, to make them G-d-fearing, students of His Torah, and observers of His mitzvos.

#### ***5748***

**Rabbi Dovid Tzvi:** Merzbach, Be’er Sheva.

## 549

14 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and learned man, whose work is the work of Heaven, a man of many accomplishments and fine character, R. Yehuda Aryeh, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter: it seems that my words in my previous letter were not sufficiently explained, specifically regarding the main point. This concerns the substance of the paragraph regarding apologetic material. My point is not about its utility, but rather the opposite—the damage it causes. This is most apparent in our current era, as it provides grounds to argue that even in their own time, this was not the correct path, even if it may have seemed beneficial for the moment.

My reasoning and rationale are as follows: Apologetics, by its very nature, is a matter of compromise. And compromise is the opposite of truth. Ultimately, the truth must be revealed, and through this, the entire structure built upon compromise is undermined, along with the conclusions reached through the study of this compromise-based system—even in cases where the conclusions themselves are true, since they are conclusions of the true system as well. Although this has long been my firm opinion, my stay in the United States has provided practical experience and brought forth many proofs of this, both from actual events and from the conduct of the youth.

In truth, we do not need proofs. Since our Torah is a "Torah of life" and the truth is one, any deviation from it—even if the intention is desirable—will ultimately lead to damage, as it is not the way of the Torah. Who is greater than the Jewish scholars of the early generations? Their intentions were certainly desirable when they sought to explain various matters in our Torah and faith so that they would align with the philosophy dominant in their time. Yet, among their students and their students' students, this resulted in the opposite of what they had hoped. A significant portion of them made philosophy the authority and the final arbiter, to such an extent that the leaders of Israel in those days were forced to forbid the study of their books, at least for a certain period. Surely, the details are known to you, and there is no need to name names.

The damage was even more apparent in subsequent generations, and especially in our own, where even the non-believers reject that system of inquiry and say that it does not even deserve to be called "scientific inquiry." In the phrasing of Chazal, there is a concern that they might "distort the entire Torah because of their idle chatter." Specifically, recent innovators have caused particular bitterness—for example, the well-known *Maamar Or HaChaim* by the author of *Tiferes Yisrael*. His intention was desirable: to bring closer those who are drawn after science, so they would not distance themselves from the religion and faith of Israel. He wrote what he wrote in that *drush*, and furthermore, he even brought support from the Kabbalists (and I must say that it is a wonder to me, as it is to many others, where this is found in the printed Kabbalistic texts). With all due respect, he distorted the interpretation of several statements of Chazal.

At the end of this past winter—and because his commentary on the Mishnayos was accepted and publicized in general—many, even among truly G-d-fearing rabbis, announced that they accept what is stated in that *drush* (even though even in the period following him, and especially in our days, they **reject** the very scientific conclusions that the author of the *drush* used as a yardstick to which the content of the statements of Chazal must be adapted). Furthermore, they printed their opinion and publicized it among the youth and the younger generation, stating that the difficulties regarding several statements of Chazal raised by the theory of evolution, the Darwinian theory, etc., have already been resolved in the *Or HaChaim* *drush* of the author of *Tiferes Yisrael*!

An even more surprising example: It is known how much they struggled with the interpretation of the verse "and the earth stands forever," wondering how this could be reconciled with the Copernican system, and they considered it a matter of *mitzvah* to distort the interpretation of the verses, etc. Yet, the theory of relativity in our generation has been accepted by scientists as "absolute" truth (without, for the time being, emphasizing the internal contradiction within it). This theory states that both hypotheses—who is standing and who is revolving—are equal, and any difficulty found with one hypothesis will also be found (in a slightly different form) with the other. The same applies to Euclidean geometry and those who disagree with it; the conclusions of science now are that there is room for all of them, and any difficulty found with one hypothesis will also be found (in a slightly different form) with the other.

To assist in this, I have also written that one must declare—especially to the younger generation—that there is no room for difficulties regarding religion and faith, just as one does not raise questions against the "certain" (*bari*) based on the "doubtful" (*shema*). Through this, the entire impetus for writing apologetic and mediating material is nullified. And since the impetus is nullified, only the damage from this material remains—the damage of compromise, which cools a person down and "compromises" the truth. And as mentioned, it does not just compromise it; in its essence, it is the opposite of the truth.

In continuation of this, I also wrote my opinion that, since he comes from a place where the system of apologetics has spread, he should see the incorrectness of the matter. It is strange, even though there is an explanation for this as well: it is harder to prove the "doubtful" nature of science to some elderly rabbis of the old generation than it is to the young people who are engaged in science and are not as imbued with the feeling of faith—to such an extent has the fear of science and its intellect taken root in some of the aforementioned rabbis!

I will add the following lines: Since I fear that you, too, might find it difficult to undermine the foundations upon which the house of the Jewish scholars was built—those who labored so hard to build it—let me recall the wise proverb brought by several of the early authorities, which was also stated by the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, in one of his letters to the *Maskilim* of his time: "Plato is dear, Aristotle is dear, but the truth is dearer than all."

With blessings for success in your holy work to bring the hearts of the Children of Israel closer to our Torah, the Torah of truth and the Torah of life.

## 551

551

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Iyar.

I have already written to several of the institutions of Anash, and to all of them collectively, that reports have reached here regarding the discrimination against our Sephardic brethren. It is imperative that this discrimination be stopped from the outset, and for several reasons. The most fundamental reason is that who can know the greatness and stature of their soul and spirit, etc., especially since they are all equal and we all have one Father, as is explained at length in Chapter **32** of Tanya (and surely there is an old intention to be precise regarding this as well; see also Chapter 30 there and in many other places). It is astonishing that after these words, which carve out flames of fire, were spoken by our first father, the Alter Rebbe, there is a need for reminders and awakening regarding them from across the sea. Although it is not my practice to interfere in the specific arrangements pertaining to the management of any particular institution or committee—and even regarding the above, my intention is not to interfere in the details that must be discussed on-site by those appointed to such matters—I have come to address the essential and inner point, which must be the scarlet thread through which all details and actions are directed...

With blessings for good tidings regarding your personal matter about which you write, as well as regarding the matters of the community, and the more detailed, the better.

## 5152

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and refined individual, a descendant of holy ones,
R' Shmuel Abba, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated [5;10amp&] and the one preceding it. Many, many thanks for the most precious gift of the cane, which comes from a holy place. According to the words of our Sages, "He who gives, gives with a generous eye," and I thank you again for what you wrote in detail regarding it.

In due course, the *Chok L'Yisrael* volume of *Sefer Devarim* was received. My double and warm thanks for all of the above. May it be the will of Hashem that through this, there will also be an increase in the benefit to the many, for "the merit of the many assists," and may we all merit, speedily and in our days, the fulfillment of our prophet’s promise that the era of the "rod of affliction" will end and the era of the "rod of pleasantness" will begin. According to the teachings of Chassidus, this should be explained based on what is elucidated in the *maamarim* for the festival of Pesach by the Rebbe Maharash (in the *hemshech* of the *maamar* beginning *Vehecherim*, the *hemshech* *V'chakah Hagadol*, and others) regarding the distinction between the rod of Moshiach Tzidkeinu and the rod that rules in the period preceding it; see there.

You do not mention the state of your health in your letter, and I wish to interpret your silence on this matter as a sign that all is in order. May it be the will of Hashem that you return to your full strength in every respect. This is especially pertinent as we are currently in the days between Pesach, the time of our freedom, and Shavuos, the time of the Giving of our Torah—*charut* (engraved) on the tablets, read not as *charut* but as *cheirus* (freedom). May it be the will of Hashem that each of us merits, speedily and in our days, an increase in freedom from all matters that distract from *avodas Hashem*. This includes matters of physical health, as is also explained in the words of our Sages that all of Israel were healthy and whole for the receiving of the Torah, even in their bodies and in physical terms. This is understood even more clearly based on what is explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 49, regarding "And you have chosen us from all peoples and tongues," that the choice revealed at the time of the Giving of the Torah is the material body, etc.; see there.

With blessings for health and good tidings.

**5152**

**R' Shmuel Abba:** Shapira, Ramat Gan. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 14, 4866, and the references in the notes there.

**What you wrote in detail:** Today [the writer] elaborated... and he shall be honored to present to the Rebbe the "cane"—the last remnant of our family [descendants of the holy Rabbi Pinchas of Koritz] that remained after the "robberies" of the Bolsheviks and Hitler. I am very happy for the privilege I had, and that all these important items have come to their proper place. To Rabbi Pinchas, *ztz"l* (one of the brothers, the "Geshmessene" [descendants of Rabbi Pinchas of Koritz]), there was an only son, Rabbi Heshel, *ztz"l*, and an only daughter, Treina, *a"h*, who was the daughter-in-law of the son (or grandson) of Rabbi Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev, *ztz"l*. This cane fell to her husband as an inheritance. She traveled to Moscow to the prison of the brothers (Rabbi Pinchas and Rabbi Shmuel Abba, *z"l*) and brought the cane with her. One day, during a torrential rain and mud in the streets, she broke the cane. One of the Polish princes who helped us repaired the cane and made the new handle that is on it now.

Regarding the other holy objects he presented—see above, ibid., and the references in the notes there.

**The *Chok L'Yisrael* volume:** Which belonged to the "Geshmessene" and was with them during the time of their imprisonment (more than twenty years) in Moscow.

**Based on what is explained in *Tanya*:** See also above, Vol. 13, letter 4382; above, 5147; below, 5164.

## 553

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write regarding the enrollment of your students, may they live, to continue their studies in Chabad institutions. May it be His will that this be at a propitious and successful time, and may you and your fellow faculty members see good fruit from your labor in raising a generation in Yisrael of whom all who see them will recognize that they are the seed blessed by Hashem. My hope is strong that this will add vigor and greater strength to you and to all those working in the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, to go from strength to strength in this holy work. For when one adds a little below, much more is added from above, and in an incomparable measure, as is known from the words of our Sages in this week’s parsha regarding the verse, "And five of you shall chase a hundred, and a hundred of you shall chase ten thousand." It was a pleasure for me to read at the conclusion of your letter that you and your wife, may they live, see a blessing in the way of the Ribono shel Olam—which is measure for measure, only many times over—in the development of your children, may they live and be well.

Regarding teaching in another educational institution, it is understood that priority must be given to work in the vineyard of Chabad in its precise sense, and I refer to the affairs of the Reshet. Only if it is impossible in any way to find such an opportunity within the Reshet should one inquire about an offer from an educational institution that is on the foundation of holiness, even if it is not the vineyard of Chabad. This, of course, is on the condition that it will not harm or affect **at all** your work and dedication to the development of the Reshet institutions and the affairs of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad.

I am certain you will utilize the day of Lag B'Omer, and that you are also preparing a program in connection with the upcoming festival of Shavuos. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned, as well as in your personal matters.

## 554

554

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Nissan and the enclosure, as you requested, I will mention you once again at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for good tidings regarding all the matters you write about.

Regarding your concluding remarks about feeling discouraged because you feel you are working with *mesiras nefesh*, yet there are things you feel you are not naturally suited for—such as conducting outreach for children and the like:

Beyond the fact that this is highly doubtful—especially given the well-known principle that all matters of holiness are achieved only through *yegiah* (exertion), from which it is understood that one cannot know if he is capable until he engages in it with *yegiah*—even if we were to assume that this has been tested and proven as you write, surely such outreach, even if it cannot be done directly, you are certainly capable of stirring others among *anash* to engage in it. You can stir them through writing or speech, in public or in private, face-to-face, and so on. Since we see that the institution where you serve in holiness is in need of this outreach, while we cannot know for certain, it is highly probable that the primary duty and privilege to engage in this lies with the staff of the institution. As I have written in my previous letters, it seems that not only have they not engaged in this—and as the well-known saying goes regarding the word **esek** (engagement), as explained in the *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the precise language of "one who engages (*osek*) in Torah" and "one who engages in a *mitzvah*"—but they have not engaged in it not because they are perhaps unsuited for it, but because of the pretext that one person’s role is to be a *rosh yeshiva*, another’s to be a *mashgiach*, another’s to write receipts, and so on, and that they have no connection to the aforementioned outreach. It is understood that there is no reason or basis for this claim. Why should their portion be any less, at the very least, than other *anash* who are not in the institution? After all, someone must engage in the outreach of acquiring children, and certainly their share is greater according to the ruling that "the poor of your city take precedence," since they live in this city, and this is simple.

It is understood that these words are directed not only to you, but to all the *roshei yeshiva*, *mashgichim*, and *mashpi'im* who are in the yeshiva... or who are currently serving in this capacity. Furthermore, this also applies to the members of the administration, both past and present, as it appears that they, too, have not engaged in the aforementioned, which is the primary cause of the current state of the institution. There is no need to elaborate on a painful and distressing matter.

May the Giver of the Torah and the *mitzvos* send His word and improve your health and the health of your entire household, may they live. As is the well-known saying of the Alter Rebbe, who prayed: "May Hashem grant Jews *gashmius* (materiality), and they will make *gashmius* into *ruchnius* (spirituality)." When physical health increases, one's potential and inner desire to increase in spiritual health naturally grows as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 5157

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter of 9 Iyar, in which you write about your activities, both regarding yourself and regarding others. Surely you are not satisfied with what has been accomplished until now, since the command of our holy Torah is to "ascend in holiness," especially in this era of ours, where "there is no day that does not have its curse," which necessitates an ever-increasing strengthening of the side of holiness.

Regarding what you wrote about fasting half-days, etc. — this is surprising and a great wonder, for it does not align with what our Alter Rebbe writes in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*. Furthermore, it is tangibly evident that this weakens the concentration of thought required for deep study of the *nigleh*, and even more so for deep study of *Chassidus*. In such a case, there is also an explicit ruling in *Shulchan Aruch* that such a fast is contrary to the intended purpose. While it is understood and simple that there must be an element of *iskafya* — not giving in to oneself — there are many ways to perform this *avodah*, even regarding matters of eating and drinking, such as eating food that one does not find tasty, and so on and so forth, without resorting to the path of fasting, which is liable to cause the harm mentioned above.

Regarding your question, on your own behalf and on behalf of your fellow *bochurim* *sheyichyu*, concerning the *avodah* of spreading the wellsprings outward—that at times this interferes with the *yeshiva* schedule, and how they should conduct themselves—it is understood that all those who are in the *yeshiva*, and especially in *Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*, must conduct themselves in accordance with the instructions of the *yeshiva* administration, the *Rosh Yeshiva*, and the *mashpia*. However, you should explain the situation to them in detail and clarify why you are of the opinion that it is necessary to affect your own study schedules; but the final decision must be in accordance with the instructions of those mentioned above. May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in your *avodah* in both areas—both within yourselves and with others—in accordance with the will of the founders and directors of *Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*, our holy Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, may their merits shield us.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5458

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the interval, your letter of 5 Iyar was received, in which you write of several reasons for the inability to influence others, most of which are beyond your control, and you ask how to rectify the situation.

Now, all those reasons you write of are nothing new under the sun, and the advice for this is already found in the books of Chassidus and also in the books of mussar. You should study, in particular, the *Kuntres Hechalotzu*, from which one can understand several ways and methods to rectify the situation. Regarding the matter at hand, one general point should be added—based on the practice of several of the elder Chassidim from times past—when they would speak at a *farbrengen*, they did not address a private individual, and consequently, it was not emphasized to whom they were directing their words. Rather, they spoke about the matter requiring rectification and the manner in which to rectify it. Furthermore, this speech was phrased in such a way that it would not be highlighted to whom it was directed, and in this manner, every listener would take for himself the remedy (*dem retzept*) that applied to him. Furthermore—when speaking to an individual and not to a group—one should mention the general prerequisite for this: "Accept the truth from whoever says it." One must act according to what is appropriate, not because so-and-so says it, but because that is the truth.

It was pleasant for me to read what you wrote regarding the *avreich*... and surely you are showing him... the letters received from here.

It is surely superfluous to urge you to strengthen and encourage him, and likewise her, in all their matters, and you should endeavor that others do the same, especially from the *Ezras Nashim* regarding matters that pertain to them. And there is a presumption regarding *ta'amulah* that it does not return empty. Especially in the aforementioned case, where a great change for the better is evident in them...

It is my hope that you utilized the bright day of Lag B'Omer, the *hillula* of Rashbi, for the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and for the dissemination of the *ma'ayanos* in particular, through which one adds to the blessings of Hashem, and also in their own private matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all that is mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 559

559

By the Grace of G-d, 18 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write that it is explained in *Likutei Amarim* (Tanya) regarding the ascent in the *avodah* of love to the point of *kallos hanefesh*, and that this matter is accessible to every soul according to its level, etc. You therefore ask what you should do, since despite having tried this several times, you have not yet reached the aforementioned levels, and your heart tells you that the obstacles are the sins that create a separation, etc. You conclude by asking how to conduct yourself regarding this.

Now, according to what is explained in Tanya, it is understood that in this matter, as in all matters of holiness, the constant *avodah* is a progression from level to level, and not a leap from one extreme to the other. Such a leap occurs only occasionally as an *hora'as sha'ah* (a temporary directive), but this is not the regular path that is demanded of everyone. Based on this, it is also understood how to approach the *avodah* you are asking about: the beginning must be as explained in Tanya, Chapter 17—the love that leads to the performance of *mitzvos* alone—and similarly regarding *yirah*, see there, Chapter 41.

Along with this, it is understood and simple that there must be an *avodah* of *teshuvah*, since you mention in your letter the sins that create a separation. In this, too, the *avodah* is from level to level and in a manner of "from below to above"—that is, *teshuvah tata'ah*, as written in *Iggeret HaTeshuvah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1 (page 91a), and explained in greater detail in the introduction to the book *Derech Chaim* and in the book itself by the Mitteler Rebbe, the son of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe. After you stand on the aforementioned levels regarding *teshuvah*, *ahavah*, and *yirah*, you will ascend to a second level, and so on. When you work on the aforementioned as written in Tanya, with the exertion of the soul and the exertion of the body, you will be able to ascend in all of these "from strength to strength." As is known from the statement of our Sages (*Tanna D'bei Eliyahu*, Chapter 25) that every one of the Jewish people is obligated to say, "When will my deeds reach the deeds of my forefathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov?" However, it is obvious that this is not accomplished in a day or two, and there is absolutely no room to ask immediately why one has not been transformed from one extreme to the other.

You surely know of the three daily portions accessible to every soul, instituted by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*: the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, which are well known. Keep to them in addition to your regular, consistent study, both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5460

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, in which you write about your current place of work and the reasons for the changes in this regard.

You should present the entire matter in its details to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and accomplished man of character, Rabbi Shlomo שי' Metusof, who is certainly familiar with the matters in Morocco, and who surely seeks your well-being.

I must comment on the strange things you write—that you are not conducting yourself well at all, and that you feel that in your current location you are not conducting yourself well, unlike in another place. These words are alarming, as if the Torah and mitzvos were given only for specific places, and as if the powers of the neshamah Elokis are greater in one place than in another. Even though Chazal said that "there is a land that raises [people]...", the two places you write about are equal in this regard. As you write in your letter, the difference is only that you have a desire in one place and not in the other. It is obvious that this has no influence whatsoever on the obligation and necessity to conduct yourself in accordance with the mitzvos of the Creator of the world and its Guide, who is the Giver of the Torah and the mitzvos.

I trust you know and keep the three daily study portions established for every soul by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—in addition to the other study portions in Nigleh and Chassidus.

With blessings.

## 5061

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Thursday, 5 Iyar.

It gave me pleasure to read that you are drawing closer to the matters of Chassidus, both in the study of its teachings and in following its guidance and conduct. May it be His will that in this, too, the directive of our Sages, "We increase in holiness," will be fulfilled, and that you will go "from strength to strength." There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since many of anash in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established, will surely assist you in this.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the question of future livelihood, finding a purpose, and the like: you should begin with the custom of the esteemed residents of Jerusalem, as it is heard here, who sit and occupy themselves with Torah and avodah. When the time comes to engage in shidduchim, you will then be able to determine your path in matters of livelihood, in accordance with the shidduch and the requirements of the bride’s side. It is a pity to scatter your soul now on matters that will only come to the fore after some time.

Regarding what you wrote about the avreich... may he live, who feels that he is rising and falling in his avodas Hashem: it is understood that there are many levels in the aforementioned. However, the common denominator in all of them is that, G-d forbid, this should cause despair or even a falling of spirit, etc., as the matter is explained in the holy Tanya in several places, regarding how a person’s heart should not fall within him, etc. Even so, it is understood and simple that he must fight against the descent and eventually nullify it, as this is also explained in the Tanya. The specific instructions for this depend on the nature of his soul and his environment, as not all the details can be put into writing; therefore, he should consult with the elders of anash in his vicinity.

I trust that you are taking an active part in the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, commensurate with your ability and talents. May you share good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 542

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the relationship with your son, may he live and be well: surely the relationship is improving little by little, and the main thing is that it should improve in the future. It is understood that when a person lives in a place where there are relatively few people, the traits of the human soul—which are not always perfect—are more noticeable than when one lives in a very large city, where the relationships between people are not close at all, and certainly not tight-knit, so one does not pay as much attention to such things.

Furthermore—and I am sure you will forgive me for this remark—it is generally in your son’s nature to be to himself (*far zich*), even when he is among people. And this trait—which is even more pronounced when he is in an environment where everyone is involved with one another (*oysgemisht*)—leads the other person to interpret this distance as a matter of coldness, and as "water reflects the face to the face."

With blessings.

## 5463

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Iyar, in which you transcribe the commentary of the Abarbanel at the beginning of Parshas Behar Sinai, etc.

Here, too, is a wondrous point revealed through the teachings of Chassidus, which is encapsulated in the well-known Torah of the Baal Shem Tov regarding the verse, "If you see the donkey of your enemy... you shall surely release it with him" — that this refers specifically to the body (printed in *Hayom Yom*, 28 Shevat 5703). This is explained further in the teachings of Chassidus, that in the time to come, the neshamah will receive vitality from the body even in matters of Elokus. Although this subject requires an extensive explanation that is difficult to transcribe in a letter, the result and conclusion are nonetheless understood: even though a person must make a reckoning of his soul, and matters of the body must be secondary to matters of the neshamah throughout all the days of his life—and certainly during those years discussed in the commentary of the Abarbanel—the intention is not that there should be an avodah that has no connection to the body. Rather, it means that in matters of the body, one should "know Him" — Hashem — in all your ways. As explained in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 3, the concept of *da'as* is a term denoting connection and bonding. Through this, "in all your ways"—which are primarily matters of the body, as explained in *Tur* and *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, siman 231—one arrives at a connection and bonding with Hashem. And this is simple to understand, for then, in a natural way, there is peace of mind, because the desires of the body do not cause confusion. However, all this applies to the desire, but not to the essence of the matter of eating and drinking, etc.

With blessings.

## 5464

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Shaul Yissachar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev the bright day of the Hillula of Rashbi, the eve of Atzeres.

At a time of favor, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you need, in accordance with the content of your letter... May it be G-d’s will that you bring good news regarding the improvement of your health very soon.

Especially as we are currently in the days between the festival of Pesach, the time of our liberation, and the festival of Shavuos, the time of the Giving of our Torah—"Charus" (engraved) on the tablets; read not "Charus" but "Cheirus" (freedom)—may it be G-d’s will that each and every one of us increases in freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem. This includes matters of physical health, as explained by our Sages of blessed memory, that all of Israel were healthy and whole for the receiving of the Torah, even in their bodies and in their physicality. This is understood even more clearly according to what is explained in the holy Tanya, Chapter 49, regarding "And You have chosen us from all nations and tongues," that the choice—revealed at the time of the Giving of the Torah—is specifically regarding the material body, etc. See there.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your observation on Likutei Torah, Bamidbar (in the discourse *U'Sefartem*, end of section 1), where it is written, "and the cows that carried the Ark in the days of David"—for this occurred even before the reign of Shaul, as the verses prove.

—And it should be noted that in the explanation of this matter in the Tzemach Tzedek’s Sefer HaMitzvos, Mitzvas HaOmer and Sefirah, section 1, the words "in the days of David" do not appear—

However, according to what is written in I Shmuel 7:2, II Shmuel 5:4-5, and II Shmuel 6:3, it is proven that at the event where the cows carried [the Ark], David was seventeen years old. The connection between "the cows sang" and David is **emphasized** in the words of our Sages of blessed memory (Avodah Zarah 24b, Midrash Shmuel, Yalkut Shimoni in its place, and elsewhere), who stated that the song they sang was "Give thanks to Hashem, etc.," which David commanded to be recited before the Ark (I Divrei HaYamim 16). See the commentary of the Radak in Divrei HaYamim there, according to which other opinions regarding the song of the cows can also be understood.

For the connection of the matter of the song of the cows to David according to Chassidus, see the Tzemach Tzedek on Tehillim, chapter 98, and the discourse *Hodu LaHashem* (Sefer HaMaamarim 5627).

## 5065

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rav, G-d-fearing and learned, known as Dr. Shapiro,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have heard from circles of Rabbis and yeshiva students of your success in your holy work—the healing of people’s bodies. For a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem, as expressed by our teacher the Rambam, who was a physician of both the soul and the body, in Hilchos Deios, beginning of chapter 4. Although I am certain that you are not in need of encouragement or requests regarding this—especially as you are a Rav and a teacher of Torah in Israel, one of the remnants of the old generation who has ascended to settle in our Holy Land, may it be built and established by Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—nevertheless, as our Sages say, "We only urge those who are already diligent."

I am writing these lines because the person in question, who is known to me as an esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and a man of fine character, is Rabbi [Name], who is turning to you regarding his health, and he will explain the details himself.

May it be the will of Hashem that what is dependent upon you for the swift recovery and complete healing of the Rav, may he live, should be successful.

I am sure that you also follow the custom of many G-d-fearing physicians who, when approached for advice regarding physical healing, take the opportunity to also inspire the healing of the soul. Everyone, especially in our generation—this orphaned generation—is in need of this, as it is written, "There is no righteous man on earth who does good and does not sin." This is especially true when we see tangibly that improving the state of the soul’s health also brings about an improvement in the state of the body’s health, literally. This is in accordance with the command of the verse, "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d," with the 248 limbs and 365 sinews of the body, and likewise of the soul, which correspond to the 248 positive mitzvos and 365 negative mitzvos, as explained by our teacher the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, regarding this verse (Likutei Torah, Parshas Nitzavim, page 45c).

With respect and with a blessing for success in the healing of bodies and the healing of souls.

I assume that what is printed in Otzar HaPoskim, Vol. 1 (2nd edition, page 164, column 2), that you perform prostate surgery **without** severing the duct, and that this remains the case even after the surgery—is true and that you still practice this way. If so, you should certainly publicize this in all medical journals, as it affects many people. For example, the doctors here say (and have influenced several of the Rabbis as well) that it is mandatory to sever it.

#### ***5065***

**As is the custom of many physicians:** See also above, Vol. 13, letters 4501, 4708; Vol. 14, letter 5160.

## 5507

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Emor, in which you write about the difficulties you have encountered—it is somewhat surprising and also distressing, as it seems this involved not only physical preoccupation but also mental preoccupation and a scattering of the soul. While there is some justification for physical preoccupation, given that we are in *galus* (see *Kuntres U'Maayan* by the Rebbe Rashab, *maamar* 17), there is no justification for the preoccupation and strain of the soul. Furthermore, it is not only unhelpful, but on the contrary, it is distracting. As is known by the parable of one who wears garments that are too long and large for his body: not only is there no benefit for walking with agility, but it actually hinders it. See also *Torah Or* by the Alter Rebbe, beginning of *Parshas Noach*, and the *Sefer HaMitzvos* also called *Derech Mitzvosecha* by the Tzemach Tzedek, in the *mitzvah* of the *metzora's* shaving. As is known, the precision of the verse, "When you eat the labor of your hands, you are fortunate and it is good for you," refers to the labor of your hands, not the labor of the head and the mind. Even though it is not an easy task to prevent physical preoccupation from disturbing the contemplation of the mind—where the power of thought must be clothed—man is born to toil, and this is well understood.

Regarding your question as to whether it is permitted to explain to women those matters of the Torah of Hashem that would make it easier for them to bear the distress of the times, etc.:

It is surprising that there is even a doubt about this, especially in our generation—the generation of the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, the final generation of *galus*, in which we must prepare for all the matters and conditions of the future, in the *aschalta d'geulah* and the *geulah* itself. It is known from the statement of our Sages that the future *geulah* will be in the likeness of the exodus from Egypt, which came about in the merit of the righteous women of that generation. Especially since, in such matters, women have always been obligated to know these concepts; this is why they were present at the discourses of the Sages even in the time of the *Tana'im*. All of the above is explained as a halachic ruling in the laws of *Talmud Torah*, including the laws of *Talmud Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, end of chapter 1; see there. For these matters are included in the laws that they are required to know, as is visibly apparent: without understanding the concepts of *hashgacha pratis*, the purpose of man's creation, his true good, etc., etc., it is very difficult to withstand all the trials of the time.

Regarding what you wrote about a special study of subjects that pertain more to a *chassan* than to others, you should speak about this with the elders of *anash* in your vicinity, and they will instruct you.

It is my hope that from time to time you are increasing the consistency of your times for studying *Chassidus* and are being meticulous in fulfilling its guidance and customs, for each and every one of us is commanded to ascend in holiness.

With the blessing in the style of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 5068

B”H, 21 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 28th of Iyar.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the matters about which you write.

Regarding what you wrote—that your heart is "clogged" [tumtam], etc.—it is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the prohibition against *lashon hara* applies not only to speaking about others, but also to speaking about oneself. Just as it is necessary in *avodas Hashem* not to minimize one’s shortcomings, so too is it necessary to acknowledge one’s own virtues, as is tangibly evident. One of the tactics of the *yetzer hara* is to cast sadness and a sense of despair upon a person who serves his Creator, by saying, "Who are you, and what good will your efforts do?" etc. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter, especially as we approach the receiving of the Torah. Although we are currently in need of the preparatory work of *Sefiras HaOmer*—which is the work of human effort to refine the *midos* through the drawing down of the *Omer* and beyond—there is nonetheless a special *segulah* for these days regarding *siyata d’shmaya* from above. This is because these days are a continuation of the days of *Pesach*, when the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, revealed Himself and transported [the Jewish people] from one extreme to the other: from the depths of the 49 gates of impurity to the heights of the 49 gates of holiness, up to the 50th gate at the time of the Giving of the Torah. See also *Zohar Chadash*, beginning of *Parshas Yisro*, the response of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai to Rabbi Yissa Zeira of the *Chavraya*, and its conclusion, "Every day He brings us out," etc. See also *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 32.

May it be His will that you bring good news regarding the improvement of your health, both literally and figuratively, and regarding your increased efforts in spreading Yiddishkeit and the wellsprings of Chassidus, especially wherever your influence reaches, in a manner of "ever-increasing."

With blessings in the style of the Rav, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 569

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5717

In response to your letter of 7 Iyar.

It is surprising that you do not mention the treatment suggested by the doctor, for in cases such as these, several treatments have been developed in recent years and months, including artisan and cortisone and others. It is possible that this is merely an oversight in your report, but if not, it is appropriate to specifically inquire about this matter.

Regarding what you write as the reason for your non-participation in the shiurim (and apparently this is also the reason for your non-participation in the activities of N'shei Chabad in general), since these activities are a *segulah* for what a person and their household require, it is understood that there is no place to postpone them to a later time, as the need is in the present. Regarding all good deeds, one should learn from the words of the Mishnah: "Whoever fulfills the Torah in poverty (literally, or in difficult circumstances in general) will eventually fulfill it in wealth." May Hashem grant you success and may you have good news to report.

With blessings,

Secretary

## 5770

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Chaim Moshe, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Surely, even though you do not mention it, you are making preparations well in advance to utilize the vacation days, especially the Yomim Tovim, and are not relying on the last minute. On a humorous note, one might point out the difference between the Exodus from Egypt and our own redemption, which is soon to come: our forefathers left Egypt in haste, whereas now, "you shall not go out in haste" (Yeshaya 52:12), as is explained in many places in Chassidus, including in the *Hemshech* "V'Kacha" at its conclusion. Since the redemption depends on preparation in the time of Galus that mirrors this, the above is understood as well.

Included in this is also the notification regarding your activities. In this regard, at least in the future, do not wait for repeated requests from here; rather, establish a routine to report on such matters at least once a week. We see tangibly that the necessity of reporting also adds to the bringing of things from potential into action—from revealed powers, and from time to time, from hidden powers as well.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success, and your wife, may she live, to bring good tidings from your activities—each according to its nature and within the appropriate framework—which are growing and expanding, as is required by the demands and necessities of the hour.

With blessings in the style of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 5771

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Damiel
Greetings and blessings,

I have just received your letter from the auspicious day of Lag B’Omer, and I was so taken aback by its content that I am compelled to answer it immediately, out of the usual order.

What surprised me most is your impression that I am dissatisfied with your teaching and your influence upon your students. Even more surprising—and distressing—is your intention to cease this work.

Where you could have derived such an idea is a great mystery, for my position is known to all and is the exact opposite of your conclusion. I have stated, repeatedly and emphatically, that in these times, every individual must utilize every possibility and every channel to disseminate the matters of Yiddishkeit in every place, circle, and environment—providing practical guidance, opinions, and a worldview based on traditional Yiddishkeit. It is a simple matter that this includes the daughters of Israel, with even greater emphasis, since they are the ones who build the home in Israel. Upon their education and the influence exerted upon them depends whether they will be the *akeres habayis* (the foundation of the home) or, Heaven forbid, the *okeres habayis* (the one who uproots the home), which affects generations and generations to come.

Especially regarding yourself, having seen success in your work in this field and having stirred the inner point of their hearts—how could it enter your mind to desist from this?

As for your concluding remark that your verse now is "He sits alone and is silent, he puts his mouth in the dust," this is entirely incorrect. I have already spoken about this in a lighthearted vein, but in truth, there is a profound and unique point here: the matter of *shlilas hara* (negating evil) on its own existed even before the creation of the worlds and the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. All of the descent from the "high mountain" to the "deep pit" is specifically for the sake of the matters of "arise and do."

Based on this, one can also understand what is explained in various places in *Chassidus*, that the essence is the *mitzvos asei* (positive commandments), and the *mitzvos lo saasei* (negative commandments) come only to prepare the person, the matters, and the world for the drawing down of the light through the *mitzvos*.

The two verses you mentioned are recited on Tisha B’Av, a day of destruction, ruin, and darkness—not in the context of building and light, which is the task of each and every one of us. As is known, the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek: "We are the workers of the day—to make it bright."

I am sending this letter as urgent and express, and I look forward to hearing good news from you, that the content of your last letter was written under the influence of a passing mood, which has since passed and left no impression.

With respect and with a blessing for success in drawing the hearts of the children of Israel to our Father in Heaven, in a manner where the heart is divided among all the limbs—that from the feeling of the heart, it should be drawn into the 248 limbs of the *neshamah* through the fulfillment of the 248 *mitzvos asei*, and into the 365 veins of the *neshamah* through the observance of the 365 *mitzvos lo saasei* (see *Tanya*, Chapter 51; *Likutei Torah*, *Nitzavim* 45c, the explanation of the verse "You shall be wholehearted"), and looking forward to good news as mentioned above.

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for the holiday of Pesach and for the *Nashi Chabad*, in which my view on the above is also emphasized.

## 5172

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Tuvia, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding your birthday:

I trust you have followed the custom of Anash in recent times: giving tzedakah on your birthday before Shacharis and Mincha—or on the preceding day if the birthday falls on Shabbos or Yom Tov—studying an additional shiur in both Nigleh and Chassidus, receiving an aliyah to the Torah on your birthday or the preceding Shabbos, and studying the three daily portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—on your birthday.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be a year of success for you, both materially and spiritually, and may you increase your Torah study and the performance of His mitzvos with abundance, including the dissemination of the wellsprings as required, and so on...

Regarding the precision in the language of the Alter Rebbe (concerning Bedikas Chametz) in his Siddur: "He should have his household members stand..."—without a condition (see his language in Shulchan Aruch, 432:8).

He explains that if he were to search alone, he would become weary and his search would be diminished.

Now, consider: a) It is only regarding women that it is said they are "lazy." b) According to this, it should specifically depend on the condition of the size of the house, etc.

If we say that the precision in the Siddur is intentional (and not merely that the language was copied from the Shulchan Aruch, as the Siddur does not delve into copying the details of the laws), one could say the reason is that he holds it is a mitzvah to also grant his household members the merit of this mitzvah, for in their searching, they are performing a mitzvah (see Shulchan Aruch there, end of section 9), even though the obligation is not upon them. That is to say, it is a mitzvah to grant others the merit of performing a mitzvah, even one that is not a personal obligation (*chovas gavra*). Furthermore, it teaches us that since he himself will also search a little, there is no issue of "a mitzvah is better performed by oneself than by one's agent" (contrary to the implication of the language in his Shulchan Aruch). There is much to learn from this for many matters, and it teaches us a great deal. This is not the place to elaborate.

#### ***5172***

**R' Tuvia, may he live:** Beloy, Jerusalem. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 13, p. 446, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 5173

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, etc.,
R' Alexander Zisha, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby confirm receipt of your letter from Chol HaMoed Pesach, along with its enclosure—which was delayed somewhat in transit. In it, you write of your activities and your work in the "work of Heaven," which is the field of chinuch. Since you write of your roots—stemming from the elder Chassidim—and that you have drawn much from this Chassidus from the primary sources, I am hopeful that this influence is also evident in your impact on your students and those you educate. 

This is especially true because, while in all recent generations and in all lands there was a necessity for additional Chassidic light and warmth in order to withstand unusual winds, in our own time, we are even more in need of this special fortification provided by the "light within Chassidus." This is necessary to withstand even those winds—which, unfortunately, have become common in the Jewish street—that are undesirable. Since every member of the youth will, in the near future, build a home in Yisrael, it is understood that every positive change effected in the student may fundamentally alter the character of the home he will build once he leaves the four cubits of the educational institution where he currently resides.

From this, it is understood that every effort and endeavor in such matters is worthwhile, for the matter affects many. May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that, in accordance with His attribute—which is "measure for measure," but many times over—you will derive much true nachas, which is traditional, Chassidic Jewish nachas, from your descendants, may they live.

With respect and blessing, in the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter concerning your state of health... I have already written to you about this: in my opinion, and as I have seen tangibly in many such cases, the more you increase your courage and efforts in strengthening and developing the holy institution, the more your health will increase—even in the simple sense of physical health. There is enough time during the day for the natural matters required for physical health—eating, sleeping, etc.—and the exertion in matters of... can be done without tiring yourself at all.

It is understood that I do not mean, G-d forbid, to diminish the avodah you have done until now, but in all matters of good and holiness, there is always room for addition. The matter depends only on the will of the person, for the ability is given to each and every one to fulfill his role in this world, which is, in the language of the Mishnah, "I was created to serve my Maker," and with joy and a glad heart.

## 5740

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter in which you write that you wish to know the root of the difference between *mussar* and *Chassidus*, etc.

You should study the *kuntres* "Toras HaChassidus" and "Limud Toras HaChassidus" from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, where these matters are explained well, as are many similar topics.

Regarding what you write at the end of your letter, how it is possible to speak of a physical object that a person acquires, given that the human soul is spiritual:

Since the human soul is bound to the body, which is also physical, through this it has a connection to other physical matters as well. Furthermore, it even has a connection to matters that are the opposite of its nature—that is, to matters that oppose spirituality, which is the materiality within the physical. Regarding a Jewish person, whose essence is the *nefesh elokis* within him, it is nevertheless possible for a person to sin because the body and the *nefesh habehamis* conceal and hide the *nefesh elokis*.

Surely you have heard of the three daily study sessions established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, which are well known. In any event, you should keep to them from here on.

## 5770

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you also write about your conduct, and in particular your conduct regarding eating, and regarding matters connected to physical health. Our holy Torah, the Torah of the living G-d, instructs us that one must follow everything the doctor says, for the Torah has granted permission to the physician, and he is nothing more than a messenger. It is understood that you may present to the doctor the arguments and reasoning you have regarding this, including the reasoning you wrote to me; however, once the doctor has heard these arguments, you must follow his instructions, regardless of whether they align with your own reasoning or not. As mentioned above, the doctor is merely a messenger who acts with the power and permission that the Torah has granted him, and since this is derived from the Torah, it is a benefit for both the body and the soul alike. Even if one does not understand this, or if it seems otherwise, this is not a wonder, for the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He. It is no wonder, then, that a person does not understand everything that is in the Torah, yet a person must fulfill everything that is written in the Torah even without understanding, and eventually, the understanding will come.

I hope that you will follow everything mentioned above, and do so with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 5716

5716

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Beyond the significance of the gathering itself—which, as you write, stirred memories of days gone by when you were within the four cubits of Torah, memories which will surely lead to an increase in action—the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself: the development of education based on the purity of holiness, Torah, and fear of Heaven, both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus. It is understood that the above, as with many matters, is that the gathering and its success are akin to plowing and sowing. Just as in the parable of a seed that is sown, it requires cultivation in order to become a tree that produces fruit and beauty—and cultivation at the appropriate time, specifically—you will surely strive to utilize this opportune time and the moment of inspiration of the participants in the gathering to bring all the resolutions into action, and to add to them as well. This is especially true regarding all those who, for whatever reason, did not participate in the gathering. May it be His will that you succeed in this as well, with the emphasis that time is a loss that cannot be recovered, especially when the matter concerns education, where in the years of childhood and youth, every hour has much greater importance than that same duration of time during the years of adulthood and old age...

I await good news regarding all the above.

P.S.
From the article you wrote in the newspaper regarding the gathering, your talent for writing suitable for public dissemination is evident. It would be worthwhile to utilize this talent more frequently, for our era demands the mobilization of all strengths and talents for the strengthening and dissemination of Yiddishkeit.

## 576

B.H., Motzoei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Bamidbar, 5717, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Convention of
Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad of the U.S. and Canada
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and Peace!

I hereby send my greetings and blessing to all the participants and members of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad on the occasion of your annual gathering. May the Ribono shel Olam help you translate all the vital plans of the convention into constantly growing achievements and increasingly diverse activities. For the ultimate purpose of *machshava* (thought) and *dibbur* (speech) is *maaseh* (action) in practice.

In accordance with the well-known saying of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad—whose name you also bear—that one must **"live with the times,"** meaning with the content of the weekly parsha, may your gathering bring life and vitality from the Source of life, our Torah, the *Toras Chaim*, as illuminated by Chassidus, the *Divrei Elokim Chaim*, into your work in general, and into your work according to the instructions and hints of the weekly parshiyos in particular.

One of the themes of the parshiyos **Bamidbar** and **Naso**, between which this convention takes place, is the shared subject of the Mishkan in the desert and the duties that were distributed in connection with transporting the Mishkan from place to place.

This emphasizes that even when Yidden find themselves in a desert, they have the power to establish a *makom kadosh*, a Mishkan, for the Divine Shechinah to rest among Yidden in general, and within every Yid in particular.

Just as there is a desert in the physical sense—a wasteland where extreme climatic elements and all sorts of harmful forces prevail—so too is there a **spiritual desert**, where the most harmful spiritual ideologies prevail. This can exist even in a land that is, physically, a blooming garden.

Our holy Torah teaches us that when one finds oneself in a spiritual desert, one can, one must, and one is obligated to establish a *Mikdash*, to carry it, and to move forward in the footsteps of the Divine Shechinah, until one reaches the G-d-blessed Holy Land, to the true and full Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

This is an instruction for **all** Yidden, but especially for Jewish women, for it is well known that when the Mishkan was being built, the women were the first to respond, even before the men.

In the spiritual desert of certain circles where a wasteland and emptiness prevail regarding Yiddishkeit in general—to say nothing of Chassidishe *avodah* in particular—you have the great and eternal *zechus* to be among the first to establish a Mishkan *lo yisbarach* here in general, and also within those circles. I hope that you will fulfill your life’s mission with devotion and vitality.

I especially wish to draw attention to the necessity of concerning yourselves not only with adults, but also with the very young children. For as one sees clearly, when one begins to educate a child in a certain direction from a very early age, one is assured of much greater success and of greater and better fruits.

With the blessing that you should be successful in your work, which will also add to Hashem’s blessings in your personal matters,

And, in the style of the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh-h*, *navgam*, *ziya*—that each one of us, within the collective of Klal Yisrael, should receive the Torah with joy and with *pnimiyus* (inwardness).

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 5178

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest silence, I received your letter from Lag B’Omer. It did not contain the reason for your silence until now, and we do not cry over the past; may it be Hashem’s will that it be rectified, at the very least, regarding the future.

I was pleased to read in your letter about your meeting with Mr. ... It is worth the effort to awaken in him the rock from which he was hewn. He must utilize this point with full force, especially since he comes from a family that dedicated their entire lives to the Torah of Chassidus and its matters. Certainly, the souls demand of every descendant to act in this specific direction as much as is necessary. Their obligation in this precedes many of their other endeavors, as this is a matter that cannot be done by others. That is to say, a descendant of a family that for several generations has occupied itself with Chassidus possesses a special talent for understanding this Torah and a unique ability to convey it to others. It is simple that the influence of this Torah must be evident in the private life of the descendant as well; for if it is said regarding all parts of the holy Torah that "great is study, for it leads to action," and regarding one who learns with the intent not to act, etc., then how much more so does this apply to the Torah of Chassidus, in which the Baal Shem Tov emphasized, "You shall surely unload with him"—with the body and its matters.

Regarding your question of what to study with the aforementioned individual: it is understood that this depends on his level of knowledge and the nature of his soul. Regarding such matters, it is also said that one should study in the place where his heart desires. It would be worthwhile to show him the booklet *Some Aspects*, in which the necessity of action is emphasized, even regarding the understanding of intellectual concepts.

Regarding the medical examination: in general, the entire matter of such examinations is nothing more than a precaution. Therefore, one should avoid an internal examination as much as possible. It seems clear that, aside from adding to the doctor’s knowledge, there is no other benefit in it. Therefore, in a delicate manner—without hurting the doctor’s feelings—one should avoid it. Hopefully, the doctor will not insist on it, seeing that you are not comfortable with it, and knowing for himself how unnecessary it is for practical purposes.

Regarding nursing the child yourself, this is a very, very proper thing. Especially in recent years, even American doctors have begun to speak and write about how good this is, both for the mother and for the child.

As for what you write about being sensitive, there is nothing to overthink here. This is a normal thing and that is how it should be, as it is written, "G-d made man upright, but they sought..." May Hashem Yisbarach help that the birth should be in an easy manner, at a good and auspicious time, with a whole and healthy child, and that you should raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S.
You will surely inform me in detail about the Lag B’Omer gathering, and may Hashem grant you success in bringing good news in this as well.

## 5479

By the Grace of G-d
25 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Moshe, may he live:

Shalom and blessing!

In response to your letter of 13 Iyar, in which you write regarding your activities to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit: It is surely unnecessary to remind someone like yourself not to be satisfied with the achievements attained thus far, but rather to increase your courage in accordance with the demands—and indeed the necessity—of the hour, to campaign for all the sanctities of traditional Judaism, pure Torah, and yiras shamayim. If this campaign was necessary in all times and in all places, the necessity is many times greater in this bitter galus, where the darkness is doubled and redoubled to the point that "they call darkness light and light darkness," and false ideologies are not only not diminishing, but are actually gaining strength. And if this is the case in the Diaspora, how much more so in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—where any deviation from the path of the King, King of Kings, the Giver of the Torah and the mitzvos, within the very palace of this King, causes damage and destruction many times greater, especially when such a deviation is made into a permanent way of life.

Instead of the foundation of our faith—that we have only one Hashem and one Torah, which was given to one nation that "dwells alone and is not reckoned among the nations"—they make it their slogan and guiding principle to "be like all the nations," and they associate the Name of Heaven with ideals that have their source in the sitra achra. Even the best among them associate the Name of Heaven with something else, which is also the opposite of faith, even if the thing itself is permissible, and even if the thing itself is inherently good (had they **not** made an idol out of it, similar to the teaching of our Sages regarding the *matzeivah* which was beloved in the days of the Patriarchs, etc.).

It is understood that this campaign is not easy and will arouse opposition from various circles—and, unfortunately, even from those who disguise themselves and claim to be religious. But this very opposition necessitates waging war against the system of incitement and leading astray from the path of our ancestors with all possible force. And since our generation is required to wage this war, even though it is an "orphaned generation," it is certain that the strength to conduct this war and ultimately win it was granted from the outset. Everyone who has influence in a certain circle must view this campaign as their specific shlichus for this period.

I have already spoken at length elsewhere that the statement of our Sages that in the footsteps of Moshiach "each day's curse is greater than the last" is not intended, Heaven forbid, to frighten the Jewish people. Rather, it is an instruction (like all matters of Torah, which is a language of *hora'ah*—instruction) that it is impossible today to be satisfied with the state of Yiddishkeit of yesterday. Since the curse has increased, this necessitates an increase and multiplication in the side of good. And this is easy to understand.

May it be the will of the Almighty that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned, with the blessing in the formula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for this time of year: to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 580

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Iyar, in which you write of the request by the avreichim of Montreal to transcribe the maamar "Pasach Eliyahu" from Torah Or, including the glosses of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) n'e, onto a stencil, and you request permission for this.

Regarding the practical aspect: if this is a request from many, and provided that the transcription is from a carefully proofread text, and that they proofread the transcription multiple times so that it is as accurate as possible, I can grant the aforementioned request. It is understood and simple that, as you write, this must only be done in a manner that does not interfere at all with his affairs, in accordance with the schedule of the yeshiva, the studies, the chazarah, etc.

It is surprising that you do not mention your studies with hasmadah and shekidah, the increase in this from time to time in accordance with the instruction to "ascend in matters of holiness," and the influence upon all your peers so that they too will apply themselves to their studies as much as is required. Surely you will fill this in on the next opportunity.

With blessings.

581

By the Grace of G-d

Brooklyn

Mr. Yosef Alter, known as Dr. Tomarkin
