## 5743

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs, R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Sivan.

I was pleased to hear that you have begun to organize a detailed program regarding the days of the Chag HaGeulah, 12 and 13 Tammuz, may they come upon us for good. You should certainly involve all those who will be required to act upon the discussion of the matter afterward; when they are involved in the planning, there is greater certainty that they will fulfill what is incumbent upon them [unlike those who overvalue themselves, to whom, when one brings ready-made instructions, their assumption (the tendency to procrastinate) is that it should be the opposite, or done in a different way].

Regarding what you wrote about the expenses — G-d willing, I will urge Anash to participate in this through half of the special collection.

It is somewhat surprising that you wrote that your plan is for the gathering to last at most two hours! What is limiting you in this?

The delay in sending the Tikkun board for the material for the publication is due to a multitude of preoccupations. In the near future, it will be evaluated and sent to you, and then it would be worthwhile to print it immediately, rather than delaying and printing a double issue or the like.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, with joy and goodness of heart, and for good tidings in your personal matters as well,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote about parables in Chassidus Chabad: they are extremely few, and they are not of the type of parables used by Maggidim and the like—that is, in the description of a story, etc. Rather, they are like the parables found in the Midrash and the like: "A parable to a king of flesh and blood," etc. Instead of these, Chassidus Chabad utilizes and relies on the concept of "from my flesh I behold Elokus"—to find the concepts in spirituality, within the soul and its processes. The advantage is that the parable itself **descends** from the nimshal—from the matters above (see Tanya, beginning of Chapter 3). The few parables that can be found, a significant portion of them are noted on the spot in the book from which they were copied, such as the parable of the Tekias Shofar and the like.

#### ***5743***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 20, p. 583, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live:** Glitzenstein, Lod. Additional letters to him appear above, 5392, and in the notes indicated there.

## 544

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Sivan, in which you write regarding your state of health, that of your wife—may she live and be well—and also regarding your livelihood.

I am surprised by the tone of your writing. After you have seen with your own eyes the open kindnesses of Hashem Yisbarach and His miracles in saving you from the camps, etc., and now that you find yourself in a place where there is, G-d forbid, no danger at all, you remain stuck on the question, "From where will my help come?"—forgetting that immediately following that, it is written, "My help is from Hashem."

It goes without saying that I do not intend this as a rebuke. The statement of our Sages is well known: "Do not judge your fellow until you have reached his place," and "Judge every person favorably." I only wish to illuminate the matter as it truly is. Once you see this, you will realize how much you need to be strong in your bitachon in the Creator of the world and its Guide. The stronger your bitachon, the sooner you will see an increase in the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach.

This is even more relevant to your situation: even when seeking work or any other matter of livelihood, the other person senses how confident you are in obtaining the work or the profit, and this influences them to fulfill your request—as we see this tangibly.

It is self-understood that one must also act according to the ways of nature, but what I have said above is also included in nature. It is also understood that one must increase in matters of mitzvos, for this is the channel and the means to increase the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in the areas where you are in need.

It would be a proper thing to have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are kosher according to the law. Furthermore, your wife—may she live and be well—should observe the good custom of the virtuous daughters of Israel to give charity before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. It is understood that this should be done without a vow.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5145

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Through the intermediary of the G-d-fearing, illustrious, and accomplished Chossid, R' Dovber Baumgarten, may he live, I received his *pan* (petition), which will be read at a time of favor at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that he brings us good tidings.

It was pleasing for me to learn that he had the merit of studying at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in our country in the past. Since the words of the *tzaddikim* are alive and endure forever, this is all the more true of their actions—especially the efforts they invested in the students of Tomchei Temimim, whether directly, for those students who merited to come to them, to see them, and to speak with them, or indirectly, through the *mashpi'im* and the *rosh yeshiva* who received instructions from the *Nesi'im* (leaders) who directed the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva regarding the *temimim* under their guidance.

It is understood that it is possible that over the years, matters accumulate that cover this over, similar to any object that needs to be cleaned from time to time of the dust and sand that gathers upon its surface. However, it is simple that this does not change the nature of the vessel; with the appropriate effort, one removes the covering that conceals and hides, and one sees the vessel in its purity.

Indeed, every single one of the children of Yisrael is a vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem, both in spirituality—meaning Torah and *mitzvos*—and also in physicality, which is necessary in terms of children, life, and ample sustenance. The cleaning, purification, and polishing of the vessel draws down and increases the light that flows into it, and spirituality and physicality will walk together, just as it is written: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My commandments, etc., I will provide your rains," and all the blessings explicitly detailed in the *parsha*.

Surely he is already aware of the three daily study portions established for every soul by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and at the very least, he should keep them from this point forward.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

And if there is no risk whatsoever in a single procedure, then surely there is no room for any benefit either, as both are dependent on the intensity of the radiation, and this is simple to understand.

## 5748

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long hiatus, your letter of 25 Sivan was received. I have already written to many others that it is a pity when people only communicate regarding their affairs in connection with an undesirable event. It seems that if Above they wish to bring about a correspondence that ultimately leads to the drawing together of hearts, there appears to be no other natural way than through an undesirable event. If, however, people were careful to write when there is good news, they would not be in need of the undesirable event, the entire purpose of which is only to draw hearts together and to increase the matter of ahavas Yisroel, one for another.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and your wife, tichyeh, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the improvement of your health and for good tidings in your affairs and those of your sons and daughters, yichyu. This also applies to your work in your surroundings to strengthen and disseminate traditional Yiddishkeit, for in truth, these are interdependent. After all, the task of Yisroel is to be "one nation on earth," and in the language of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, they must extend this unity into worldly matters as well—into the material and physical affairs. Through this, the unification of the physical and spiritual parts of a person’s life on earth is accomplished, so that they form a true unity; and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

I await good news, revealed and manifest, regarding the matters you mention in your letter, and may it be His will that this happens soon.

## 5751

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 5th of Sivan, and surely by now you have received my letter responding to your previous one.

Regarding the contents of your letter—the feelings of low spirits, despondency, and so forth—this is not the path charted by the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, and the disciples of his disciples, the luminaries of Chassidus. They emphasized, time and again, the commandment of the Ribono shel Olam: "Serve Hashem with joy." I have already written this to many of anash, and I believe to you as well, that this is truly a halachic ruling, not merely a standard of Chassidus. Furthermore, it is a fundamental and primary halachic ruling, not a peripheral one; it is the ruling of the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Lulav—see his language there, that it is a "great service." When combined with his ruling in Hilchos De'os, end of chapter 3, regarding one who serves Hashem constantly and "in all your ways know Him," it is also cited in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 231. And even if, upon contemplating your own situation, you wonder what place there is for joy, the matter has already been addressed in the holy Tanya regarding the nature of the joy of the soul, its causes, and how the body and its affairs do not interfere with this; see there.

May it be Hashem's will that you bring good news regarding the above, and also that you are increasing your studies in that part of Torah called the "Tree of Life," and that life and joy are linked until they are united with one another.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 5454

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community,
R' Chaim Zusia, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 24 Sivan, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which was read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I await good news regarding the matters you wrote about, and may it be His will that this happens soon.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that merely removing a specific name is not sufficient at all, since the name of Chabad has not spread throughout the entire area, and consequently, a "vacant space" remains. It is well-known what is said in such matters—a teaching brought in the books of Chassidus and Kabbalah—that a "vacant space" comes about through *Tzimtzum*, and it is the root of *dinim*.

This is similar to the story told in a response by one of the *Nesi'im* regarding the difference between Chassidus and *Mussar*. He explained that when a thief enters a house, there are two ways to deal with it: 1) One raises a shout, which scares the thief away. However, he can return once his fear passes, or when the shouting stops, or when he becomes accustomed to it. 2) One captures the thief, or even better—subsequently brings him to *teshuvah*. The analogy is understood, as is the lesson regarding the matter at hand.

Everything has its opportune time and *eis ratzon* (time of favor) from above and below. We must also take advantage of the fact that we are approaching the days of the *Chag HaGeulah*, 12 and 13 Tammuz, for this matter as well, through explanation—for perhaps it is a matter of... [i.e., it is a delicate matter], and the wise will understand.

With blessings for good news regarding all that was mentioned, as well as for your health and that of each of your household members, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5150

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn

Mr. Shlomo, may he live,

Shalom u'Bracha,

In response to your letter dated June 18.

It is surprising that you do not write about what you are occupied with in Montevideo, nor about your *kviyus itim* in our Torah—the Torah of life, which is our life and the length of our days, and the channel and vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, the Giver of the Torah, in all that a person requires, both materially and spiritually. I am certain you will fill this in at the next opportunity.

Regarding your question as to the reason why it is not advisable to name the group in Montevideo "Shuva Yisrael":

The reason is that there is no matter in the world, and no organization in the world, that does not have some deficiency or shortcoming. In other words, there is no perfection except for the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is, in the language of the holy Zohar, the "perfection of all."

Since there is some deficiency in everything, it is possible—and we see this tangibly—that there are people who do not wish to draw near to a certain thing because of the deficiency within it, even if the other aspects are upright in their eyes. Therefore, when forming a new organization in a new place, where it is necessary that the largest possible number of *Bnei Yisrael* join, it is better to give this organization a new name, rather than an old name associated with any existing organization—even one like "Shuva Yisrael," whose purpose is Torah and *mitzvos*. This is so that even those who have some criticism of "Shuva Yisrael," whether justly or unjustly, will not be hindered from joining the new organization. It is understood that this is different if the intention were to open a branch or a chapter, in which case one should name the branch after the center; however, this is not the case for a new group as described above.

I am sure you are aware of the *takanah* to recite the monthly *Tehillim*—as it is divided for the days of the month—every day after the morning *davening*. It is also proper that every weekday, before the morning *davening*, you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*, *b'li neder*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5757

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

## 5758

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Sivan, in which you propose questions for which you have not yet found a clear solution, namely:

1) There are times when you have a desire to learn, and times when the opposite is true, etc., at which point you turn to other matters. How can one achieve constant vigor?

The advice given for this is well known: "Habit becomes second nature." The instruction is that a person’s ascent from level to level must be step by step, not by jumping from one extreme to the other. This ascent is achieved specifically through *yegiah* (exertion), for "If one says, 'I have exerted myself and not found,' do not believe him." The contemplation of how to nullify the enticements of the *yetzer hara* is explained sufficiently in *Tanya*, as indicated in the index there.

2) How is it possible to remember *chiddushei Torah*?

In general, not all people are equal in this, as it depends on talents and faculties; our Sages of blessed memory said, "Their minds are not alike, and their faces are not alike." Generally, the instruction for this is to study the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, where there is instruction on how even one who is naturally forgetful can gather Torah, progressing and adding more.

3) What is the concept of *kavanah* in *tefillah*?

The general *kavanah* is "Know before Whom you are standing," which is divided into three contemplations: who is the one standing, before Whom he is standing, and the connection between them through *tefillah*. Then there are the specific *kavanos*, which are divided according to the parts of the *tefillah*, the content of these sections, and the meaning of the words.

4) Through which *mussar* book can one reach the level that every Jew is required to reach?

In order to reach that level, a book alone is not enough; one must work at it until the point of *yegiah*. Then, the study of the book will be successful and achieve its effect. You should set a *shiur* in the study of *Tanya* and *maamarim* of Chassidus in general; when you study with *iyun* (depth) and the appropriate attention, your eyes will be enlightened.

In general, move away from questions and difficulties; study with *hasmadah* (diligence) and *shekidah* (assiduity), and then the promise of our Sages of blessed memory will be fulfilled: "You have exerted yourself and found."

I trust you keep the practice of reciting the monthly *Tehillim* *shiur*—as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month—and in any case, you should keep to this from now on.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

This matter should be engraved in your memory by studying it multiple times, so that you will easily recall the concept and its details. This will also influence your actual conduct, for obviously, Hashgacha Pratis precludes anger and even the state of becoming agitated [except in matters of fear of Heaven, as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh]. This is neither hidden nor far away, for the matter is sufficiently understood. Furthermore, with a little contemplation, one sees how this is a direct result of the simple faith that "there is no place void of Him."

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings.

**R' Yehoshua:** Levi, Jerusalem. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 8, 2890; below, 5758.

## 5162

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Yisroel [Gordon]
Shlita,

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan and the attachment included with it.

May it be the will of Hashem that the beginning of the day camp be in a good and auspicious hour, both materially and spiritually. May the vacation days—even according to the laws of the state, which mandate secular studies—be utilized to instill in all those who attend the day camp, and through them in their families, a spirit of purity and a spirit of yirah, ahavas Hashem, ahavas HaTorah, and ahavas Yisroel.

As it is written in the name of Yisroel: "For you have struggled with Elokim"—which has the same gematria as *hateva* (nature)—"and with men"—meaning that one should not be ashamed before those who mock (as in the beginning of all sections of the Tur and Shulchan Aruch)—"and you have prevailed." And as it is written, "And you shall choose life." It is explained in the teachings of Chassidus that this is both a command and a promise: we are promised that if we only decide to choose life, we will succeed in it. The Nesi'im of the teachings of Chassidus added light and vitality to this, teaching that the success will be with joy and a glad heart, and not only for the neshamah, but—as in "you shall surely help him"—also for the body.

Certainly, the reward for those who occupy themselves and strive in this will also be drawn down openly, in the things they need: children, life, and abundant sustenance.

With blessings for good tidings in all general and personal matters.

P.S.
Surely you are receiving from Tzeirei Agudas Chabad here the points from the farbrengen.

#### ***5162***

**R' Yisroel Shlita:** Gordon, Worcester.

## 5604

May you continue your holy work with joy and a glad heart, focusing on the purity of the daughters of Israel, which leads to holiness and, subsequently, to Chassidus, as stated by our Sages at the end of Maseches Sotah.

With the blessing that each of us will bring only good news to one another.

## 5065

5065

*[Sivan 5717]*

The mitzvah of milah of Avraham Avinu was also in the physical realm. Furthermore, this is a primary intent of the mitzvah, as is written in the maamar beginning *Hinei Avram* (Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Lech Lecha), at the end of the section, and in Likkutei Torah in three places explaining this (86c).

#### ***5065***

**The mitzvah of milah of Avraham Avinu:** Whether it is similar to the fulfillment of mitzvos by the Avos, which is explained as being only in the spiritual realm, or to the fulfillment of mitzvos after Matan Torah, which are also in the physical realm.

## 5766

[Sivan 5717]

Regarding what you wrote—that the spreading of your wellsprings (*u’faratzta*) refers to all schools of Chassidus and not only Chabad—the truth is that broad conceptual understanding (*hasbarah*) and intellectual grasp of Chassidic concepts is the specific path of Chassidus Chabad, and not that of Poland. Those whose way it is to study Torah through *hasbarah* specifically, and not merely to review (*l’migras*), it is understood that this must be the case in Chassidus as well. See also *HaTamim*, Vol. 2, p. 56 and onwards.

Regarding what you wrote—that someone wishes to offer an opinion as to whether Chassidus is Kabbalah, and whether the generation is capable of receiving it—it is simple that in this matter (as in other matters), only one who is an expert in this field (in Chassidus), having engaged in it for several years with consistency, etc., can render a decision. If not, it is not his concern at all to offer an opinion on this. This is *kal v’chomer* from what the Rosh writes in *Bava Kamma*, Chapter 4, Section 6 (where he speaks of one who is more accustomed and more precise, etc.—let alone those for whom this is not their study at all. *V’kal l’havin* and it is simple). See *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*.

#### ***5766***

The letter is to Moreinu HaRav Yonah Eidelkopf, and was written on the margin of his letter from Sunday, Parshas Naso. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 14, 5034, and where noted in the footnotes there.

5717

By the Grace of G-d
1st of the week of Parshas Hen Am Lvadad Yishkon, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the annual convention of the Rabbinical Association,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your notification regarding your annual convention taking place on the second, third, and fourth days of this coming week.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that your convention be for the sake of Heaven, and that it bring forth fruits and tangible results in strengthening traditional Judaism and disseminating it within the holy communities and holy institutions where the members of the Association serve in holiness, and in every place that your influence reaches.

The dissemination of traditional Judaism must reach the point where it becomes the absolute and governing force in the life and affairs of the community, as well as in the life and affairs of the individual.

For the role of the Rabbis of our day is not the same as the role of the Rabbis of the past.

In these days of ours—days of concealment and hiding, and of alarming confusion of mind—it is the duty of the Rabbi to declare, and to declare again, that "this Torah is transmitted from the Creator, blessed be He, and from no other; nothing may be added to it and nothing may be subtracted from it, neither in the Written Torah nor in the Oral Torah."

—For the essence of the Oral Torah consists of the judges of Israel, the "pillars of instruction," and the "ordinances, decrees, and customs" which they have taught to the masses*—

**And this is one of the foundations** of our religion.

What the Torah forbade in generations past is forbidden now as well, including in the United States, and even if someone were to invent one hundred and fifty reasons to declare something pure (see Eruvin 13b)—the prohibition remains in full force.

The necessity of fulfilling this role has grown even greater in recent years, as, in His compassion for His people Israel, a powerful awakening has entered the hearts of many of the younger generation to seek the truth in its absolute form.

Some of them have already grasped the truth—that it is our Torah, the Torah of truth—to the extent that they have changed their lifestyle in actual practice in their day-to-day lives. Others are moving in this direction but have not yet reached their destination. And others still feel within themselves that they are in a void, without any support or foundation in life upon which they can stand firmly—and they are waiting and hoping that someone will come to explain to them what is happening to them and set them on a path of light.

The common denominator among all three of these types is that their eyes are turned toward the Rabbi and their leader to instruct them and teach them the truth as it is—a complete and perfect Torah, without compromises, for every compromise is founded upon falsehood and is false in its essence.

This awakening and this anticipation increase many times over the responsibility and duty of every Rabbi, and especially that of the young Rabbi who grew up in the same environment in which those who have awakened to the truth were raised and educated.

It is his duty and his privilege to inform them of a true and complete Judaism without compromises. As the Shulchan Aruch instructs at its very beginning—one should not be ashamed before those who mock. And one should not be afraid of the well-known argument that "the entire congregation is holy," and that one should not divide or create partitions between one movement in religion and another.

This is true even though the other movement makes changes to the Torah, and its status has been ruled to be not a movement within the religion, but a movement fighting against the religion of Moshe and Israel, increasing heresy among the Jewish people.

This is the opportune time, and the call of the hour, to strengthen the foundations of Torah and mitzvos in purity and holiness, for the power of teshuvah and the awakening prevailing in the camp of the Children of Israel is great. Heaven forbid that we should ignore those who are returning, or put them off with "go and come back tomorrow," or disappoint them with compromises. Every day and every week that passes—not only is this a failure to rectify, but it causes destruction and ruin. For from the conduct of the Rabbi, the members of the community and the laypeople in general learn about the value of Torah and mitzvos and the importance that the Rabbi must place upon them as their standard-bearer. It makes no difference in this matter what the reason for the Rabbi’s silence is—whether it is out of fear that he might lose his livelihood, or his honor, or the number of people who frequent his door—for in any case, his silence is interpreted as an admission to the opposing side and its ideology: the lowering of the Torah from its holiness and its adaptation to the conditions of the time and place.

This is an ideology that has led in the past, and leads even now—directly, step by step—to Conservatism, Reform, assimilation, and total disappearance, G-d forbid.

The essence and authority of every Rabbi is that he is a shaliach to transmit the da'as Torah, the mission of the pillars of the Torah, from the earliest generations, man from man, back to Moshe Rabbeinu who received the Torah from Sinai—a shaliach of the Makom.

A faithful shaliach who does not alter his mission possesses the power and authority of the One who sent him; as our Sages say, "a person's shaliach is like himself." And this is true on a higher level of holiness, up to, as it were, the "Supernal Man upon the Throne,"** who says to every true student: "And I have put My words in your mouth."

A shaliach who alters his mission acts by his own will and his own power—the will and power of flesh and blood, fashioned from matter, of whom it is said, "and the superiority of man over the beast is naught."

And if he calls himself a Rabbi and a shepherd of a congregation and group in Israel, how will he answer to the word of Hashem through His prophet:

"You eat the fat and you clothe yourselves with the wool... but the sick you have not healed, and the broken you have not bound, and the strayed you have not brought back, and the lost you have not sought... and they became food for every beast of the field" (Yechezkel 34:3-5).

May it be the will of Hashem that your convention will be successful in awakening, strengthening, and encouraging the members of the Association and all Rabbis, so that despite the pressure from without and the pressure from within, they will fulfill the aforementioned role of the Rabbi in its entirety, without perversion of justice and without delay of justice.

And through the mission and power of the Torah and the Giver of the Torah—who alone rules and leads the entire world—may you establish holy communities in Israel and lead them on the path that ascends to the House of G-d, with abundance in all things.

Until the prophecy is fulfilled: "And I will set up one shepherd over them, and he shall feed them, My servant David."

With respect and with a blessing for success in the holy work of strengthening the Torah of truth—the truth of Hashem is forever—and disseminating it.

**M. Schneerson**

## 5768

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Sivan, in which you write that you ask yourself from time to time whether the fact that all of this comes about [in a certain way] detracts from the value of the matters, etc.

The instruction of our Sages is already well-known: "A person should always engage in Torah and mitzvos, even if not for their own sake, for from [doing them] not for their own sake, one comes to do them for their own sake." If this is true regarding general matters, how much more so when a person has already contemplated this issue and is reflecting upon it, and the matter touches him (*es rirt im on*). This itself brings the matter closer to being performed for its own sake, even if you were to argue that from the outset there was a mixture of some secondary motive—especially since it is possible that this is merely a doubt.

The main point regarding the future is the teaching of the Mishnah: "The deed is the essential thing," and in the language of the holy Zohar, "Action is above." While reflection on this and *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-searching) are generally necessary, the parable of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well-known: A merchant who stops his business every single hour to calculate his accounts from the past, comparing income and expenses, etc., will not only fail to benefit his business, but on the contrary, will cause it harm. As it is said, "For everything there is a season."

When you become friendly and draw closer, with an internal closeness, to the *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* and the *Temimim* in your vicinity—with a firm resolution to remove and nullify the barriers that stem from a different upbringing in childhood and the like—this indirect closeness, in addition to the direct guidance you will receive from them from time to time, will steer your path and conduct in the desired direction. That is to say, toward a Chassidic way of life in your day-to-day living, and not only on Shabbos, Yomim Tovim, and exceptional occasions. From time to time, the matter will become easier for you, until, if you truly desire it, the adage will be fulfilled: "Habit becomes second nature."

It is difficult to advise on what follows from such a great distance, but in general, we see in human nature that a total change, visible to all, facilitates internal changes and adaptation to a new environment. As the expression in Yiddish goes, *farbrennen hinter zich di briken* (burning the bridges behind one). It is possible that in your situation, this will constitute the matter of "the greatness of the elder" (*gadol hazaken*). See also the *Reshimot* of the Tzemach Tzedek printed in the supplements to his commentary on Tehillim, where "the greatness of the elder" in its completeness draws down the blessings of Hashem from above, without taking into account judgments and accusations. And who in our days can afford to forgo these great mercies, and is not in need of them?

You will surely participate in the *farbrengens* of the days of the *Chag HaGeulah*, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which are approaching. This year marks the thirty-year period since the first *Geulah*.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 5768*

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, whose work is work for the sake of Heaven,
Rabbi Dober, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday, in which you write regarding the great responsibility placed upon the heads of yeshivos concerning the difficulties in arranging suitable lives for yeshivah students, and you describe the difficulties involved in obtaining a teaching position, as well as regarding the position of the rabbinate, where everyone does whatever they see fit.

Regarding the difficulties in obtaining a teaching position, the situation has improved in recent years. In any case, this is not a question for the yeshivos alone, but a question of the general state of the Jewish street in matters of Yiddishkeit. It is surprising that you do not raise this at the meetings of the Chareidi organizations that deal with such matters—meetings of rabbis, meetings of Chareidi parties, and the like. Even though there is a great distance between the resolutions of such meetings and their implementation in practice, there is still benefit in the discussion itself, as it awakens public opinion. At the very least, in some places, the situation improves; and surely, for the sake of even one Jewish soul, the effort and trouble are worthwhile.

Regarding the point you write, that in the field of the rabbinate everyone does whatever they see fit: you should have spoken with several of the younger rabbis who also feel this painful point. However, each one complains in his own corner, and it is difficult in the United States to make an individual opinion heard. This is not the case if they were to organize together and voice their protest, which **without a doubt** would make an impression and lead to a shift in the matter.

With blessings for a good arrangement in both material and spiritual matters, and for avodah specifically from a place of joy. After all, avodas Hashem is for all twenty-four hours of the day (as it must be: "**In all** your ways know Him," as per the ruling of the Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 231).

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### ***5768\****

**Rabbi Dober:** Gansky, Monticello.

## 5160

By the Grace of G-d
2 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of the 28th of Sivan, in which you write that preparations are being made for action, etc.

Surely you are continuing, and will continue, with the appropriate efforts—all those who have it in their power to do something to negate this alarming matter. We do not know what or when the opportune moment for such actions might be, and surely for someone like yourself, encouragement in this is superfluous. I write this only based on the dictum of our Sages: "One does not urge the diligent, but it is necessary for the sake of adding [to their efforts]."

There is another point here regarding the verse, "Your destroyers and those who lay you waste shall go forth from you" (Yeshayahu 49:17). In its most subtle sense, this means that when those who tremble at the word of Hashem show weakness in any matter of religion—even if it be as thin as a needle—it provides a foothold for the "other side" to launch an offensive on many fronts. This is not merely a spiritual concept; it is understood in the natural order as well. Furthermore, many of the secularists say this explicitly: since you have conceded on such-and-such a matter, why the uproar regarding a second matter? And sometimes, they even use it to their advantage.

My intention here is specifically regarding the matter of the Israeli ships that travel even on the holy Shabbos. Alas, many who fear G-d are stumbling in this because they silence, whether maliciously or inadvertently, the absolute prohibition of the matter. Moreover, there are those who clothe this capital offense—G-d forbid—in the guise of a mitzvah, claiming it is a matter of saving lives, etc. Great is the darkness of the galus, where even arguments that are laughable and absurd are seized upon and relied upon if they happen to suit the desires of the one applying the pressure.

A second point is the current situation regarding the issue of separation in schools between boys and girls, the lack of which, alas, has caused many to fall until now. When I have raised this—and with bitterness—I have been answered as if it were a matter of idle talk, [claiming] that there are many rabbis and Torah giants in the Holy Land—may it be built and established—and if the situation were as I write about it, they surely would not be sitting with their hands folded.

It is clear that regarding these two points, if there were an effort made, there would certainly be some improvement. And he who saves one soul of Israel is as if he has sustained an entire world—all the more so when it involves hundreds and thousands.

And a third point, which seemingly is more difficult to rectify, is the matter of women in the army. Based on what I discussed with... in our conversation, I find it a great wonder that they have not spoken about the primary issue: the prohibition for men in this mixed environment. Instead, they have focused on the secondary issue—the women—regarding whom [the halachic status] is that "Esther was like the soil of the world." Furthermore, in accordance with reality, those who are not religious actually constitute more of a stumbling block than those who are religious, on the face of it. I write "seemingly difficult" regarding this point because it is possible to take action based on the latest rumors that have arrived. Even though, officially and openly, they will certainly not agree to cancel the drafting of women, unofficially—they might. For they have already realized—even the opposing side—that the matter is not worth the damage; damage by all accounts, and not only in religious areas. Even though during the winter months it would have been more opportune to apply pressure and succeed in this than it is now, we do not cry over the past. If only the G-d-fearing would at least now utilize the possibility and the ability that is in their hands. The effort itself is also a mitzvah, especially since there are good prospects that they will succeed in this to a certain degree in all three points. When taking into account the value of these matters, every effort and exertion is worthwhile.

With respect and blessings,
Looking forward to hearing good news.

***

5160

Israeli ships: See also above, letter 5134, and the references in the notes there.

The matter of separation: See also above, Vol. 14, letter 4812.

## 1715

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, R' Nachum Shemaryahu, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 26th of Sivan, and many thanks for the good news and the report regarding the repeating of *maamarim* of *Chassidus* in the synagogues.

Regarding what you wrote—that you spoke with the esteemed Chossid R' M. Weber, may he live, so that he would prepare capable students from *Tomchei Temimim* for the aforementioned task—it is surprising that you write that it has not yet been put into practice. Although the discussion was generally that all students from the upper classes of *Tomchei Temimim* should repeat *Chassidus* every Shabbos, it is understood that it is not absolutely necessary for this to take place in the Yeshiva building. On the contrary, they should be accustomed to the "awe of the congregation," for which repeating in a synagogue or similar setting is suitable. Surely you will speak with the aforementioned person once again regarding this matter and find persuasive words until the matter is put into practice.

Regarding what you wrote about [Name], may he live, that it is very difficult to find a match for him: surely it is no more difficult than the splitting of the Red Sea. Our Sages of blessed memory said this regarding every *shidduch*, and at the same time, they commanded us regarding the matter. The commandment of the Torah is also a bestowal of strength, as is discussed in many places in *Chassidus*—that the language of the commandments is also the language of a promise.

Surely you are preparing a suitable program for the celebration of the *Chag HaGeulah*, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which is approaching, especially since this year marks the thirty-year period since the day of the *Geulah* for the first time.

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah* and for good tidings.

## 5761

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, involved in communal needs,
R' Menachem Zev, may he live, Halevi

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 26th of Sivan, and surely the response to your previous letters has arrived by now...

Regarding what you wrote concerning comments on the students' papers—it seems you do not envision that this requires detaching oneself from the matters one is currently engaged in and focusing on this specific task, and after arranging the comments—detaching from this matter and re-engaging with the matters at hand. It appears from your letter that you think if a comment is one line long, it only requires the time it takes to read that line, plus at most a moment before and a moment after.

Now, if there were a standard procedure where such matters required comments from me, then a necessary task would certainly have its time. But I hope that even for someone like you, there is no need to elaborate and explain that this is a matter for the Yeshiva administration where the students are studying. On the contrary—even if it were necessary for me to contemplate and comment on various details, the comment should still come in the name of, or through, the administration to the student, for that is the established order in educational institutions. Especially when there is doubt in the matter, and particularly when dealing with students who are Chassidim by nature, but who, due to the *yetzer lev ha'adam*, require extra effort or a specific type of effort.

It is understood that the above does not mean I will never write comments, etc.; I only wish to emphasize—even though it is simple—that this is not the way of chinuch, even in Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim. I have never heard that this was the procedure in years past. And if there is an appropriate time and a necessity for it, we shall see in the future...

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***5761***

**R' Menachem Zev, may he live:** Gringlas, Montreal. Additional letters to him—above 575, and in the references noted there.

## 5762

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Sivan, in which you write regarding your future brother-in-law and what he said to you concerning the study of Chassidus and its related matters—that he conducts these things in private, etc.

Now, although in previous generations this conduct was a relevant consideration—especially so that one would not appear to be acting with arrogance—in our current era we see tangibly that while it is obvious that one should not be ostentatious or the like, nevertheless, when one conducts oneself openly in these matters, it strengthens and binds the individual more firmly to these concepts. Knowing that it is already public knowledge that he belongs to this circle and follows these practices, it is not becoming to suddenly and abruptly backtrack, etc. And since a person must strive with every possible justification to avoid being brought into a state of trial, or at the very least to minimize them as much as possible, then conducting oneself openly in a Chassidic manner is one of the means to weaken the trial. And this is easy to understand.

It is my hope that each of them, and all of them together, will utilize the upcoming days of the Chag HaGeulah, 12 and 13 Tammuz, as much as possible—for the strengthening of Torah study and the fulfillment of mitzvos in general, and for the spreading of the wellsprings (hafotzas hamaayanos) in particular.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

At an opportune time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to their needs. May it be His will that you bring good tidings in this.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

#### ***5762***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 20, p. 590.

## 5173

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and pious leader of his community, who sits in judgment and guides his flock with integrity, Moreinu HaRav Yehuda, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of the twentieth of the month of the giving of our Torah reached me. At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to their specific needs as described in your letter.

These days are indeed auspicious for the arousal of great Divine mercy through my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of Israel. As with every faithful shepherd, his leadership remains constant: just as he stood and served [his flock] during his lifetime in this world, so too, from on high, he continues to serve by arousing great mercy regarding everything that concerns those who are connected and bound to him, and to the entirety of the Jewish people. This connection is relevant to one who walks the straight path that he taught us, following in his ways—as per the language of our Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 27.

Since the days of his redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—from the imprisonment where he was held for his mesiras nefesh in spreading Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos—are approaching, we recall the interpretation of the Arizal on the verse, "And these days are remembered [when they are recalled with the appropriate arousal, the previous influences and bestowals are drawn down] and performed." Just as they witnessed open miracles then, transcending the natural order, so too is it now. It is an opportune time and a period of spiritual favor for the fulfillment of the requests of those who are connected and bound to him regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos, and in all matters that assist in this, which are included in the three categories of "children, life, and abundant sustenance." If this is true for any person, it is certainly true regarding a Rabbi who leads a community in Israel, as the expansion of his own affairs will surely bring about the expansion of all matters of Yiddishkeit within his holy congregation.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

***

## 515

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Sivan, in which you write regarding the rationale for being here during the upcoming days of Tishrei.

My opinion on this matter is already known, namely, that there are several conditions for this:

1) It is understood that this must be with the full consent of your wife, may she live and be well. 2) That it should not place pressure on expenditures for necessary household matters. 3) Consultation with the administration of the affairs in which you serve in holiness, such that the trip will not cause any damage, Heaven forbid, to those affairs. 4) This trip must also be for the *to'eles harabim* (benefit of the many); that is to say, that upon your return, the trip and its results will be felt in your environment through the dissemination of the study of Chassidus and the following of its guidance and customs. Only if all the aforementioned conditions are present should you take an interest in the trip.

I trust you are keeping the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the well-known *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5106

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Tammuz, in which you write about the changes that have taken place in your class, and that for several reasons these changes do not seem right to you, and that you have consulted with some of those in the yeshivah and the administration who also share your opinion, and you ask what you should do.

It is understood and simple that all matters of the yeshivah must be conducted according to the instructions of the administration, for the existence of any institution depends on obedience to its administration. However, regarding the above, you should explain your reasons to the administration—and surely you have already done so—and you may also ask those with whom you consulted to speak with the administration as well. But all of this is by way of offering suggestions; regarding the actual implementation, obedience is mandatory, and as mentioned, this is a fundamental matter.

The response to your previous letter has surely been received by now.

With blessings for success and good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Monday and the days following, in which you ask whether you, too, should connect with the vegetarian institute.

This is the correct thing to do, especially since you write that you have already spoken with them and it is evident that their method is suitable for your needs...

Regarding what you wrote about the *kvi'us itim* (fixed times) for Torah study before going to sleep, and how this impacts your preparation for the lessons you teach in your class: the ruling on this is already well-known—see *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by our Rebbe HaZaken, end of Chapter 1. However, you must certainly ensure that you maintain the aforementioned *kvi'us* without it compromising your preparation for the class, by scheduling the *kvi'us* earlier, or similar methods.

Regarding what you wrote about putting on *tefillin* on *Chol HaMoed*—your doubt is puzzling. For those who hold that it is forbidden, one of the reasons given is the alarming statements regarding this in the *Zohar* and *Kabbalah*. From there, it is also understood that not reciting a *bracha* over them does not rectify the matter. At the very most, what one can do is daven in a place other than the aforementioned *minyan*, or daven in private (and surely there are several *minyanim* in your location), and then there is no room for the difficulty.

You should certainly utilize the upcoming days of *Chag HaGeulah*, 12 and 13 Tammuz, for matters related to the "master of the miracle and the joy." May Hashem grant you success and bring you good news regarding all the above, and regarding your health and the health of your wife, *tichyeh*.

With blessings,

## 519

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long hiatus, I received your letter from the 27th of Sivan. Regarding your questions:

1) Whether one recites a blessing upon a lunar or solar eclipse.

It is a known rule that one should not innovate a blessing that was not mentioned in the Gemara (Beis Yosef, Orach Chaim 446). One could say the reason we do not recite a blessing over this is because it is a sign of **impending** calamity (Sukkah 29a). On the contrary, it requires prayer to annul it, and an outcry, not a blessing.

2) Whether Chazal knew about the matter of these eclipses and whether it is a natural phenomenon.

The phenomenon of eclipses is mentioned in several places in the words of Chazal, and it is surprising that there is even a doubt about this. It is well known that even the sages of Egypt, and before them in Babylon, had already compiled tables of the aforementioned eclipses. This is known from historical records and is also mentioned—lehavdil—in the Holy Scriptures, that the Children of Israel were in contact with the sages of Egypt and Babylon.

From the compilation of these tables, it is understood that the phenomenon in question is a natural matter. However, at the same time, it also serves as a sign, similar to the matter of the rainbow—which is also a natural phenomenon now, yet simultaneously serves as a sign, as written at length. There is no contradiction here. For when do we say that a solar or lunar eclipse carries the interpretations of Chazal (Sukkah 29a)? When the eclipses are visible on earth (and are visible to one who knows how to interpret the eclipses). This is not the case if the heavens are covered by clouds or the like; then it is not a matter of a sign or instruction for the person upon the earth. The same applies to the matter of the rainbow, as explained in the commentaries on the Torah.

3) What is the difference between those who follow the guidance of Chassidus and those who have not grasped it; is there a difference in their worldview?

It is understood that this is indeed the case, and it is visible to the naked eye. It would take too long to explain in a letter, especially since these matters are explained in several books that elucidate the teachings of Chassidus and its concepts. See also the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

4) Regarding your question about creating abridgments of the Tanya: surely you can find them at the beginning of the book *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya* by the Tzemach Tzedek. It is understood that this does not preclude you from making your own notes and abridgments for yourself, so that it will be easier for you to commit the concepts brought in the Tanya to memory and to review them when the opportunity arises.

5) Regarding studying for yourself versus doing what you can to spread Yiddishkeit.

I believe I have already written to you that there is no contradiction between the two. On the contrary, in order to influence others, one must also study for himself. However, the division of time between the two types of study—and in general, the two types of engagement, for oneself and with others—is not the same for everyone. Since a person is close to himself and biased, he needs to consult with another who can judge the matter without bias or ulterior motives.

6) Regarding what you wrote, that the lifestyle in a kibbutz and the order of things is not suitable for activities to strengthen Yiddishkeit, etc.

As mentioned above, this depends on the temperament of each individual. For in and of itself, there is no contradiction between the lifestyle of a kibbutz (provided it is based on Torah and mitzvos) and fulfilling the role of a Jewish person in his world, as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Creator."

It is my hope, even though you do not mention it explicitly, that you are keeping the three daily study portions established for every soul by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the well-known *Chumash, Tehillim,* and *Tanya*—in addition to your fixed times for studying the revealed Torah and Chassidus.

Surely you will participate in the celebration of the *Chag HaGeulah* of the 12th and 13th of Tammuz, especially since this year marks the thirty-year period since the first *Geulah*, as discussed in the *sicha* of the Shabbos on which we bless the month of Tammuz, regarding the significance and concept of a thirty-year period.

With blessings.

## 580

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with noble character, scion of a noble lineage, etc., R' Sh. Z. [Shazar]—may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I have been informed of your efforts regarding the naming of Kfar Chabad, and that your efforts were successful. While it is superfluous to thank you for this, it is nonetheless appropriate to express my appreciation. Primarily, I wish to emphasize once again what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, several times: that because of the mesiras nefesh of Rabbeinu HaZaken, he merited that all those who engage in the affairs of Chassidus should have the upper hand. This gives me further hope that you will recognize your most sublime strengths and possibilities and utilize them to the greatest extent for the benefit of the Jewish people in general, and among them, for the benefit of the community of Chassidim and their affairs in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—in particular.

Regarding the teachings of Rabbeinu HaZaken in manuscripts that have not yet been printed, the work is progressing in accordance with what we discussed when you were here, and in accordance with the telegram you sent from London, that the means will surely be available by the time discussed.

Approaching the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, may they come upon us for good, I wish to express my blessing that these days should influence you with abundant good. For just as every good thing is eternal—since its source is in the Hakadosh Baruch Hu, who is was, is, and will be as one—so too, the mesiras nefesh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the holy matters of the Jewish people stands even now and resonates in the void of the world, even in this physical and material world. It diminishes the concealment and hiddenness in the world and awakens everyone who wishes to listen to this awakening and dedication—mesiras nefesh, and certainly also mesiras haguf—to the Ohr Ein Sof and the Maor, from whom no place is devoid. This is achieved through the speech and action of a person, and in the language of Rabbeinu HaZaken, "no thought can grasp Him at all, except when it grasps and clothes itself in Torah and its mitzvos" (Tanya, end of Chapter 4).

With respect, appreciation, and a blessing for a Chag HaGeulah.

## 5181

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 29 Sivan: The interpretation of some commentators on the verse, "And we were in our own sight as grasshoppers, and so we were in their sight," is already well-known. It means that only through this—that when Bnei Yisrael, who tremble at the word of Hashem and are attached to the living G-d through His Torah and mitzvos, recognize their own wisdom and capacity—through this very fact, many concealments and obstructions are nullified, and success is added to the avodah of upholding and disseminating true Yiddishkeit.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter that the sincerity of the above is evident from the style of those with whom you speak. Surely this will add strength and courage to the vital avodah of bringing Bnei Yisrael closer to Hashem, wherever they may be, to an actual and practical connection with our Torah—the Torah of truth—and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "And he shall live by them," both for the individual and for the community.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the order of studying Chassidus, it is understood that even though everyone is obligated in this, not everyone is equal in the quality and quantity of study. Since a person is close to himself and biased in his own affairs, you should consult with anash in your surroundings who know you, as is known the saying of the Mitteler Rebbe that when consulting with a friend, there are then two nefesh habahamis against one yetzer hara.

Also, in this letter you do not mention anything regarding shidduchim, yet time is passing. This mitzvah is a primary mitzvah that affects all of a person's affairs, including his matters of Torah and mitzvos. Although I have already written about this many times, due to the importance of the matter, I am writing it again and again. If only I could hear good news very soon, specifically regarding the actual deed—that in a good and auspicious hour you become a chassan, set a date for the wedding, and subsequently [I hear] good news of your wedding in a good and auspicious hour. These days of the Chag HaGeulah, 12 and 13 Tammuz—which was a manifest victory, far above the way of nature, for all matters of Torah and mitzvos—are also auspicious for the beginning of this matter.

With blessings for good news in all that was mentioned and in the other matters you write about in your letter.

## 5182

B”H, 6 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Sivan, in which you write regarding the reasons and matters that have led to a deficit, and perhaps even to a cessation of certain activities of yours, etc.

I have already written to several of anash that every individual has a unique role in the world of the Ribono shel Olam. Although the central point of every role is as the Mishnah states, "I was created to serve my Maker," to serve Hashem—just as in the literal service in the Beis Hamikdash, the tasks of the singer and the gatekeeper were distinct, and one was not to neglect his own work to perform the work of his colleague—so too is it in the avodah of all Bnei Yisrael. Even though all are responsible for one another, nevertheless, "the poor of your city and the poor of your people take precedence," and a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others takes precedence over all other matters. From this, it is understood a fortiori that Bnei Yisrael should not perform the work of the angels.

Furthermore, the calculation of the reward and punishment of others, and the searching for the reasons for their situation—whether they are justified or not—and likewise regarding oneself in a general sense, this is the work of the angels who record the merits of Yisrael. However, a person must fulfill the instruction: "We are the workers of the day," to perform avodah in actual deed, in "arise and do." Regarding the claims that a person is coerced in this and compelled to "sit and do nothing"—even if we were to say that they are correct, and that the concept of "love covers all transgressions" does not apply here at all—we do not say "it is considered as if it were done." And if so, there is a **deficiency** in his **primary** role, and this applies to your letter mentioned above.

I do not wish to elaborate further on this, as the matter is simple. And since we do not cry over the past, and primarily because you write in your letter that from here on you will continue with good activities—and there is no good other than Torah, especially when it is permeated with the light of the "Tree of Life," which contains no mixture of good and evil, but only pure good—may it be the will that you increase these activities, going from strength to strength. Through this, you will go from strength to strength in your personal matters. I look forward to hearing good news, especially since these days are auspicious, as we are approaching the days of the Chag HaGeulah, 12 and 13 Tammuz. These are days of segulah, and the days preceding and following them, when there was an open victory, a miracle above the natural order, for all matters of Torah and mitzvos.

With blessings.

#### ***5182***

**We are the workers of the day:** See also above, Letter 5071, and the references in the notes there.

## 5183

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished,
R' Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding the matter in Albany: I have requested that they be in contact with the activists there, and afterwards they will inform you of what has been done in this regard. May it be His will that there be good news, and "good" refers only to Torah—the true good, good for Heaven and good for mankind, as our Sages of blessed memory have said (Kiddushin 40a). This is especially true when it concerns the purity of the Children of Israel, in accordance with what is brought in the Likutei Torah of our Alter Rebbe in Parshas Ki Savo (36d, end).

Based on what is explained there, one can find sweetness in the statement of our Sages of blessed memory that purity leads to [the coming of] Elijah the Prophet, and [ultimately] to the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu. This is also explicitly stated in the prophecy of Ezekiel regarding the order of the Redemption: "And I will sprinkle clean water upon you" (Yechezkel 36:25), for the essence of Moshiach and his primary sign is that "he smells and judges" (Sanhedrin 93b).

I will conclude with a matter relevant to the days of the season—the days of redemption of the 12th and 13th of Tammuz, which are approaching. At that time, they witnessed open miracles, above the way of nature, showing how through mesiras nefesh all concealments and obstructions are nullified, to the extent that even the "evil angel" is forced to answer "Amen." Furthermore, he fulfilled his obligation through mesiras nefesh with strength, and for long days and years, they continue with that same avodah for which they were prepared to sacrifice themselves. This is also a clear directive for our current period of double and redoubled darkness: that the intensity of the will to fulfill the Creator’s will nullifies concealments and obstructions. With joy and a good heart, it is possible to fulfill the command to "increase in holiness" and to go from strength to strength with the vitality and light that is drawn down through all of this—by means of the pnimiyus haTorah, which in our generation was revealed by the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, and his disciples' disciples, in their teachings—the Torah of Chassidus. This is what Moshiach Malka promised: that when the wellsprings are spread outward, he will come and redeem us, as explained in the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

## 5180

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following a long hiatus, I received your letter of 5 Tammuz along with the enclosure. Regarding what you write as the reason for the delay—that you felt you could not report [positive] accomplishments, etc.—it is understood that this only increases the bewilderment, for it is well known that the command of our holy Torah is that "each and every day performs its own work," as it is written, "Days were fashioned, and not one of them [is lacking]," which means that every day must be filled with the content of Torah and mitzvos unique to that day.

May it be His will that, at the very least, from here on out, things will be in accordance with the above. This is especially true given that it is known that the very fact that the Torah commands something is also a bestowal of strength and a promise that, in the end, it will be so. As explained in the sefarim, this is also the reason why all the mitzvos in the Torah are also phrased as a promise. For example, "And you shall love [Hashem your G-d]"—where love is the root of all 248 positive mitzvos, from which also comes the mitzvah of fear, which is the root of the 365 negative mitzvos—is both a command and a promise: "You will eventually come to love."

Regarding what you wrote about the tendons in your wife’s (tichye) legs—it is surprising that you do not mention whether the doctor instructed her to wear rubber stockings, and also that she should frequently interrupt her walking or standing and lie down to rest for a few moments.

May Hashem fulfill the days of your wife’s (tichye) pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time, properly and easily.

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah—in which you will surely participate in the farbrengen—and for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned.

## 5187

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Mr. Avraham, may he live,

Shalom u'Bracha!

1) Several girls from your housing development are requesting a place to daven, as their shul does not have an ezras nashim.

It is understood that they are justified in this request, especially in our times, when an ezras nashim in the shul or in close proximity to it will strengthen them to walk in the ways of Yiddishkeit, to keep His mitzvos, and to establish homes in Yisroel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. The necessity of this is understood, and surely a suitable place can be found without excessive expenses, for in an ezras nashim there is no need for the construction of an Aron Kodesh, a bimah, etc.; it only needs to be a place where they can gather and daven together. It would be best if they were also taught the halachos relevant to them. If this is not possible otherwise, at least in the beginning, they could gather **after** the men’s davening time in the shul that currently exists...

You surely know of the three daily shiurim for every person, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, which are well-known. In any case, you should ensure they are kept from now on.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5789

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Tammuz.

May it be the will of Hashem that from here on you know no more sorrow or distress, and may you only share good news, in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the method of your work for the establishment and development [of the Yeshiva]... it is understood that from here it is difficult to enter into the details and the minutiae, which depend on the local situation. However, since a person is closest to himself and is personally involved, you should present your matter to three of the anash in your location. May it be the will of Hashem that He grant them the correct idea to advise you. If only the anash were already present and standing upon the truth that the Yeshiva does much more for them than they do for the Yeshiva. Just as they exert themselves and toil and go beyond their limitations in matters of physical livelihood, if they would do the same—or at least to some extent—regarding their efforts for the Yeshiva, it would surely result in good, both visibly and revealed, even in their own physical affairs.

These days are especially auspicious for making resolutions regarding all of the above, with the intent of bringing these resolutions into action, for we are approaching the days of 12 and 13 Tammuz. This is especially true as this year marks the thirty-year period since the day of the Geulah for the first time, as was also discussed at the farbrengen of the beginning of the month of Tammuz regarding the virtue of the thirty years.

With blessings.

## 590

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter received at the end of Sivan, in which you express surprise at what was hinted in my letter regarding a doctor.

It is surprising that you are surprised, for in addition to the general teaching of our Sages that "the Rabbis are ill" (Nedarim 49b), your being here has evidently involved the strain of travel, a lack of regular schedule in eating and sleeping, etc., which certainly did not contribute to your health. That is why I hinted and wrote as I did, and I hope that you have done so, or that you will do so at least now.

Regarding what you wrote about traveling here: based on the above, my perspective is that it is not advisable, at least for the time being. Especially since the success of the aforementioned [medical] treatment is almost certain, and particularly given that the summer days—and the end of summer—are more difficult than the summer itself. The benefit that would come from your arrival here, in addition to what your brothers and friends will surely do on your behalf, is doubtful. The One who sustains and provides for all with grace, kindness, and mercy can certainly provide for you in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established, especially if you also create a vessel through natural means via your brothers and friends here. Why leave the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, and the Holy Land, may it be established, to expend energy on a doubt? May it be His will that you bring good news that is visibly and revealedly good, consistent with all the above, and that you celebrate the days of the Festival of Redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz, among anash with joy and a glad heart, and at the core point: spreading the wellsprings outward as much as possible and as much as is required.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 591

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos, and I will, of course, fulfill your request to mention you at the holy resting place of the Baal HaSimcha, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that his merit not only protects us from above, but also stirs us from within—in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and specifically regarding the central point: the dissemination of the wellsprings outward. Since this is the demand and the necessity of the hour, surely everyone is capable of accomplishing this, especially those who merited to see him. This is all the more so, and a fortiori, based on the words of our Sages regarding the effect of seeing [the staff of Rabbi Meir and the basket of Rabbi Meir]. This is especially true given that this year marks the thirty-year period since the day of the Geulah for the first time, as was also discussed at the farbrengen of 12-13 Tammuz regarding the significance of thirty. I am enclosing a short reshimah.

**M. Schneerson**

## 590

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is both surprising and distressing that, in addition to the fact that no reports are received from him regarding the affairs of the Yeshiva in general—and not even regarding the Chassidus matters within the Yeshiva, which is his primary, essential, and internal responsibility—in all the reports received concerning Chassidus matters and farbrengens in the Yeshiva of... (where, naturally, they mention who farbrenged, when so-and-so farbrenged, etc., and especially during these days, which are days of the festival, etc.), not one of them mentions his name.

Even if we were to assume that he teaches the Chassidus shiur at certain times in a manner that is, according to everyone, sufficient and nothing more, we see tangibly that for a student to absorb the study of Chassidus, there must be the "moisture" of the matters surrounding Chassidus. If the student does not receive this from the one teaching the shiur, or receives it only on very rare and distant occasions, this significantly and substantially weakens the absorption of the studies as well. It is understood that it is distressing that one must stir up such a matter from across the sea, at a time when there is a Yeshiva administration on-site. Furthermore, it is the **responsibility** of the one teaching the Chassidus shiur to **awaken** the members of the administration to the necessity of vitality and light in all the Yeshiva’s studies—even in the study of Nigleh, and certainly in the study of Chassidus, whose purpose is to enliven the Jewish person. It should not be the case that the teacher of Chassidus must be prodded by outsiders to do so for the students. It is also understood that it is distressing that the students themselves do not demand this from the one teaching them Chassidus. But in the natural course of things, the fault for this also lies with the teacher, for they were surely not educated in this direction, in line with the words of our Sages on the verse, "And their guilt shall be upon your heads." If this is true regarding the study of Nigleh, how much more so regarding matters of Chassidus. It is difficult to elaborate on a matter so distressing that it is alarming.

May it be the will of Hashem that, finally, the principle of our Sages—cited in Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Chapter 9—will be fulfilled: that regarding a matter requiring correction, if until now one page or one chapter was sufficient, from here on, two pages or two chapters are required, etc. And from what is explained in other places regarding the concept of "double and twofold wisdom," and as hinted at by our Sages on this verse in Shemos Rabbah, it is understood that doubling the pages and chapters is not merely twice as much, but a change in quality in addition to the change in quantity. And this is understood.

Awaiting good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 595

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter conveying good news, for peace increases peace in the world, and all the more so among Torah scholars. Furthermore, one mitzvah leads to another, for good news is itself a mitzvah, as it brings joy to the heart of a Yid, thereby fulfilling the great principle in the Torah: "Love your fellow as yourself." The good news is that the medical treatment of your son-in-law, the Rav, shlita, was successful.

May it be Hashem’s will that from here on, you shall only hear of good, in a revealed and manifest way. Regarding health, may it be specifically in the manner of the healing of the Ribono shel Olam, as it is written, "For I am Hashem your healer," and consequently, "I will not place upon you" from the outset. It is known that this is an acronym for *Arich*. Regarding this it is said, "Your healing shall sprout forth speedily," which is better than any *shaked* (almond/diligence) of Aharon, the High Priest.

I will conclude with matters of the day, namely the upcoming 12th and 13th of Tammuz, the Chag HaGeulah of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzkllh"h, nbgm, zy"a. May we have a complete and immediate Geulah from all matters that confuse and disturb, so that we may be able to engage in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and its strengthening in general, and the strengthening of Chassidus and its dissemination in particular, in an ever-increasing measure.

With blessings.
