## 5196

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc., R' Yitzchok, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Balak. Enclosed is a copy of a letter to someone else, and naturally, the contents are intended for him as well.

With blessings for good tidings and blessings for the Chag HaGeulah, with success,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding the *pidyon nefesh* concerning the man whose father, of blessed memory, appeared to him in a dream, etc. — he should ask for his father’s forgiveness in the presence of ten men, for the fact that during the year of mourning, not everything was done as it should have been. It is a known ruling of our holy Torah that if a father forgives, etc., it is forgiven. It is also appropriate that his tefillin and mezuzos be checked in his residence.

Regarding what you wrote about how prophecy is possible for the nations of the world, when it is all the more so regarding the resting of the Shechinah, which requires one to be *batel* in their existence, etc. — you should have asked *a fortiori*: how were they commanded in the Seven Mitzvos — which implies *tzavta* (connection) — when in this, **every single one** of the nations of the world was commanded, not just select individuals?

The explanation is that at that moment, he is *batel*. And this is even more pronounced in prophecy, as it is written, "falling down," etc. See Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, Chapter 7, and Torah Or, Toldos 19c.

#### ***5196***

**R' Yitzchok:** Dubov, Manchester. Additional letters to him — see above, 5138, and the references in the notes there.

## 5197

B"H, 10 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter which begins with the adage, "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its root," in which you write the main points of your life story and your current activities, including your involvement and efforts in disseminating the study of Tanya, etc.

Now, the statement of our Sages—with which you began your letter—points clearly to the fact that there is no need for further "throwing" after the first throw; the first throw is sufficient, as it already lands on the root. This is understood in the analogy as well: one should not seek further "throws," not even "throws" of kindness and mercy. For the Ribono shel Olam did not create a single thing in His world in vain. Since it already "lands on the root," it is up to the person himself to walk in this path and in this direction that corresponds to the root. And since this is required of him, surely he has been given the strength and the ability to bring the matter into actuality. By contemplating, even for a brief moment, his root and the source from which he was hewn, he will certainly not be satisfied with his current standing and situation, and he will do everything within his power to go from level to level and from strength to strength. It is understood that in all this progress—which includes his activities in influencing others—it is as understood from the teachings of Rabbeinu HaZaken, that "Love your fellow as yourself" is a vessel for, and is one with, "Love Hashem your G-d," the primary and fundamental mitzvah between man and Hashem.

As is known, love is the root of all 248 positive mitzvos (Tanya, Chapter 4), which generally includes fear, which is the root of the 365 negative mitzvos. Thus, the general mitzvah of the love of Hashem is the foundation for all the mitzvos.

These days are auspicious for making additional resolutions regarding the above, for they are the 12th and 13th of Tammuz, the days of the redemption of our Nasi from his imprisonment for his mesiras nefesh for the dissemination of Torah and mitzvos among the Children of Israel. Each and every year, the matters of the season of the year are reawakened: the redemption from imprisonment and the nullification of the imprisonment through the power of the mesiras nefesh of the Jewish person for Torah and its mitzvos.

May it be the will of Hashem that you find appropriate words—words that explain and also illuminate—to convey the above content and disseminate it among the youth within the sphere of your influence.

With blessings for good tidings and for a successful celebration of the Chag HaGeulah.

P.S. Regarding what you ask about the method by which you drew the youth in your environment to the study of Tanya: since you have seen good fruits from this, there is no need to be concerned about matters related to melancholy, which might cause them to stumble through questions and challenges, etc. With contemplation and attention, you will surely be able to frame the questions in a way that minimizes room for concern, until it is nullified entirely. Especially since the adage is known: "The Torah was not given to the ministering angels," and "After a stumble, one stands upon the words of Torah." The matter depends only on desire, and the merit of the many will assist you.

***

**5197**

**The teachings of Rabbeinu HaZaken:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 4890, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 599

[11 Tammuz 5717]

... Regarding the matter of keeping a Sefer Torah that has not been proofread (by means of a modification—tying the sash over the mantle): There is a halachic discussion in Responsa Minchas Elazar (Vol. 3, 52) and in Zecher Yehosef (31) that permits it. Sefer Chassidim (Section 834) is not a proof, for it can be argued that torn or erased letters are different (as that is a situation where) there is no room for error. This requires further study.

## 5600

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

Mr. Yitzchak, may he live,

Shalom u’vracha!

Since your last letter, following the *Isru Chag* of the time of the giving of our Torah, I have not received any correspondence from you. I would like to hope that this is a sign that you are continuing in your *avodah* to bring the hearts of the children of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven, wherever your hand can reach. We have already been promised regarding such *avodah* that one who engages in it with sincerity will succeed—even though the *avodah* required for this is not the same for every person, in every place, and at every time, nor is the time for the sprouting and growth of the fruits of this *avodah* the same. It is human nature that when one knows in advance that the *avodah* will succeed, one performs it with greater alacrity and joy, and consequently, the success itself increases.

I have chosen to write in this vein on the eve of the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz, as you are surely familiar with the narrative of the imprisonment and the redemption. My hope is strong that the very date of this letter will awaken contemplation regarding the cause of the imprisonment itself, the redemption, and its manner—and primarily, contemplation regarding the purpose and goal for which all this knowledge has reached us. For there is nothing in the world that is in vain, and everything is by *hashgachah pratis*. May this date serve as per the adage: "A hint is sufficient for the wise," for an imprisonment is more difficult when it is at the hands of friends and acquaintances, and when it is not bound by chains of iron. Sometimes, redemption from such an imprisonment also requires *mesiras nefesh*—especially according to the explanation in *Chassidus* of the precise terminology of *mesiras nefesh*, from the phrase "my soul (*nafshi*) is not toward the people," which means my will (*retzoni*).

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and with the hope that it will be accompanied by an improvement in health following the attack you suffered, may Hashem spare us, about which you wrote at the end of your letter, and for the continuation of the matters of *Chag HaGeulah* throughout the entire year, with joy and goodness of heart.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

Regarding what you noted in one of your previous letters, that you were troubled by the matter of impure animals and the like, which are from the three completely impure *kelipos*, and why their portion is diminished such that they have no elevation, etc.

Here are a few points on this: The primary one is that every matter has its role in the world—that is, a manner of its elevation to its source, and even to its most primal source and root. Just as with pure animals this is through the act of eating and the like, with impure animals it is through refraining from eating them due to the commandment of the Torah, and likewise through using them for purposes other than eating—such as a donkey for carrying a load, etc. At that time, the *Elokus* spark that is found within them as well—as is understood and simple, for there is nothing else besides Him, and "You give life to them all"—ascends on high and unites with its root and source, through a *mitzvah* being performed with it in the two ways mentioned. See also the *Zohar HaKadosh* cited in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 29 (Zohar Vol. III, 163a), that even the one who entices receives his good reward. See also the *maamar* "Acharei Hashem" by the *Tzemach Tzedek*, printed at the end of *Derech Mitzvosecha*.

Likewise, regarding what you wrote about the matter of *bechirah* (choice): True *bechirah*, which is **completely** free choice, is possible only for the children of Israel, by virtue of their being a part of His Essence and Being, may He be blessed, Who is—and **only** He is—truly free from all definitions and limitations. See also *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Emor*, 40b, and it is also explained in the *maamarim* of the Rebbe Rashab—those not yet printed—on the verse, "He will **choose** for us our inheritance."

## 5101

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And although the explanation of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse "A Psalm of David, when he was in the wilderness of Judah..." is well known—"If only"—that "so I have beheld You in the Sanctuary," and similarly regarding those who were in that country of yours, where the observance of Torah and mitzvos is bound up with literal mesiras nefesh, and despite this, they stood with actual mesiras nefesh and accomplished great and hidden things—the Baal Shem Tov made known that "If only" [one could maintain that same level of devotion] "so I have beheld You in the Sanctuary," for by the way of nature it is not so.

Yet, despite all this, there must be **some** comparison between the previous situation and the current situation, in a place where a Jewish person—and a Chossid in particular—has the ability to spread the wellsprings. As I said to you face-to-face, [doing so] in the midst of **hundreds and thousands of our fellow Jews.** And it appears that despite this, there is not even a proportional decrease in the dedication and enthusiasm in avodah—[except that, based on what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 25, I wonder why the students suffer...].

May it be the will of Hashem that since we are on the eve of the days of Geulah, in which we have seen miracles above the way of nature, and even with physical eyes, these days will be remembered as they ought to be. Consequently, there will be continuations [of this light] below the ten [sefirot], such that without seeking excuses and pretexts, they will recognize their true role: to draw thousands and myriads of Jews to the Torah of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 5717

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 29 Sivan, in which you write about the yeshiva where you study and the fact that every Shabbos a Chassid of Chabad comes there to teach a shiur in Tanya. You mention that you are in doubt as to whether you should join the Tanya study, and that you even have a notion to wait until you reach the age of forty, etc., etc.

How great is the concealment and hiddenness of our exile in these "footsteps of Moshiach," that after all that has been brought in many places regarding this (in the introduction of Rav Chaim Vital to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* of the Rebbe Rashab, and elsewhere) concerning the **necessity** of studying the inner dimensions of Torah in these generations, one can still stand in doubt about it, to the point of having the notion to begin this study only upon reaching the age of forty!

The difficulty is even greater when based on the principle of *maaseh rav* (the conduct of the great), for we see in practice that in order to withstand the unusual winds that, unfortunately, blow in the street, a special strength is required. The strength of previous generations is insufficient. This is analogous to the well-known statement of Chazal: "A great breach was found, and he built a fence in it." Just as with remedies for bodily illness—when a new disease arises, G-d forbid, one does not suffice with old medicinal ingredients—so too is it with the illnesses of the soul. In the "footsteps of Moshiach," where "insolence will increase," etc., it is impossible to suffice with the study of the revealed parts of Torah alone, even when one adds the study of *mussar*. The study of the inner dimensions of Torah is essential, which in our generations has been revealed in a manner of understanding and comprehension only through the teachings of Chabad, as is evident to the senses.

If one were to contemplate, even for a short while, the words of Rav Chaim Vital in his introduction to *Shaar HaHakdamos* regarding the "footsteps of Moshiach," and contemplate, even for a short while, the words of the aforementioned *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*, any upright person whose desires do not rule over his intellect would immediately begin and persevere in this study. And whoever is earlier in this, and whoever increases in this, is praiseworthy.

May it be the will of Hashem that a spirit from on high be poured upon you, and that you set fixed times for this study—a fixity not only in time, but also in the soul. Before long, you will see that it is good; the true good, as our Sages said: "Good to Heaven and good to people."

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 5304

By the Grace of Hashem
11 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, meticulous in his mitzvos, engaged in communal affairs, our esteemed R' Sh. Y. [Zevin]—may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the conclusion of Shabbos, Parshas Balak, and the one preceding it. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings regarding all the matters about which you write.

This is especially true as these days are auspicious for good tidings in the aforementioned matters, for they are the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—the redemption of our Nasi. This occurred in a manner of an open miracle, completely transcending nature. And "the body follows the head," and every year the events, the spiritual draws, and the influences are recreated in a manner similar to how they were the first time. This is alluded to in the well-known teaching regarding the verse: "And these days are remembered [properly] and kept"—meaning the spiritual draws and influences are re-effected.

With blessings for good tidings and for a successful Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote (in your third letter) concerning the difficult situation of... I am doing my utmost in this matter (as it is an exceptional case). And although it is difficult, it is impossible to be exempt without doing so.

The sefer *La'or HaHalacha* was received. As a token of appreciation and out of affection for the subject matter, I have noted—below—two or three comments, written in haste. *Sipurei Chassidim*, Vol. 2, has not yet been received.

Thank you for writing regarding the words of B. Mark. Surely you are aware by now that he has already been in contact with R. P. Althauser regarding this matter...

**Notes.**
**The War, etc.** Regarding the *Urim V'Tumim* in a *milchemes reshus* (discretionary war). The Rambam’s opinion: Since he equates it to the offerings, etc., and does not distinguish between the First and Second Temple, it implies that he holds there is no **necessity** for the *Urim V'Tumim*, but rather it is [done] "by the **advice** of the High Priest." And what is written, "And he shall ask of him"—this is a narrative of how the Kohen determines his advice. And what compelled the Rambam to explain it this way is the reality that in the Second Temple period, we also find instances of *milchemes reshus*.

By the way: The aforementioned Rambam is not the end of *Shoresh Yad*, but rather the beginning of *Sefer HaMitzvos*, as the Rambam states: "And now I will begin, etc." The printers were not precise in the division of the paragraphs and the page headings.

**Regarding the above.** In the note. It is surely known that Rabbi Kahana has already responded to this, and it is in print. It is somewhat surprising that it is not mentioned in this context. And the main point—regarding the words of the aforementioned [person] in the name of several others, attempting to refute the entire matter of the sale. Your honor brought them up as a passing, separate point.

**From "And so on" onwards.** At one of the *farbrengens*, this was discussed at length, regarding the reason for the dispute between Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel concerning the New Year for trees. An essential point was added: that nevertheless, Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel did not disagree on **all** the laws of the Torah, even though in every case there is both *koach* (potential) and *po'al* (actualization). For there is no room for the logic that the *koach* is sufficient, except in laws concerning matters that are in the realm of *koach* (that which is in the future), some of which they disputed, such as Rosh Hashanah, the susceptibility of food to ritual impurity, etc. And likewise a miracle (as in the case of Chanukah)—which changes [nature] and includes within it the future as well, as is proven by the proof from the Gemara (*Shabbos* 97a) that "the attribute of good is greater, etc.," and that it was a miracle within a miracle. And based on this, it is also explained why the statement regarding a "miracle within a miracle" was brought there in general.

## 5175

B"H, 12 Tammuz, Day of the Redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Israel, 5717

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned immigrants from Morocco residing in Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem grant them life!

Peace and blessing!

On this bright day, I acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you inform me of your settling in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily and in our days—a village founded and directed by the Baal HaSimcha of this day.

For if, even during their lifetime in this world, physical location does not limit the reception of the blessings of the Tzaddikim, then all the more so when the limitations of the soul’s vessel, which is bound to the body, have been removed—as is explained in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (who decides in the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who decides in the revealed aspects of Torah), in the explanation to Epistle 27.

Especially when the subject is the Nasi of Israel, the faithful shepherd, the *atpashuta d'Moshe* (extension of Moses) of our generation, regarding whom—and regarding his extension—our Sages of blessed memory said: "Just as he stands and serves there, so too he stands and serves here." He awakens great mercies for all who are connected and bound to him, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, for whatever they and their households may need, both materially and spiritually.

Based on all this, I am confident that you will settle well in Kfar Chabad, where Hashem has ordained the blessing, with goodness that is visible and revealed in all your affairs. And through the strengthening and dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs within the four cubits of each and every one of you—and from there, in your respective portions of the world—you will bring the true and complete Redemption ever closer, as explained in the holy Tanya, Chapter 37. May we merit speedily the fulfillment of the prophecy: "They shall all know Me..." and "The earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem..."

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and to carry the inspiration, joy, and success of the Day of Redemption throughout the entire year—I await good tidings in the near future, together.

## 5707

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Yosef Menachem, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 6th of Tammuz, which was received on the auspicious day of the 12th of Tammuz—the day of the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from his imprisonment for his mesiras nefesh for Torah and mitzvos. He stood up against a mighty empire, and as is known, open miracles were seen, such that even an "evil angel must answer amen." The details of these events are well known, even though for several reasons not all the particulars are yet publicized, as was discussed at the farbrengen. Since nothing in the world is in vain, the fact that this news reached us serves as a directive in our avodah as well: one must not be impressed at all by the environment and its opposition (even if we were to assume that it is not merely imagined), but rather to walk in the path of the King, the King of kings. Not only does one fulfill the command of the Creator in this manner, but ultimately, one also sees success despite the opposition, and in the vast majority of cases, it is clearly seen that the opposition has no reality, but is merely imagined.

It was pleasant for me to see your father, the esteemed Rav, may he live, at the farbrengen of the Chag HaGeulah. May it be His will that in your own affairs and the affairs of the entire family, you too will see redemption from all things that distract from the study of Torah and peace of mind, and may you have expansion in the fulfillment of His mitzvos with joy and a good heart.

Regarding what you wrote about ships traveling on Shabbos, it would be worthwhile for you to ask our relative, the esteemed Chossid R' Avraham Zvi Slonim, may he live, to show you the copy of my letter that he has, which describes the sailing of ships in our times. From it, you will realize the magnitude of the alarm regarding this matter and the darkness of the galus—that despite it being a clear prohibition with no room for doubt, people turn a blind eye, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient. As I wrote to someone else, never before has there been such a thing where those who are fearful of the word of Hashem stumble en masse in a mitzvah that is weighed against all other mitzvos, and specifically in public, and specifically in the name of Klal Yisrael. Furthermore, they dress this up in the guise of love for the Land, etc., etc. It is difficult to elaborate on a matter that is so painful it causes alarm.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the matters you mention in your letter—it is understood that you are included in this—and with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah.

## 508

13 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter. I will begin with the primary matter regarding your sister, *tichyeh*. Regarding what the *chassan*, *shiyeh*, told you—that you should speak with your sister—I hope that you have already begun to act on this immediately. One must allow time for her to become accustomed to the idea, quite apart from the fact that there are specific *halachic* details involved, in which it is not appropriate for the *chassan* to assist, for several reasons.

It is understandable that she may find this difficult to accept—all the more so, and *kal v’chomer*, even for those who come from and reside in a more religious and *chareidi* environment. However, it goes without saying that this does not change the essence of the matter: that it must be observed. I hope that now, as you bring up the conversation we had during her visit with me, you will emphasize that she must consider my opinion regarding *shemiras haTorah* in general, and *shemiras haTaharah* in particular. Emphasize this with appropriate words until it reaches actual implementation.

May it be the will of Hashem that these words, which come from the heart, be expressed with pleasantness yet with the necessary firmness; for then one is successful. If only you would speak—with ways of pleasantness and with even greater firmness—to the *chassan*, you would have more success than you imagine. As for the proof that he comes from such a family and environment, yet it did not influence him—what more can you do? It is well known that there are greater precedents than this. As the Gemara relates regarding the *nachash hanechoshes* (the copper serpent), it became an object of *avodah zarah*, and many righteous kings did not eradicate it until Chizkiyahu came, and "the place was left for him to distinguish himself." This is true in all eras and all places. Especially now, his conduct in *Torah u’mitzvos* affects your sister and their building of a *bayis b’Yisrael*. Furthermore, the fact that a *chassan* on his wedding day is forgiven for all his sins is proof that there is a special *hemshech* from Above, providing an opportunity to establish themselves on the proper Jewish, Torah-true foundation. As I have written to many people regarding many matters: since the Torah says, "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor" (*hocheiach tochiach*), even to the point of rebuke and striking, one understands from this how much rebuke can accomplish. For even when the person is already rebuked and the striking is not yet needed, the Torah still says to continue the *hocheiach tochiach*. And I certainly hope that in this case, the situation is not at all like that, *chas v’shalom*.

I am surprised that you do not mention what your sister told you about the conversation here, and I hope you will complete this at the next opportunity.

I hope you will also find the appropriate words to explain to the *baalei batim* of the stores that the concept of *is'arusa d'leila* (arousal from Above) does not mean that an angel with two wings comes down and shouts, "Do *teshuvah*!" Rather, there are many *shluchim* for the *Makom* through whom the *Ribono shel Olam* points with His finger that one must change and begin to walk in the path of *Torah u’mitzvos*. This is also the "pointing with the finger" in this matter: a law has been issued that one must close on *Shabbos*. The fact that a few hours remain not included in the law is nothing more than a *nisayon* (test), to provide an opportunity so that with free choice (*bechirah chofshis*), they may choose life and good, and keep the stores closed during those hours as well. And the matter is understood. It goes without saying that you have permission to mention my name in this matter as well, if you think it will increase the chance of influencing them as stated above.

Finding ourselves on the day of 13 Tammuz, I hope that for you, too, this day is different from all other days—not only in the omission of *Tachanun*, which is merely a consequence, but in the essential matter: that the *helem v’hester* (concealment) regarding *Torah u’mitzvos*—which unfortunately exists, both in general matters and in private matters—is transformed. *Megalgelin zechus l’yom zakai* (merit is brought about on a meritorious day), so that the *hachlatos tovos* (good resolutions) accepted on this day should be successful and be drawn down for the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and with the blessing of *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 5717

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 6th of Tammuz, in which you write regarding the difficulties you have encountered in studying the holy Tanya.

I have already stated this to many who have asked about such matters: it is puzzling why, when studying Tanya, people change their method of study from how they approach other parts of our Torah, and then express wonder at the difficulties they encounter.

My meaning is this: when one approaches the study of the Written Torah—Chumash, Mishnah, and Gemara—it is simple and understood that when a beginner starts studying Vayikra or Bereishis, one does not explain to him Rashi’s commentary, and certainly not the commentaries of the other *meforshim*. Rather, one conveys to him the content of the text in general, and the explanation of the verse according to its literal meaning, in the **greatest** simplicity. Even if he is a *talmid chacham* and asks why a certain *aleph* is small, unlike other letters, or asks about other such nuances that Rashi and the Torah commentators resolve in their works, he is told that the time for that will come later, and that he should not demand that all this be explained at the beginning of his studies. Even though his question is a valid one, he must continue studying **specifically** in the simple manner until he matures and gathers more knowledge of the subject matter.

The same applies to the study of the Oral Torah. When one studies the Mishnah for the first time, not only does one not study it with *Tosafos*, but one does not even study it with Rashi, nor with the nuances that the Gemara derives from the Mishnah. **The opposite** of logic is to do otherwise, as per the instruction of Chazal: "A person should first learn [the text] and then understand [the reasoning]," as discussed in the *sugya* (Shabbos 63a; and similarly at the end of Berachos and Avodah Zarah 19a). This applies even to those who are intelligent and possess broad knowledge; in relation to their level of *lisbar* (understanding), they must engage in *lemigras* (learning the text) more and more. From this, it is understood that in the study of Chassidus, too, one must proceed in exactly this way: first, one grasps the general concept; afterward, one studies it superficially; and from time to time, one delves into greater depth and detail.

While it is understood that the aforementioned approach is easier for a young child than for someone who has been studying Torah for many years, as mentioned above, the rule of "first learn and then understand" applies to them as well. For them, too, applies the obligation of "we will do" preceding "we will hear," for only in this manner did Yisrael receive and maintain their Torah (Shabbos 88a).

It is understood that if it is possible to go to someone who is an expert in this study, one should ask him about the specific nuances even at the beginning of one’s studies, as this will generally make the learning easier. But as stated, this is not the [primary] path, even if the expert is able to explain the nuances through concepts with which they are accustomed.

To facilitate your study of Tanya—even in your current situation where you only rarely have the opportunity to ask the opinion of an expert in this part of Torah—it is appropriate that you first study *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, then *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, and only afterward the first part of Tanya. Likewise, study the *Kuntres Umaayan* and the book *Derech Mitzvosecha* by the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, which is written in a more standard style, and to a certain extent, each topic is explained independently. Together with the aforementioned approach, I hope that within a short time you will see good fruit from your labor in studying this part of our holy Torah, and that the verse will be fulfilled in you: "Taste and see that Hashem is good," for the Torah and the Holy One, blessed be He, are one, and the hidden aspects of the Torah correspond to the hidden aspects of the Holy One, blessed be He (Zohar Vol. III, 73a).

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 5110

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters from the 27th of Sivan and thereafter, in which you write regarding the state of your health and the opinions of several doctors whose advice you sought, and that consequently the thought has occurred to you, etc.

It is appropriate in such a case that during the month of mercy—Elul—there be a consultation (*consilium*) of two expert physicians whom you have visited and who have examined you. You should explain to them your reasoning and rationale, and thereafter act according to their instruction, for the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal.

Regarding what you write concerning the attitude of so-and-so toward you—that he should have drawn you close but did not do so, etc.—and that you apparently connect this with your own attitude toward the study of Torah, etc.: it is simple that there is no connection between the two. For the study of Torah is because it is the will and wisdom of the Blessed One, and it is our life. If someone’s attitude toward you is not as it should be, is it truly possible to say, logically, that because of this you should harm yourself by reducing your study of Torah, etc.? Especially since it is possible that the attitude of the aforementioned person is, in truth, better than you imagine; but a person is close to himself, and self-love covers all transgressions. In particular, you should take into account what is written, "He who spares his rod hates his son," and as our Sages of blessed memory said, "Your children—these are the students." You should increase your diligence and perseverance in the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus. It is certainly possible to arrange this without it affecting your health matters at all, as is evident in practice, and it will be good for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

#### ***5110***

**That he should have drawn you close:** And since he did not draw him close, he therefore did not study.

## 515

## 5716

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Professor Avraham Yitzchak HaKohen, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the catalog of Hebrew manuscripts brought via microfilm from those located in Russia, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me. It is my hope that you will also send me the second part when it is ready, and I thank you in advance.

In glancing through the catalog in haste, I found a few matters to remark upon, which I am sure will interest you:

1) Manuscript M 38. You are surely aware that in *Yoma* 69b there are several variant readings. Perhaps that is why you chose this fragment.

2) Manuscript M 95, *Drush HaMelachim*. You write that this is a *Midrash* on the names of the kings of Israel. If that is the case, it is an extremely rare item. On the other hand, the *Drush HaMelachim* in Kabbalah is well known—it concerns the names of the kings of Edom (at the end of *Parshas Vayishlach*, and in the parallel passage in *Divrei HaYamim*).

3) Manuscript M 98, *Sefer HaTekunah* by Rav Chaim Vital. I believe it was printed in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and I also believe it is found in our library, although it is not currently at hand. Regarding your note that there is an introduction to the book titled *Mavo Shearim*, you are surely aware that there is an entire book by Rav Chaim Vital by that name. Therefore, it is unlikely that Rav Chaim Vital would also name an introduction to another one of his books *Mavo Shearim*. Perhaps it is not by Rav Chaim Vital.

With respect, blessing, and thanks.

In a separate package, we have sent you some of what we have published recently.

***

## 5717

5717

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, Tel Aviv Branch
May Hashem grant them life!

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Friday, Erev Shabbos Parshas Balak, 6 Tammuz. I am certain that in the meantime you have received the copy of the letter sent via the secretariat regarding the need to increase your avodah. It is my hope that you are doing everything possible in this direction, especially since we have since passed the Yom HaGeulah of our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who invested so much effort in the organization, development, and avodah of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad.

Although, on the face of it, the period of Bein HaMetzarim is a time of diminished joy because it reminds us of the destruction and ruin, it is obvious that this time is not a matter for sadness or low spirits. On the contrary: that which was destroyed was the lower Beis HaMikdash, built of wood and stone, not the spiritual and internal Beis HaMikdash. As is well known, the statement of our Sages regarding the verse "And I will dwell within them" [refers to] within each and every one of them. The purpose of Bein HaMetzarim is to remind and awaken us that it is the obligation of every Jewish man and woman to create a "dwelling place in the lower worlds" through the observance of Torah and mitzvos in daily life, to fulfill that which is written, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell within them" — literally. [We must] hasten the complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu by spreading the wellsprings, even among those who are still "outside." The responsibility upon each and every one of us is great, especially in these days, following the terrible destruction and ruin that we saw with our own eyes. Divine Providence saved us and left us as a remnant to keep a great nation alive. Since Hashem does not deal harshly with His creatures, it is clear that along with the great, double-fold responsibility placed upon each and every one of us, we have also been given the strength, the ability, and the possibility for each person to fulfill their role.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that very soon these days will be transformed into joy and gladness.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5118

[Tammuz 5717]

...Regarding what was written about my desire that the wellsprings be spread in every Chassidic shul — it is clear that this is not precise at all. For my intense desire and longing is that we merit to see, in actual reality, the fulfillment of the prophecy that in every shul of Bnei Yisrael, without any distinction whatsoever, they will study the inner dimensions of the Torah. This is an explicit verse, and a **clear** halachic ruling (Rambam, Yesodei HaTorah 2:2: **"And from them one will perceive** the wisdom that has no value... **to know the Great Name**..." See also the beginning of chapter 5 of Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah by the Rambam, the explanation of the halacha which is also cited in Tur Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 231. These are wondrous and absolutely clear matters).

## 5619

5619

*[Tammuz 5717]*

...Regarding what is written in the glosses of Rav Chaim Vital to the Zohar Chadash (231a) that prior to Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai, they did not observe Rosh Hashanah in Eretz Yisrael for only one day—yet according to the Tosafos in Rosh Hashanah (19b), even in the days of Ezra they did so.

Even according to Tosafos, the event of Ezra was an absolute exception. As the Gemara states there: "From the days of Ezra, we do not find..." whereas the Zohar speaks of a permanent, fixed practice "at all times." See also the language of the Alter Rebbe in Likutei Torah, in the *maamar* beginning *Yechayeinu Miyomayim*.

Regarding the opinion that holds one should observe Rosh Hashanah in Eretz Yisrael even now for only one day—this is not the *halacha* (and according to their view, the inner dimension of the matter is resolved—following the style of Rav Chaim Vital, that in Eretz Yisrael there is no fear). See also the response of Rav Hai Gaon on this (printed in *Otzar HaGeonim*, Beitzah, Chapter 1).

#### ***5619***

This letter is to R' Shaul Bik, and it was written on the margin of his letter dated 12 Tammuz 5717. Additional letters to him appear above in 5564, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 520

520

*[Tammuz 5717?]*

... A note (written in haste) regarding a point of interest — in the attached sheet (page 9) to your letter, in your first explanation.

At the beginning of the **Maamar "Ar"i"**: You remain with a *tzarich iyun* regarding the Rambam. To me, it is not difficult, for one must conclude that "they do not accept" in this Tosefta applies even *bedieved*, since it concludes, "but if they sanctified them, their sanctification is valid," and it does not say the stronger case that "if they sanctified them, they accept them." And in *Arachin* 6a, *reish amud alef*, it is a different *baraita*, as is evident *b'lo hachi nami* from the fact that it is taught in different language. See there in *Shitah Mekubetzes*. There is no need for the forced explanation in *Korban HaEdah*, nor does he distinguish, etc. And what you wrote regarding *Tiklin Chadtin* and *v'ib'a iteima*, etc., requires further study. It seems you were drawn after the *sugya* in *Arachin* there.

**There, *amud beis*, *dibbur hamaschil* "Aval":** You suggest that it comes **also** according to the opinion of Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai, etc. — It seems to me that it comes (according to the commentary of the Rash Sirilio) only according to the opinion of Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai. For according to the one who says that *Kohanim* are exempt from the *machatzis hashekel*, there is no need to reason that the exemption of *Kohanim* from the *kolbon* is because they are like women. Especially according to the language of the Rash Sirilio on this, which is transcribed in *Meleches Shlomo*.

#### ***520***

The letter is to R' Ephraim Zev Garbuz.

**In the attached sheet:** *Yerushalmi Shekalim* according to the *Rash Sirilio* and R' Ephraim by the aforementioned R' A.Z. Garbuz (Jerusalem 5718).

## 5761

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the day that was "doubled in goodness" [Tuesday] of Parshas Masei, along with the enclosed.

It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, the condition of your foot has already improved. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all matters related to this, as well as in spiritual matters. As is known, the "foot" in spirituality refers to the concept of *emunah*, regarding which it is said that the 613 *mitzvos* were given to Moshe at Sinai, and Chavakuk came and established them upon one, as it is written: "And the *tzaddik* shall live by his *emunah*." This is explained in several places, among them in *Shaar HaEmunah* by the Mitteler Rebbe.

And this day brings it about—it is the *yom hilula* of Aharon, the great Kohen.

With the blessing that we merit, together with all of *Klal Yisrael*, that through the events of these days which come from the "Father" (and note the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe, *siman* 22, beginning with the words "And like"), they will be transformed speedily in our days into a revelation of countenance in the dimension of revealed *ahavah* permeated with *Chassidus* (as is known the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the example in the beginning of the aforementioned *maamar* of the Alter Rebbe: that in the description of the example at its beginning, he did not write the title "Chassid," even though he is merciful, wise, and a *tzaddik*, because in its revealed form it is a matter of rebuke. And this is understood). And the *Menachem* [Comforter] will be revealed, until we say, "I will thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me... and You comforted me," specifically through the double comfort.

## 5622

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding the situation of your son... shlita.

At an opportune time, I will mention him at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the improvement of his situation and for a favorable resolution soon.

Since his state of mind was caused by the passing of his younger brother, a"h, it should be explained to him that by involving himself in matters that bring benefit to the children of Bnei Yisrael, he will thereby cause nachas ruach to his brother’s neshamah—and only through this, not through isolation, etc. After all, all of Bnei Yisrael, and indeed all religious people, believe in the immortality of the soul; that is to say, the soul is eternal and exists forever, waiting for those who care about its happiness to do something for its benefit and for the aliyas haneshamah through good deeds for the benefit of Bnei Yisrael. It is obvious that in a state of isolation, he cannot do anything for the soul, whereas by being active in a way that suits his talents and abilities, he can.

It is understood that you may show this letter of mine to your son, and may it be Hashem’s will that he listens to this instruction of mine, and seeks—and then he will also find—a position and work, through which he will bring benefit and, consequently, also cause nachas ruach to his brother’s neshamah.

It is appropriate to have the mezuzos in your home checked, and that your son’s tefillin be checked as well.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 17th of Tammuz.

May it be the will of Hashem—who guards His people Israel and watches over each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, and who is the essence of goodness—that He guard you, both physically and spiritually, wherever you may be.

Since "there is no one among us who knows how long", you must view yourself as having been sent to the environment where you are now in order to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit in general, and the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs in particular. Any exertion and effort in this regard is worthwhile, commensurate with the magnitude and importance of the matter. For if this is true wherever one happens to be, it is all the more so in an environment where an additional specific command has been added, and which is a holy educational institution. And as mentioned above, "there is no one among us who knows how long," and it is possible that once you fulfill this *shlichus*, you will be returned to your previous environment in an orderly fashion, with kindness and in peace.

You have surely read the transcripts of the *sichos* based on the saying of the Baal Shem Tov that from every matter, a person must learn a lesson in *avodah* to Hashem. When one is in an environment founded on the principle of discipline and *kabbalas ol*, this serves as a constant and ceaseless reminder that the beginning, essence, and root of *avodah* is the matter of *kabbalas ol malchus shamayim*, and this is well understood.

You surely held a *farbrengen* during the days of *geulah*, and may it be His will that the *hisorerus* and joy continue throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***5717***

**In an environment... holy:** In the army.

## 5717

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 3 Tammuz, in which you outline the main events of the past two months: Fortunate is your portion, for you have merited to disseminate the wellsprings of the words of the Living G-d—the teachings of Chassidus—by studying this Torah with several of your peers. May it be the will of Hashem that your efforts succeed in increasing the number of participants in this study, going from strength to strength. As the Sages of blessed memory have promised: "If you have labored and found, believe it."

Certainly, you will also utilize your position as the head of the group of... to influence them as well in this regard, in a manner appropriate to their understanding, comprehension, talents, and knowledge. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially when the merit of the many assists you.

Regarding what you write—that you engage in self-reflection, questioning who you are to teach others, given your knowledge of your own standing, etc.—the test to determine the source of such a claim is already well-known: if a claim prevents one from performing a good deed, it is known to come from the *sitra achra*. This is as per the saying of our Rebbe, the Rebbe Rashab, recorded in *Hayom Yom* for 23 Sivan, 5703; see it there. Refrain from such distraction of the soul and mental confusion, and may you bring good news regarding your influence upon your students and those you affect. Your reward is guaranteed by our Father in Heaven: that your own heart and mind will become a thousand times more refined.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of the 17th of Tammuz:

I have already written to you that you should cease fearing what man can do to you. Our G-d in heaven oversees each and every person with Divine Providence, and He is the essence of good. One only needs to create the channels and vessels for the drawing down and receiving of His blessings, which are the matters of Torah and mitzvos. When one requires an increase in blessing, one must increase in Torah and mitzvos, for through them and by means of them, one receives the blessings of Hashem.

Regarding your wife, may she live and be well, who you write cries out and weeps in the middle of the night, etc.: you should have the mezuzos of your home checked. She should set aside a few coins for tzedakah before lighting the candles and every weekday morning. Before sleeping, she should recite the first paragraph of Krias Shema, and she should not eat foods that are difficult to digest an hour or two before sleeping.

It gave me pleasure to read that you participated in the Chag HaGeulah in Kfar Chabad. May it be His will that the joy and the hisorerus for matters of Torah and mitzvos continue throughout the entire year.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5206

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5717

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5727

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5717

The work of chinuch and teaching on the foundation of taharas hakodesh—in our current era—is a mitzvah that **cannot** be performed by others (since "the performance of others is not sufficient" in any way, shape, or form), and all the relevant halachos apply to this, as explained in the Shulchan Aruch. See Hilchos Talmud Torah of the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 4, Section 3 and onwards.

#### ***5727***

Printed in "Teshuvos U'Biurim" (Kehot, 5747), p. 313. This is a response to the question: Do the statements of Chazal, such as "Minimize your business and occupy yourself with Torah," or "Make your Torah study fixed and your work temporary," apply also to one who is engaged in the work of chinuch and teaching; or is it the case here that one should say, "The more one increases, the more praiseworthy it is"?

See also the following letter.

## 5717

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

... And he should explain to the father of the young woman in question that the matter of the proper chinuch of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in our current era is a mitzvah that cannot be fulfilled by others, since, as our Sages of blessed memory expressed it, their efforts are not sufficient in the slightest. A mitzvah of this nature overrides even the mitzvah of Talmud Torah, which is weighed against all other mitzvos, and it certainly overrides financial and material considerations.

May it be the will of the Creator of the world, who watches over each and every one with hashgacha pratis, that He guide him in what is good in His eyes, both materially and spiritually.

5717

7 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, etc., R’ Shazar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 15 Tammuz. I derived special satisfaction from reading that you participated in the farbrengen of Chag HaGeulah in Kfar Chabad, in the presence of several individuals who were eyewitnesses and brothers in adversity during those days. Seeing is not like hearing; furthermore, one who has seen with his own eyes—and is not a stranger—can influence the listener with the vitality within him. This is especially true when the listener possesses the Chassidic vessels to receive this influence. When both are combined, a reciprocal influence and wholeness are achieved: both for the listener, for whom the matter becomes verified, and for the speaker, who is influenced by the enthusiasm he has stirred in the listener.

I received a letter from Rabbi Kalman Kahana, along with the material regarding the Shmittah year, which he sent to me—as he writes—at your encouragement. Many thanks for this as well.

Regarding what you write concerning the village’s agriculture, surely they have told you of my perspective on this: that all those who are connected to it should continue in this specifically, as is also known from the letter of the Mitteler Rebbe.

I was especially happy with what you write regarding Mr. Ben-Gurion. May it be the will of the Almighty that his participation in the farbrengen of the days of Geulah will also make him a recipient and one who is guided. As is known, one of the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus is based on the verse, "There is no man who is not found from beginning to end." Through the Creator’s compassion for all parts of creation, and His desire that the good be in its fullness, they were arranged in such a way that each one is both a recipient and a provider. So much so that, as it were, the Creator Himself says of Himself, "You shall yearn for the work of Your hands," and in the language of our Sages, "Avodah is a need of the Above," and when Yisroel performs the will of the Makom, they add strength to the Power Above.

With this, I return to the question of the necessity of expanding the village (although, of course, I am not at all dismissing the idea of founding a second village—once this village is established to its full need). Through this, the question of names would also be negated in the future, so that it would not be possible to raise it again.

I was happy to read in your letter that you will speak with Mr. Yubiler regarding the publication of the writings of Rabbeinu HaZaken. Since we are moving forward from Chag HaGeulah—which, as we heard from the Rebbe Rayatz, was not his private redemption, but the redemption of all matters of Chassidus Chabad—may it be the will of the Almighty that this auspicious day bring redemption to all matters of the dissemination of Chassidus, and especially the father of the teachings of Chabad, Rabbeinu HaZaken.

Regarding what you write about housing for the students of Toras Emes, this has long been part of my plan, especially for those who are about to get married and, for various reasons, are settling specifically in Yerushalayim, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established, even though the issue of housing there involves very great expenses. Since they are settling there regardless, and eventually find the means to rent or purchase an apartment, there is surely room for their commitments regarding the housing project about which you spoke with me. Following the conduct of the Rebbe Rayatz in utilizing the strengths of the young, it is my intention, as the matter nears a practical stage, to link the housing issue with the commitment of the young people residing there to dedicate their time to the benefit of the public as teachers, guides, etc., whether in Yerushalayim itself or in other places for a certain period, since the shortage in this area is becoming increasingly acute.

It is my hope that it is possible to arrange assistance for the aforementioned in a way that will not detract at all from the assistance for the village’s needs.

It is understood that I have been following the discussions of the Vaad HaPoel. Everyone looks for matters that suit their spirit and that they can utilize over time. It was pleasant for me to see that step by step, you are approaching the traditional perspective. In addition to the matter we discussed, now everyone has agreed that this is not the coming of Moshiach, G-d forbid (although he is standing behind our wall, but due to our many sins, the wall still exists, even though several windows and cracks have already been made in it, and he is watching and peering through them). And now another essential step has been taken: the recognition that first and foremost, every single one of the children of Yisroel, even those who are in Eretz Yisroel, are Jews, and only after that comes the matter of being found, living, and settling in Eretz Yisroel. This is consistent with what we discussed, that we are looking for the common points and those matters in which we can walk arm-in-arm—and even more so, walk together. This is a happy fact, that you are progressing in this direction.

Surely you also participated in the international research conference that just concluded.

Enclosed is a list of what was discussed before the children of our summer camp, "Gan Yisroel," based on the words of the Nesi'im of the teachings of Chassidus.

During my work in such matters, I have realized that one of the most difficult things is to translate matters from the teachings of Chassidus into a language that is understandable even to those who are, for the time being, "outside." And our era is the era of dissemination, primarily to those who are "outside."

To conclude with words of comfort during these days of Bein HaMetzarim: although we diminish our joy during them, their intention and purpose is not merely punishment and depression, G-d forbid. On the contrary, they are days of rectification for those matters that brought about destruction and ruin. The rectification is according to what is known from the words of Chazal on the verse, "A Psalm of Asaf, O G-d, the nations have come..." that He poured out His wrath upon the wood and the stones—that is, upon the external Sanctuary. But the main Sanctuary is the internal one, within each and every person, as Chazal expound on the verse, "And they shall make Me a Sanctuary, and I will dwell within them"—within their hearts. The heart of a Jew is awake. Through the purification and sanctification of this internal Sanctuary in the heart of each and every one of the children of Yisroel, to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds, we will merit, in our own time, the building of the Beis HaBechirah by Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessing for success.

## 5731

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 23 Tammuz, in which you write regarding the two possibilities for renting a location for the cheder.

It is understood that renting a location under a hidden name, which would result in a constant fear of pressure, etc., is not advisable at all.

Regarding the name of the institution, it is a matter that requires study as to whether it is worthwhile to establish it immediately, as this will place a specific stamp upon it. The positive side of this is that those who are foreign to the spirit of this place will see immediately that they have no hand in it. However, there is also a negative side, in that it might prevent the participation of people who do not want it to be openly said that they belong to this framework. Accordingly, you should decide based on which of these considerations is more decisive in your current environment. If you decide to give it a name, and you are confident that the institution will be sustainable and managed properly, it should be named Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch and be incorporated into this network.

Regarding what you write about your desire to bring closer even those people whose influence is a concern should they express an opinion in the management of the institution, the safeguard (bavarenish) for this is simple: utilize their assistance in a manner that ensures they will have no spiritual influence on the management of the institution.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5733

11 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Tzvi, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters of the 26th and 27th of Tammuz.

May it be the will of Hashem that the commencement of the discussion regarding the issue of the ships will bring about a **tangible** shift toward resolving the matter in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life. One of the interpretations of this is that the Torah is a guide for daily life in every place and at every time, for "this Torah shall not be exchanged," etc.

And since Chazal have said, "He looked into the Torah and created the world," it is impossible—and contrary to reason—that worldly matters should hinder or prevent the fulfillment of what is stated in the Torah. For it is impossible, as is understood even through simple logic, for the effect to be stronger than the cause. Especially since, in the case at hand, the effect is but a tiny fraction of the matters of the Cause. Moreover, the Cause, in and of itself, is far too exalted even to be a "cause," as the Alter Rebbe writes in Tanya, Chapter 4: It is His will and wisdom, may He be blessed, which no thought can grasp at all, and it is obvious that it has no connection to the worlds; rather, "only G-d understood its path and knew its place" (see at length in Kuntres Acharon in Tanya, s.v. *Zemiros Karis Lehu*).

Enclosed is a clipping from an old letter in which there is mention of a ship that departed from Eretz Yisrael to Marseille on Thursday—that is to say, a journey that by all accounts could be made without *chillul Shabbos*, since it does not require more than six days. Yet, it departed specifically in a manner contrary to this! And this is not enough, but rabbis even arranged... prayer on it on the day before! This is providing a *hechsher* to the ship owners for a matter that, by all accounts, is forbidden *mi-d'oraisa*! After all this, is there any room for your question as to whether this might be perceived as an affront to someone’s honor? I must say that after all this, I do not know if I would have involved myself in the matter had there not been such conduct. The ship voyages in general bring destruction also to the observance of Shabbos **here**, even though it is not as desired even without this. Thereby, the matter becomes a problem for the city of New York and its inhabitants as well. Furthermore, as I have written to you previously, for many of those who tremble at the word of Hashem, this is not a problem at all, since the rabbis in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—act in the manner mentioned in the enclosed clipping, and so on and so forth.

Regarding the jubilee book in which you wish to print my letters concerning the ships, and I am enclosing a copy of another letter: if the letters are printed **as they are**, without softening them, then even though, as I have explained in my previous letters, it is not the custom of the house of the Rebbe to participate in a jubilee book or the like for understandable reasons, nevertheless, since my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the great Rabbi, etc., etc., *shlita*, the subject of the jubilee, is among those whom I approached with this question, it is obvious that he may publish them in the place he sees fit.

Regarding what you write about the Yekaterinoslav book: we are endeavoring to find a connection with the *Landsmanshaft*, and once the facts are known, we will correspond with you.

Give my regards to your family members, may they live... and may it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned, and especially regarding the matter of the ships.

With blessings for good tidings in the aforementioned.

Enclosed is a copy of my talk before the children at the Gan Yisrael summer camp under the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. In its opening, I intended it for all the children of Yisrael, and especially for those whom I mention, and their son Yehuda Leib, may he live, in all of this, as is understood and also simple.

## 5717

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the condition of your wife, may she live and be well.

May Hashem fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child, at the proper time, properly and with ease.

Regarding what you wrote concerning physical contact during pregnancy and at its conclusion—you did not clarify the nature of your doubt. Is it in this specific case that there is some concern from the perspective of Halacha (in which case you should present the matter before a Rav, and he will instruct you), or is it from the perspective of nature and health? If the latter, although there is a known statement of our Sages regarding this (Niddah 31a), it has already been ruled that "natures have changed" (see Rema in Shulchan Aruch, Even HaEzer, 156:4; Responsa Maharam Schick, Yoreh Deah 244; Sdei Chemed, Klalim, Ma'areches Tes, Section 6, and the sources cited there). [See also Rambam (Hilchos Geirushin 11:21) and Taamei HaMitzvos by R. Chaim Vital, Parshas Bereishis, s.v. V'b'inyan HaOnah]. Therefore, you must seek the opinion of an expert physician in this matter, especially in this case where she has seen stains, etc. I will not elaborate further.

## 5717

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av and the one preceding it, in which you ask regarding your intention to order *parshiyos* for *tefillin* for members of your family **who are of Chabad Chassidic background**, and you are in doubt as to how they should be written.

It is surprising that there is any doubt here, for the rule and the *psak* is that in the place (and among the followers) of a *Rav*, one follows his custom. As for the question you raise—that in your opinion, the conduct desired by Hashem is that which is practiced by the majority of *Klal Yisrael*—it is astonishing that you would pose such a question. It is surely obvious that our *Alter Rebbe* also wished to establish *tefillin* in a manner that would be desired by Hashem. It is simple to see that in the time of the *Alter Rebbe*, there were fewer people practicing according to his instructions than there are now, as the teachings of Chassidus have spread to many circles. Yet, despite this, he commanded that they be prepared specifically in the manner he instructed. If only you would abandon your path of seeking questions and contradictions, and begin to walk in the straight path by prioritizing *naaseh* before *nishma*—the path taught by our *Rebbeim Nesi'einu HaKedoshim*, which is also the general path for all of *Klal Yisrael*. This is similar to what is explained by the *Maggid* [who was also the teacher of the *Baal HaHafla'ah*, who was the teacher of the *Ran Adler*, who was the teacher of the *Chasam Sofer*] regarding the virtue of the "thirteenth gate" that includes all twelve gates; see the introduction to *Shaar HaKollel* for the *Siddur*.

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not yet feel capable of studying and feeling the teachings of Chassidus, and that, in addition, you have time constraints:

It is obvious that Hashem, *chas v'shalom*, does not make His Torah a mockery. It is written in His Torah that Hashem does not deal harshly with His creations. Since the knowledge of the teachings of Chassidus has already reached you—and furthermore, you have already begun to study it—the command of our Sages (*Eruvin 64a*) applies to you with full force: "Whoever says, 'This teaching is pleasant, but that one is not pleasant' [i.e., he admits that the latter is also a teaching, but for him, it is not pleasant]," the punishment, *r"l*, is terrifying. See there. From the above, it is clear that you are capable, and the obstacles can be overcome. Every day that passes without your study of Chassidus is an irretrievable loss—not only regarding the study of Chassidus, but also regarding the study of the *nigleh* (the revealed Torah). For in the *Zohar HaKadosh*, the inner dimension of the Torah is called the "soul of the Torah," whereas the *nigleh* is called the "body of the Torah." The descriptions in the Torah are precise, and we see tangibly that a small deficiency in the soul is felt throughout the entire body. *Kal v'chomer*.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5736

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and industrious, R' Menachem Zeev Halevi, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 11 Menachem Av and the one preceding it, along with the enclosures. I was very pleased with the few pages of *Likutei Minhagei Chabad* (Compendium of Chabad Customs), as well as the fact that you leave space between each section. Since your intention is that whoever possesses this compendium should not need to search through the original *kuntreisim*, you should also transcribe the footnotes from the *kuntreisim* wherever they exist, so that it becomes a complete work.

Regarding the sheet of questions—whether to add more: one should add to section 1, and also regarding the giving of *tzedakah* before *davening*, and cite the source in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Tavo* (43d), section 4, 7.

Regarding the other sections, it requires study (*tzarich iyun*) whether there is a defined, detailed, and absolute *kabbalah* (tradition) for them. In a place of doubt, "sit and do not write" is preferable.

I do not know the speed of your work on this compendium, but it is understood that if it were possible to publish it during the upcoming month of Tishrei, the timing would be most appropriate.

You should certainly continue with the lists of well-known Chassidic customs. Even though there are matters in them that are not accepted, and some where people even act in the opposite manner, I nevertheless enjoyed several of the citations within them. There will be further opportunity to write about this.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 5717

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter, in which you write about the difficulties you are having at home, particularly with your young children, may they live and be well. You write that—in your words—this is a matter of life and death for your children, and you are beginning to think about placing them, Heaven forbid, in a Christian missionary institution in Ramla.

I am certain that the above was written by you without any real thought. For even if it were, as you write, a matter of life and death for your children, placing children in a mission is not a "question" to be considered; it is a certain death, Heaven protect us, that one would be contemplating committing with one's own hands.

It is a source of terrible heartache that after Hitler, may his name be blotted out, murdered six million Jews, may Hashem avenge their blood, there are Jews who would express themselves (even if they do not actually intend it) about placing their own child in a Christian institution, Heaven forbid. It is well known what priests in Germany and elsewhere did to Jewish children, fathers, and mothers.

However, as I said, I am certain that this was written without due consideration, and perhaps someone gave you the advice to write in such a manner in order to make a stronger impression.

Regarding the practical matter, you should turn to people and organizations that deal with such issues. You can certainly find their addresses in Lod, and without a doubt, something will eventually come of it.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize that children are a blessing from Hashem, given to parents to raise and make happy, not, Heaven forbid, to destroy with one’s own hands by even thinking about a mission, Heaven forbid, or the like. This is especially true when one is in need of special blessings from the Ribono shel Olam regarding the health of your wife, may she live and be well, your own health, and your livelihood, etc.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you to be able to report good news in all of the above.

With blessings,

## 5740

15 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

This is especially relevant as we have entered the days of consolation—a double consolation. This means a double measure relative to all the *agmas nefesh* (distress) and pain, etc., *rachmana litzlan*, that occurred in the past, and a double measure in *kedushah*. For the Jewish body is also holy, as our *Rabbeinu HaZaken* states: "And You have chosen us from all peoples and tongues"—this refers to the material body, which appears in its materiality to be like the bodies of the nations of the world (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 47). And the day itself causes this, for as is known from our Sages, from this point forward, "whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good news regarding the above.

## 5781

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Furthermore, they added and informed us that if the Jewish people were to observe even one Shabbos, Mashiach would come immediately. Yet, despite this, there is no movement on the matter, and as the saying goes, they "move on to the order of the day." If it were those who do not desire the coming of Mashiach, one would not question them, for we are dealing with those who are not of our kind. But anyone who mourns for the Churban and the Galus, and who yearns and thirsts for the Geulah and the rebuilding, surely has every reason to exert all effort and toil, even for a single step and a single action, to alleviate the Galus and hasten the Geulah.

May it be the will of Hashem that since we have entered the days of consolation—and as our Sages of blessed memory put it, a double consolation, double against all the grief and sorrow, G-d forbid, of the past—we will merit to see the consolation of Tzion and Yerushalayim through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily and in our time.

With respect and blessing, looking forward to hearing good news.

The sefer *Eden Tzion* has also just been received. Many thanks.

## 5743

B"H, 15 Menachem Av,
A Yom Tov for Yisrael like Yom Kippur,
5715 – Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the listeners participating in the shiur of Tanya Kadisha
in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established speedily.
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, which brings good news regarding the study of the Tanya Kadisha of Rabbeinu HaZaken, of blessed memory, and of your *sevi'as ratzon* (satisfaction) with this shiur.

The precision of this expression, common among all Bnei Yisrael, is understood: *sevi'as ratzon* (satisfaction of will) rather than *sevi'as chefetz* (satisfaction of desire). For *chefetz* is the inner dimension of the will, which is always firmly attached to Him—to Hashem and His Torah. *Ratzon*, by contrast, is subject to change, to the point where one may sometimes need to be coerced until he says, "I want to." Therefore, it teaches us a great deal that even the power of *ratzon* reaches a state of *sevi'ah* (satiety)—not merely the fulfillment of a desire, but a *sevi'as ratzon*, meaning the performance of a mitzvah, which is the will of the Makom, in a manner of *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min ha-mehadrin*.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as is required of each and every one of us, you go from strength to strength. Consequently, the measure of your *ratzon* will also be increased, in the language of the Mishnah: "Make your will as His will." May you fill and satisfy this measure as well, through increasing your shiurim and studies, and may the promise be fulfilled: "Whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***5743***

**In the shiur of Tanya Kadisha:** Conducted by R' Yehoshua Elboim. See the letter from 5735 below.

**For the *chefetz*... the *ratzon*:** See also the letter from 5382 above.

## 5744

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is understood that to sell the stock shares he currently holds, when such a sale involves a loss, is entirely inappropriate.

The merit of his commitment to the Lubavitch institutions, about which the travelers—may they live—informed me, will surely stand by him in the promise of "tithe so that you may become wealthy" (*aser bishvil shetis'asher*), in its literal sense—that is, for the expansion of his livelihood. From this, it is understood that he should delay the sale of the shares until such time as the sale will yield a profit.

We are approaching the days of the month of mercy and joy. It is well known that the acronym for *Elul* (*Aleph-Lamed-Vav-Lamed*) refers to "a man to his fellow" (*ish l're'ehu*) and "gifts to the poor" (*matanos la'evyonim*). Our Sages of blessed memory explain that "a man" (*ish*) refers to Hashem, as it is written, "Hashem is a man of war," and He calls every one of the Bnei Yisrael by the names "brothers" and "friends." Even one who does not merit that title is included in the second category, "gifts to the poor" (*evyon*), which comes from the word *mit'aveh*—longing for everything.

May it be Hashem's will that with joy and a glad heart, he will increase his involvement in matters of Torah and mitzvos, including an increase in the fixed times for studying the teachings of Chassidus and an increase in matters of tzedakah. After all, yesterday we entered the day regarding which our Sages promised: "Whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good tidings.
