## 5717

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the state of your health, specifically concerning your eyes.

Based on how you describe the ailment, it appears to be what is called glaucoma. In such cases, it is common to perform a second surgery, although, naturally, this requires the guidance of the most expert specialists in the field. There are several such doctors in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and you should consult with them; the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal.

It is known that one of the segulos for a person’s eyesight, according to our Sages, of blessed memory, is to be careful with Kiddush and Havdalah over wine.

Regarding your question about a younger daughter marrying before an older one: In these days, the double and redoubled darkness of the *ikvesa d’meshicha*—the era when the son of Dovid will come once all the souls in the *guf* have been exhausted—if the older daughter grants a complete waiver, and it is best if this is done in writing or in the presence of valid witnesses, the matter is permitted. This is, of course, provided that the chassan is a *yirei shamayim*, etc. It is appropriate that, in addition to the waiver, the younger daughter and the parents of the girls should set aside a sum of money for the wedding expenses of the older daughter when she becomes engaged, in a good and auspicious hour.

You are surely aware of the three daily study portions that are equal for every soul—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and you should keep them, at the very least, from this point forward.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, regarding establishing a proper order in your path of Torah and yirah:

In general, this is not a matter that is the same for every soul; it depends on a person’s talents, the nature of their soul, and the time available to them. However, for a yeshiva student—which you appear to be—the standard approach requires learning for *iyun* (in-depth analysis), but also learning for *girsa* (covering ground). Furthermore, one must learn the halachos required for daily life, for Shabbos and Yomim Tovim, and in this final generation, it is **essential** to also learn the *pnimiyus haTorah* that has now been revealed in a way of understanding and comprehension—namely, the teachings of Chassidus. This should be studied every day for at least a short hour, and one should add to this significantly on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

Since one requires *siyata d’shmaya* for everything, including *Talmud Torah*, you should set aside money for tzedakah every weekday before the morning davening, study a Chassidic concept before davening, and be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*. May it be His will that you share good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5750

## 5717

18 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, a man of action, involved in communal needs, R' Reuven Tzvi Yehuda Feigelshtock, I learned of your state of mind, and that you say it is difficult for you to be comforted.

It is obvious, both according to faith and even according to reason, that the soul is eternal. This is especially true of the soul of a Jew, which is literally a "part of Hashem from above." From this, it is also understood that the soul always yearns for ascent. While it is in a physical body in this world, this is in its own hands through its performance of Torah and mitzvos. This is not the case once it ascends from the body; at that point, it depends on those who wish it well to earn merit for the soul by increasing their own involvement in Torah and mitzvos for its sake. In order for the Torah study and the performance of mitzvos to be in proper order, they must be done specifically with joy and a glad heart—out of gratitude for the privilege of fulfilling the will of the Giver of the Torah, and for the privilege of acting for the *aliyah* of the soul. If one is in a state of sadness, or even just bitterness, this is the opposite of the intended purpose. It detracts from the quality of the study and the performance of the mitzvah, and consequently, it also detracts from the *aliyah* of the soul.

Since we are speaking of an only son, it is obvious that you must do everything within your power for the *aliyah* of his soul. Being strong in your faith—that the soul is alive and exists—you can accomplish great things to earn it merit. You should be joyful for this ability. Sadness, *chas v'shalom*, or even bitterness as mentioned above, is proof of a weakening of faith, *chas v'shalom*, in the immortality of the soul, and so on.

May Hashem, blessed be He, strengthen your heart and mind to understand these matters in their truth, and to serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart. May you and your wife, *she-tichyeh*, raise your daughter, *she-tichyeh l'orech yamim tovim*, to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in good health.

It would be appropriate to hire someone to say Kaddish for the *neshamah* of your son, *a"h*, but not for you to say the Kaddish yourself. You should set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday morning for the *neshamah* of your son. Additionally, you should have the mezuzos in your home checked, as it appears that some of them are not kosher.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above.

## 5793

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the questions in your letter:

a) Regarding whether you should continue studying Tanya.

It is astonishing that there is even a question or doubt about this, Heaven forbid. It is understood and simple that the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*—which in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus—is **essential**. See the words of our teacher, R. Chaim Vital, in his introduction to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, and what he quotes from the holy *Zohar* regarding this—the words are staggering. See also the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by the Rebbe (Rashab), father of the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which discusses this at length. Even those who are students of the students of the Gra—here is the language of the Gra regarding this matter: "As long as one does not understand the *sod* (the mystical dimension), even the *peshat* (the literal meaning) is not clear to him. And one who could have grasped the secrets of the Torah but did not endeavor to do so is judged with harsh judgments, Heaven forbid. But those who occupy themselves with *remez* and *sod*—the *yetzer hara* cannot incite them" [Copied in the book *Even Shleimah*, Chapter 8, **and elsewhere**].

b) Among the advice given for dealing with distracting thoughts during *davening* is to minimize idle chatter throughout the day, as in the vast majority of cases, this is the source of idle thoughts. [Also helpful are] *davening* and learning from inside the *Siddur* and the *sefer*, and *davening* and learning in a state of purity—that is, by being careful with *tevilas Ezra*, and giving *tzedakah* before the morning *davening* on weekdays. Above all, in the language of the *Mishnah*, one should accept upon himself the **yoke** of the Kingdom of Heaven, and afterwards accept upon himself the **yoke** of Torah and *mitzvos*. As for influencing your peers in all the aforementioned—this merit of the many will stand by you to succeed in these matters.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**The language of the Gra:** See also above, Vol. 13, Letter 4601, and the references in the notes there.

## 5717

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you write, that matters are dragging on and on, etc.—although I have already hinted at this when speaking to your father, *shiy*, I will reiterate it here once more: It is a well-known teaching of our Sages that the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is *middah k'neged middah* (measure for measure). When one delays fulfilling a promise regarding matters of *tzedakah*—notwithstanding the *chasadim* of Hashem that one sees tangibly in **many, many** matters, and **without any reason** for this delay in fulfilling the promises, promises made in thought and even in speech—it is surely understandable that by doing so, one **himself** delays the *hemshech* (drawing down) from Above. How great is the *choshech gadol* (great darkness) of this *galus*, that one sees this even with physical eyes, yet fails to learn a moral lesson from it. May it be His will that, in any event, now all promises should be fulfilled **immediately and in their entirety**, and it would be proper—**with an addition** to the increase in blessing. And there should be a **complete resolution** for such good conduct also for the future, **with the intent to fulfill it in action**; then there will be the *k'neged middah* from Hashem, that "His word runs swiftly" in goodness and kindness that is revealed and manifest.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5556

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos, 20 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And since we have entered the days regarding which our Sages, of blessed memory, said that whoever adds, they add to him, may it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of you add to your involvement in Torah and mitzvos, illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus. May Hashem add His blessings in all that is needed for a person and his household.

We are also approaching the days of the month of mercy, the month of Elul. The letters of Elul (אלו"ל) are an acronym for "a man to his fellow" (*ish l're'ehu*) and "gifts to the poor" (*matanos la'evyonim*). It is well known that our Sages explain that "man" (*ish*) refers to the Holy One, Blessed be He, as it is written, "Hashem is a man of war," etc. He calls out to the Children of Israel, "My brothers and My friends." Even those who do not—on the surface—appear to be in the category of "brother and friend," are certainly included in the second category, "gifts to the poor" (*evyon*). An *evyon* is one who "desires" (*mit'aveh*) everything, for he lacks everything. May Hashem, in the words of our Alter Rebbe, with a pleasant countenance and a smiling face, fulfill the requests of everyone's heart for good and for blessing, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***5556***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 26, p. 443.

**We are also approaching:** See also Letter 5554 above. Similar content was written to several individuals.

## 5717

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter regarding your question: what should be one’s attitude toward the approach that suggests that in certain places or during certain eras there is no need for religion, or that one should make "reforms" in religion and the like, and that one sees in this a benefit for bringing hearts closer together?

It is astonishing that there is any room for doubt on a matter that is so clear, as it is a definitive ruling in many places in our holy Torah. Among them is the Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, Halachos 8-14, which states that one who says that the Torah is not from Hashem—even one verse or even one word—is a denier of the Torah. The same applies to one who denies its interpretation, which is the Torah Shebaal Peh. Regarding those we have enumerated, even though they are of Yisrael, they have no portion in the World to Come. In his Commentary on the Mishnah (Sanhedrin, beginning of Chapter 10), he elaborates further on this in the eighth fundamental principle.

From this, it is understood that the approach called "Reform," or the one that says there is no need—Heaven forbid—for religion, is not an approach within religion, but rather an approach of denial of the religion of Yisrael, and it is at war with it.

You do not mention this regarding yourself in your letter, but my hope is that the aforementioned question is merely for the sake of academic inquiry, and that you are strengthening yourself in the study of Torah and fulfilling mitzvos as required. May Hashem grant you success and bring you good tidings.

## 5758

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Yehoshua, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter regarding your question: since you are living in cramped quarters, is it advisable to rent a new apartment, even though doing so will cause you to incur debt?

Our Sages have stated that a pleasant dwelling expands a person's mind, and "if you have acquired knowledge, what do you lack?" Therefore, it is appropriate that you move to a more spacious apartment—provided, of course, that your wife, may she live, is in agreement with this. Through this expansion of mind, you will be able to increase your efforts in your most exalted work concerning the laws of family purity in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and in all matters of Torah and mitzvos in general. As is known, the explanation in the holy Tikkunei Zohar regarding the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that a pleasant dwelling expands a person's mind.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Regarding what you wrote concerning Rabbeinu Tam tefillin—I have not received anything on this matter. You should clarify this with the scribes of Anash in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

## 5760

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that it seems to you that you are not successful in your endeavors, etc.

You should divert your attention from all of this, for it is not true. The Ribono shel Olam, who created the world and directs it, is the essence of good. He watches over each and every one of the Bnei Yisrael in their affairs when they prepare the appropriate vessels to receive the blessings of the Creator of the world—which are the matters of Torah and mitzvos. Through these, they draw down the blessings, receive them, and succeed in life. The more one’s bitachon in the kindness of Hashem increases, the greater the blessing will be and the sooner it will arrive. Therefore, you should arrange your life according to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and continue in the profession in which you are currently working, or in which you worked previously, whichever is easier for you to manage, and Hashem will grant you success.

It is appropriate to have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and every day after morning davening, you should recite some chapters of Tehillim, or at the very least, one chapter.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5765

By the Grace of G-d
23 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 21 Menachem Av, containing the expert’s opinion regarding your health. May it be G-d’s will that you bring good news of continued improvement in this regard.

Regarding what you write, that you are preparing to travel to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—it is surely unnecessary to remind you that a journey such as this, which everyone refers to as an *aliyah* (ascent), and to a land that even the common folk refer to as the Holy Land, requires preparation. This means a spiritual *aliyah* of the person even before the journey, and a suitable resolution regarding one’s conduct while there. If a visa of flesh and blood is required to enter a country (or at the very least, notification that one does not require a visa), then how much more so is a "visa" from the Creator and Guide of the world—He who promised Eretz Yisrael to the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov—absolutely essential. If this applies to one’s general conduct, it applies all the more so to the manner of the journey, which must be in accordance with the laws and instructions of our holy Torah.

I am writing these lines because you mention in your letter that you intend to "set sail" (*lehaflig*) for there—an expression commonly used in reference to a ship. To our greatest sorrow, many people err and travel there on Israeli ships that continue their voyage even on the holy Shabbos. This constitutes a public desecration of Shabbos in the most alarming manner, and in the most public forum, before the eyes of all the nations. Regardless of how an individual may conduct his private life, this is not comparable to a ship that flies the banner of the entire Jewish people, while those traveling on it tell themselves that by doing so, they are expressing their love for the Jewish people and for Eretz Yisrael! Yet, it is impossible for the greatest prosecutor to become a defender! As is well known from the statements of our Sages, Shabbos is equivalent to all the mitzvos combined.

I would be happy to learn that I misinterpreted your use of the word "set sail," and even then, my hope is that these lines are not in vain. Explanation on this matter is essential, for according to the opinion of Torah, anyone who travels on such a ship on Shabbos contributes to the destruction of the Land and the destruction of the Jewish people, Heaven forbid. Since many err in this due to a lack of knowledge, one who informs them of the truth of the matter saves them from this most alarming act and sets them on the path of truth. The benefit is for the Jewish people and for our holy Land. I have enclosed a copy of what I have written to others who have asked me about this, so as not to repeat the points.

I have heard some ask: if the matter is so alarming, why do the Rabbis not issue a protest and cry out in a loud voice, etc., commensurate with the severity of the issue? But it is obvious that this question does not change the reality of the matter, especially since there are many such phenomena about which no alarm is raised at all.

With blessings for good news in all the above, in good health.

#### ***5765***

**On Israeli ships:** See above, 5734, and the references in the notes there.

## 5706

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, R' Nissan, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 19 Menachem Av, regarding the *Rosh Perek* of the *Siddur* during the summer days. It is possible that the discipline of the teachers is even more necessary than the discipline of the students, and this is understood. From this, it is understood that one should not be discouraged by the fact that it was necessary to dismiss one of the teachers, since the benefit of the many overrides the benefit of the individual.

I was pleased to read that the matter of *metzitzah* is progressing. May it be His will that you succeed in this as soon as possible. And if it becomes necessary, one should add regarding the glass tube you write about: there are those who place cotton in the tube and perform the *metzitzah* through the cotton. The reason for placing the cotton is that it performs a sterilization function and inhibits the bacteria passing through it. To clarify: my intention is that when one places a certain amount of cotton in the tube in such a way that it does not hinder the suction power, the breath of the one performing the *metzitzah* and likewise the blood being drawn will pass through the cotton, which is sterilized...

With a blessing of success for you and all your colleagues, may they live, in this holy work in all the aforementioned areas, from a state of proper health—health in physicality and health in spirituality,

**M. Schneerson**

... By the way: regarding a woman—the custom is to write "**all** limbs," since there is a dispute regarding this in *Bechoros* (45a). [Although there are those who strain to justify the version—*Ramach*].

## 5718

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Avreich Yehoshua, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter in which you write that you succeeded, with assistance, in bringing [the individual] into the covenant of Avraham Avinu, etc. It is surprising that the matter was apparently delayed until the necessary sum of money was collected, at a time when the Ministry of Religious Affairs responds to such matters and performs them at the Ministry’s expense. Indeed, you yourself mention in your letter a few words regarding the activities of this Ministry in this area.

Incidentally, since you write that the one being circumcised—who was already past Bar Mitzvah—was given "shlaf-getrank" before the circumcision, which means general anesthesia, this should have been clarified with a Rav who is a *moreh hora’ah*. This is because there is room to say that it is possible to use an injection in a nearby area (usually done in the back and the spinal cord), the effect of which is only the removal of the **sensation** of pain for a period of time, but it is not anesthesia; the person remains in control of all his senses—that is to say, he remains obligated in all the *mitzvos*. The differences between the two methods are understood.

Regarding what you wrote about proper education for those who have not yet been circumcised, even though they are already at an early age, and [regarding] their circumcision—what to prioritize—it is understood that one must do everything possible in both matters, and one should not delay one because of the other.

I trust that in addition to your activities in the aforementioned matters, you are participating in the activities of *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad*, and in a manner of "adding and increasing," as is the requirement of these days, regarding which it is said: "Whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

**To the Avreich Yehoshua, may he live:** Yozevich, Jerusalem.

**Since you write:** See also the following letter.

## 5069

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To my dear friend, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 15 Menachem Av, following the long interval, in which you write about the activities that have taken place in the meantime.

I have already written to several activists of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad that it is not advisable, for several reasons, to turn every activity into a separate organization that deviates from the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. For many reasons, it is necessary to centralize the activities, although it is understood that one can maintain the autonomy required by the nature of the activity, and even that which is required by the nature of the people actually involved and the relationships between them, until they can participate and work in full cooperation. However, one central authority, at least in a comprehensive sense, is beneficial for the activities in this field.

Since you mentioned in your previous letter regarding involvement with new immigrants who are already past the age of Bar Mitzvah, I am enclosing a copy of what I wrote to someone else regarding this, and it is worthwhile that you clarify the opinion of the local Rabbonim on this matter.

With blessings.

... Regarding what you write, that for the one being circumcised who is already past Bar Mitzvah, they gave him a "shlaf getrank" [sleeping potion] before the bris—the meaning of this is general anesthesia. You must clarify this with a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah*, as there is room to say that it is possible to use an injection in the adjacent area (usually this is done in the back and spinal cord), the effect of which is only the removal of the sensation of pain for a period of time, but it is not anesthesia, and the person remains in control of all his senses—meaning, he is obligated in all the mitzvos. The differences between the two methods are understood.

## 577

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Avreich, Yitzchak Meir, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, in which you ask about the contradiction between two accounts regarding the revelation of the Baal Shem Tov: 1) that it occurred on Chai Elul 5494, and 2) what is brought in the letters of the Baal Shem Tov (printed in *HaTamim*, Issue 1, section 577) that he would be revealed on the day after Thursday, Parshas Vayeishev.

Regarding this, the account that the Baal Shem Tov was revealed on Chai Elul 5494 is something we heard explicitly from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the name of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory. This is also printed in the *sicha* of 20 Kislev 5693, in the name of the great Chassid and great Tzaddik, the foundation of the world, etc., etc., R' Menachem Nachum of Chernobyl (printed in *Likutei Dibburim*, Vol. 2, section 2; see there). There is no contradiction here with what is written in the aforementioned letter, for there are several levels of revelation.

Since no further details have been received regarding this, it is understood that there is no room here for mere conjecture. However, it appears from several stories that Chai Elul 5494 was definitively the day of his revelation to the entirety of Klal Yisrael, as the Nasi of Yisrael, openly and in practice.

It is my hope that since you have approached me with such a question, you surely have set times for the study of Chassidus. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you increase in this, in accordance with the command of our Torah to "ascend in matters of holiness," and that the study be in accordance with the law—to understand and to grasp (*Magen Avraham* - *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, end of section 50).

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your move to the city of Cholon and the difficulties you have encountered concerning your grocery store business.

There are two points in your letter that may be the cause of the aforementioned difficulties, namely:

a) The concern of *hasagas gevul* (encroachment on another's livelihood). You should clarify this with a *rav moreh hora'ah* in Yisrael to see if there is a basis for this concern, and if so, in what manner it can be rectified.

b) You write that you sealed a door, and it is known from the *tzava'ah* (testament) of R' Yehudah HeChassid, section 20, that one should not completely seal a window or an opening.

There is room to say that once these two points are rectified, your situation will improve. May it be Hashem's will that you bring good news regarding the above, and in increasing your involvement in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, for whoever adds [to their efforts], they add to him [from Above].

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,
Secretary

***

 Regarding "that one should not seal": See also above, Vol. 13, Letter 4561, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

*) In a case that requires this sealing, there is an instruction from our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, which is known to *anash*: to make a hole in the seal using a metal tube (pipe), and even if it is subsequently sealed on both sides, one may then apply plaster over it.

## 5717

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 2 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the unfortunate events that have occurred to your daughters, may they live and be well, in recent years.

It is necessary to investigate as soon as possible, for it seems that in your shidduch with your wife, may she live and be well, there was some slight to the honor of a son or daughter of Yisrael. You must make every possible effort to clarify this, and also determine if there is room to ask for forgiveness, or at the very least, to ask for forgiveness in the presence of ten Yidden. Furthermore, check if any financial compensation or the like is applicable in this matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that you exert yourselves in the aforementioned investigation as required, and through this, all these matters will be removed, in accordance with what is said, "And your iniquity shall be removed and your sin atoned for," according to the explanation of our Alter Rebbe regarding the expression "to atone before Hashem," to provide satisfaction to His Creator.

It is appropriate to have your tefillin checked, and your wife, may she live and be well, should set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday morning and before lighting the Shabbos candles.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5713

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Tammuz, in which you write that you are serving in the army and are meticulous in observing the Torah and mitzvos, etc.

Surely you also look favorably upon others and influence your peers in this direction as well.

Regarding one who is in the army, in particular, he must do everything within his power to strengthen all matters pertaining to the army, and the personnel of the army included in this. It is understood that anyone who does otherwise is a traitor. This applies to all these matters, and even to a greater degree regarding the observance of Torah and mitzvos within the framework of the army. Since our Torah is a "Torah of life," and regarding its mitzvos it is said, "you shall live by them," any addition in this regard adds further life, strength, and courage to the army. Conversely, any deficiency, G-d forbid, in Torah and mitzvos leads to weakness and faint-heartedness, and compromises the security of the unit in which one is stationed, and through this, the security of the army as a whole. It is only because of the double and redoubled darkness of the galus that some are mistaken in this, since the results are not immediately apparent on the spot. Yet, this is a kal v'chomer: since at all times and in all places every single one of the children of Israel is commanded regarding Torah and mitzvos, how much more so is this true for those in the army, who were specifically commanded, "and your camp shall be holy."

At the same time, it is also understood that even though you are in the army under special conditions—as you write, that there is no assistance, and perhaps even worse than a lack of assistance, in observing the Torah and mitzvos—since the Giver of the Torah and the Mitzvos has commanded a special holiness in the army camp, He certainly provides the ability for each and every one to fulfill this, for the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and regards to your peers, may they live.

#### ***5713***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 293.

## 5717

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that you find it difficult to overcome a certain matter and do not know how to go about it:

It is already well known that the beginning of the rectification is, first and foremost, the effort to divert one's attention from the entire matter. This diversion of attention also means not fighting these thoughts, and not entering into any *shakla v’tarya* (debate) with the *yetzer hara* that is inciting and tempting you to think about this matter. Instead, you must invest your thoughts in the opposite subject—that is to say, in a matter of Torah, regarding which it is said, "Torah is light."

Furthermore, it is appropriate that you have memorized several chapters of Mishnayos, or at least one chapter of Tanya. Every weekday, before the morning *davening*, you should set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. After *davening*—and also on Shabbos and Yom Tov—you should recite the monthly *Tehillim* *shiur* (as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month). It is understood that you must be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*, and first and foremost, have complete regret for the past and guard your eyes from seeing or reading things that arouse and stimulate [the *yetzer hara*]. Be strong in your trust that the *Ribono shel Olam* has promised that "no one shall be cast away from Him." If, *chas v’shalom*, one even stumbles, sadness over this is ruled out, as is explained at length in the *Tanya*. Surely you have a regular *shiur* in this book; if you have not yet established one, you should establish a fixed time for learning it now. You will find there, in the index of subjects at the end of the *Tanya*, the chapters that discuss how it is forbidden to be in a state of sadness, and that even if one has stumbled, one must contemplate [the relevant concepts], etc.—see there.

May it be His will that you are able to share good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5175

By the Grace of Hashem
24 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Chaim Abba, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, as well as your previous one. Thank you to Hashem for the good news that there has been a minyan for Mincha and Maariv throughout the entire week. Surely, this success will provide you with the courage and energy to see to it that the shul is expanded even further, both in ruchniyus and in gashmiyus, both in quantity and in quality.

Regarding the nusach: Although "strife is hateful," the question is surprising, for as you yourself write, the mispalelim told you that this is a Lubavitcher shul. If so, there is no doubt as to which nusach should be used for davening.

Perhaps the entire doubt arose because there are not enough Siddurim of Nusach Lubavitch in the shul. If that is the case, then it is the fault of the shul’s administration, not the mispalelim.

It is worth noting the psak din of the later authorities that an individual may change from Nusach Ashkenaz to Nusach Sefard, but not vice versa. Furthermore, it is well known what the Tzemach Tzedek related: that his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe, selected the nusach from sixty different Siddurim before printing his own. From this, one understands that this nusach is "fine flour sifted from many variations." This is also consistent with the concept of the "Gate of Prayer" (Shaar HaTefillah), which includes all the gates of prayer, as brought in the introduction to Shaar HaKollel in the Siddur.

Actually, this matter pertains to the Rav of the shul, and I am writing to him regarding it. Since you touched upon the question in your letter, I am answering you as well. You will surely consult with the Rav, may he live. May it be the will of Hashem that all prayers be accepted amidst the prayers of all of Klal Yisrael.

With blessings for good news.

## 5716

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your brief letter regarding your activities was received some time ago. It is surprising that you write so infrequently, and even then, with such extreme brevity. May it be the will of Hashem that, since we have entered the days regarding which it is said, "Whoever adds, they add to him," you will also add to the aforementioned as much as is necessary. If only this would happen very soon. It is understood and obvious that you may write in any language you wish, or through an intermediary, provided that the letters are frequent and sufficiently detailed.

It is surprising that you did not write anything regarding the matter of the *nusach* of *davening*. This is a fundamental matter, and it is both the duty and the privilege of the *Rav* to ensure that it is in perfect order. This is especially true when the *Rav* has knowledge of *Toras HaChassidus* and its explanations regarding the matter of *tefillah*, which is like the spinal cord of a person. Consequently, it is understood how critical the *nusach* is. Since a question regarding this also reached me from the esteemed *R’ Chaim Abba* (may he live) *Weil*, in order not to repeat the matter, I am enclosing the response that was sent to him, along with the conclusion of my letter to him, as he will surely speak with you about this. I have written this only to emphasize once again that one must **not** turn this matter into a major dispute, nor even a minor one. In general, it is more correct to arrange matters simply—that is, to increase the number of *Siddurim* of *Nusach Ari* in the *beis medrash*. The main thing is to place one on the *amud*, according to the custom in several *batei knessios* where there is a large, special *Siddur* for the *amud* (attached with a cord and chain, or the like). If this is in *Nusach Ari*, it will establish its place, and eventually, people will become accustomed to it. May you bring good news regarding all of the above, in addition to good tidings regarding matters of *Torah* study.

With blessings.

## 5717

By the Grace of Hashem, 24 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, [Name], known as Dr. Ullman,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter along with the two articles you enclosed. As you requested, I have reviewed the monograph, and I must say that your explanation regarding the method to prevent immunity against medicinal drugs is most compelling. My only wonder is why this approach has not been adopted and implemented until now in accordance with this logic. Even though there are many such phenomena in the history of science, the past should serve as a lesson for the future, and the number of such occurrences should be steadily decreasing.

Understand that my intention here is not to express mere surprise, but to suggest that perhaps research has already been conducted in the direction you propose and actions have been taken, although I am certain that before publishing the article, you researched and investigated this as thoroughly as possible.

Incidentally, although this is not my field, I noticed in the tables of your monograph that you cite medications and treatment methods used 150 years ago or more. This is also surprising, for in either case, over such a long period, they have surely been used many times, with variations from the original methods and refinements in their application. It is impossible that there would not be innovations, whether for better or for worse. Since the purpose of the table is not a history of medical science, but rather practical utility regarding the medicine and the treatment, one should utilize only the most recent results. This is similar to the principle in our Torah—to distinguish—which is a logical rule: the halacha follows the later authorities, since they have seen the words of those who preceded them. It is understood that all of the above is written as the opinion of someone for whom this is not his field, and merely as a remark from an outsider.

With blessings for success in your research, in your work in the healing of the soul (through education based on the purity of holiness), and in the healing of the body.

With respect,

#### ***5717***

**Dr. Ullman:** Additional letters to him appear above in 5708, and in the notes indicated there.

## 5718

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Menachem Av, in which you write that you lack the quality of *moach shalit al halev* (the mind ruling over the heart), and that you become emotionally agitated by every small and large matter, etc.

Know that this entire situation stems from the fact that your belief in *Hashgacha Pratis* is only in a manner of *makif* (encompassing). For when it enters into one’s *pnimiyus* (internalized consciousness), it is understood that there is no room for such agitation, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 25.

It would be appropriate to keep the words "before the King," mentioned at the beginning of Chapter 41 of *Tanya* (up to page 56b), engraved in your memory. Whenever you feel yourself beginning to become agitated, contemplate this in your thoughts, or even articulate the words.

I trust you are keeping up with the *shiurei Chitas* (Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya) and are not drawing yourself into seeking out too many complex accounts. Since "G-d made man upright," it is his duty to walk in this straight path—the path of *Toras Hashem*—to study it with *hasmadah* (diligence) and *shekidah* (assiduity), and to fulfill His *mitzvos* with *hiddur* (beauty/meticulousness). Do not busy yourself with superficial "accounts of the soul" or "psychological analyses," etc. As the saying of our Sages goes, "You have labored and you have found." May it be His will that you influence your friends in this manner as well.

#### ***5718***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 440, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 5719

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write about your state of mind, the doctors' opinions, and that you are suffering greatly, etc.

It is truly surprising, for you are at a young age and have already merited to engage in the field of proper chinuch—that is, to bring the hearts of the children of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. From this, it is understood—and it is also simple—that if even flesh and blood feels gratitude and wants to do everything in their power for the benefit of one who brings their children’s hearts closer to them, then how much more so our Father in Heaven, who is the essence of good and is all-powerful, certainly bestows blessing and success upon those who strive to bring the hearts of His children closer to Him. And if "Hashem is with me," it is simple that "I will not fear; what can man do to me?"—as our Torah, the Torah of life, informs us.

It is understood that every person is subject to changes, including changes in their state of mind. But it is obvious that one should not magnify or exaggerate this. An unpleasant state of mind is merely a passing thing. However, in order for it to pass quickly, the aforementioned contemplation is helpful, even for a short while—especially when you remember one of the foundations of our faith, which is explained so beautifully in the teachings of Chassidus: the concept of Hashgacha Pratis, in its literal sense, that the Creator of the world watches over each and every person in all their affairs, and their details, and the details of their details.

It is my hope that after the chinuch you have received, these few lines—few in quantity—will suffice to set you upon the truth: that we are in a world about which the Creator of the world says, "And G-d saw that it was good," just as our great teacher, our Rabbeinu the Rambam, explained at length in his specific books on this matter. It is just that a person should not seek out many complications that obscure reality and distort the truth.

The conclusion from the above is that you should cease dwelling on your state of mind, etc., and your faith in the Creator of the world, who watches over each and every one, will bring vitality, energy, and joy into all your affairs. You will live a simple life, without tangled thoughts, and you will be happy in the path of Torah and mitzvos.

I await good news regarding all the above.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5723

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs and conducting his business with integrity,
R' Yaakov, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding meeting with the leaders of the Nusach Ashkenaz shul concerning a merger, and how far one can go regarding the *nusach*: it is self-understood that this must be safeguarded. For *tefillah* is the primary purpose of a *beis hatefillah*. Just as in any *Chassidishe* shul, when someone wishes to daven **his** *nusach* **biyechidus**, that is a private matter. And if, **by chance**, someone davens a different *nusach* in front of the *amud*, even though many are unhappy with it due to the **din**, nevertheless, *mipnei hashalom* (for the sake of peace), it is overlooked. However, on a permanent basis, the *nusach* must be Lubavitch. Especially since, according to *din*, one may change from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Nusach Sefard* and to *Nusach Ari*, but not the reverse.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that as we approach the days of mercy, when we begin to say every day, "I seek Your countenance, Hashem" (which is connected to "Seek My countenance"), we should strengthen and deepen the matter of *tefillah*. This is the connection between Yidden and Hakadosh Baruch Hu, and it is the channel and vessel for the fulfillment of a person’s needs, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

With the blessing of a good Shabbos, and may the blessing continue for the entire month and for all the days ahead, for good, speedily and in our days.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***5723***

**R' Yaakov, may he live:** Katz, Chicago. Additional letters to him – above 5723, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 5717

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Tammuz—which was delayed somewhat in transit—in which you write about the situation in your family life and your relationship with your wife, may she live.

It is already well-known what our Sages have taught regarding one’s wife, the wife of one’s youth, as it is written: "Can the wife of one’s youth be despised?" Especially when Hashem has blessed you with children who are being educated in the path of Torah and mitzvos, it is understood from all this that the matter of a *get* (divorce), *chas v'shalom*, is to be rejected. It is nothing more than an absolute last resort, only after one has exerted the greatest possible effort to bring about peace, in accordance with the instruction of our Torah—the Torah of life and the Torah of peace.

As you describe in your letter, it appears that you have significant influence over your wife, may she live. However, it seems that until now, due to your preoccupation with your business and the like, you have not exerted yourself in this, or at the very least, you have not engaged in this after the necessary contemplation regarding the appropriate methods for this influence; therefore, you have not been as successful. Based on the above, every effort and exertion is worthwhile, especially since, as mentioned, through this you will also draw her closer and bring her into a life according to Torah, step by step—not only for the sake of not separating, but gradually, through a change in her perspectives as well.

It is understood that there are specific situations according to Torah that necessitate separation, *chas v'shalom*, but all of this is only taken into account after there is clear proof that it is impossible to change the situation.

When you write your name and your mother’s name, as well as the name of your wife and her mother, and your children, may they live, I will mention them at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*.

It is appropriate that you observe the practice of reciting the monthly *Tehillim*—as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month—every day after morning *davening*, and on every weekday, before *davening*, you should set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5720

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you and your family, *shichyu*, through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Yosef Halevi Weinberg, who also writes to me that, unfortunately, your financial situation has not been the best of late.

The advice of our Sages, of blessed memory, regarding such a situation is well known: one should give more *tzedakah*, and in a greater measure—and whoever increases is praiseworthy. The *tzedakah* that one resolves to give can be given in smaller installments if it is difficult to give all at once. The appropriate time to set this aside—whether by writing a check or placing cash in a designated place—is each weekday before putting on *tefillin* and *davening*. When one does this with strong *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach—who gave us these *mitzvos* and promised us regarding them that "you shall live by them"—it brings life. In a tangible way, one sees the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in the areas where one is in need, and through the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah* in particular, one sees this in the matter of *parnassah*. I will be pleased to hear good news that you are doing this and are seeing the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in what you require.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5728

By the Grace of G-d, 28 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Committee of Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I sent a telegram yesterday stating my opinion that all the funds the village will receive back from the Agency regarding the electricity installation should be invested in the construction of a housing project in Kfar Chabad. This housing project is essential for the development of the village. If those interested in the village’s development build houses individually, it will surely be without order, and who knows how long it will take. This is in contrast to building a housing project, where one can create a suitable plan according to the village’s boundaries, in a way that the houses will be compatible with one another, etc. As soon as they begin construction, they should publicize this in an announcement, stating that all interested parties must register for the apartments being built—naturally, provided they are suitable for the spirit that must prevail within Kfar Chabad, in accordance with the will of its founder and director, my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

I arrived at this decision some time ago, but I did not see a way to obtain the sum required to begin an entire housing project. The matter of the funds being returned is also an additional indication that our holy Nasi is stirring and awakening [us] regarding all the affairs of the village, with success beyond the natural order.

I also wrote in the telegram that, in my opinion, this should be started as soon as possible. For if those interested see that matters are becoming complicated, there is a risk that they will settle elsewhere.

It is possible that there are arguments for how to utilize these funds for other purposes, but it is understood that the benefit of the many, as mentioned above, takes precedence over the benefit of the individual. It is also understood that matters requiring small sums will surely have several opportunities for funding, unlike a matter that requires a significant amount. It is also understood that for matters where there is hope of obtaining assistance from various funds or through volunteers, these funds should not be utilized; this is not the case for building private apartments, where there is no hope of receiving a budget from funds and offices.

Furthermore, I should note that in the above, I did not intend to finance the entire budget of the housing project, for certainly several offices assist in the establishment of housing projects. This is especially true since, as I believe, Kfar Chabad has rights as a settlement not far from the border—meaning, not only are the development offices interested in this, but also the security offices. However, these offices only assist with a portion of the budget, and I believe less than half, and the returned funds should be utilized for the portion of the budget that falls upon the village.

It is simple that, eventually, the money will return to the village committee’s treasury (in full, or at least in its large part), for the apartments being built will **not** be given as a gift, and then there will be room for further discussion on how to use these funds.

2) Regarding the concern that building a housing project might change the Agency’s attitude toward the village as a whole—and apparently their intention is not for the good, since its status as an agricultural settlement would be diminished—in practice, this makes little difference. For the areas upon which the housing project will be built, it is understood that they cannot remain empty; rather, there would be dilapidated houses there, as there are now. Consequently, they would rent or sell them out of necessity to those who are not as suitable for the village’s requirements, and surely the Agency’s attitude would be further diminished because they would be neither farmers nor suitable in all that is required. This is not the case with the aforementioned plan.

3) Based on the above, it is also understood regarding the location of the housing project, that it must be in a way that does not detract from the plots designated for agriculture. As I believe, according to the map, the most suitable place is in the old village. If, for this purpose, it is necessary to remove the dilapidated houses, well, eventually they must be removed anyway. However, as mentioned above, the removal would have been done in piecemeal fashion, and consequently with additional expense and without a general plan, etc., which is not the case with the aforementioned [plan].

4) I believe I have already written several times that it is essential for many reasons (and not only because of the Agency’s attitude) that the number of farmers not be reduced, and that it even increase as much as possible. It is a wonder that no proposal is heard from them regarding the areas in the vicinity of the village—how many of them are suitable for this purpose, and in what way it is possible to acquire them and add them to the village’s area. This, and matters like this, should be the primary occupation of the village committee. In addition to the reasoning that this is a primary matter, when the village develops, new sources of income and livelihood will be added, in a way that will diminish the source of friction that leads to discord, as is known from our Sages: "When the barley is finished in the jar, strife knocks at the door," and from the negative you hear the positive.

5) It is self-understood that the development of the village must be not only in material matters but also in spiritual matters. This is certainly true regarding educational matters, which require the best educational forces that can be obtained. It is worth the effort and even toil to obtain them, especially since, according to the situation in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily, there is a great shortage of teachers, and especially since Chabad has special requirements regarding education...

6) Regarding what I wrote about the negotiations—if there will be any, whether through Mr. Shazar, may he live, or without him—I spoke about this with Mr. Shazar, may he live, at length during his visit here. He promised that in matters such as these, he will not only dedicate his time to being involved in the substance of the matter, but he will also dedicate his attention and time to safeguarding the point that Kfar Chabad, in **all** its affairs, must be directed toward the name and will of its founder, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This is in addition to the fact that one must certainly be careful not to infringe upon his connection and affection for all the village’s affairs and not to act without him, especially in a matter he spoke about explicitly.

7) Regarding their question of whether to participate in a fundraising campaign (abroad) with any political party or the like, the doubt in this is also a wonder, at a time when they know that Chabad’s affairs have been non-partisan and above-partisan for hundreds of years, and this is also one of the foundations of its success. Why, all of a sudden, is such a question proposed?

With a blessing for success in all the affairs of Kfar Chabad, in accordance with the will and the direction, awaiting good tidings in all the above.

P.S.
All of the above is in confirmation of and in response to the letters from the 5th and 17th of Tammuz—may it soon be turned into joy and gladness—and it is a wonder that since then there has been not only no detailed news, but no news at all. This was written on the 21st of Menachem Av.

## 5717

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and industrious individual, engaged in communal needs, R' Dovid, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 7 Menachem Av and the one preceding it. My official response on behalf of the Vaad has been sent in a separate envelope, and I am certain you will provide further clarification should there be those who require it.

It is naturally distressing that in all matters concerning the village (such as the farbrengen you write about), there is a lack of advance preparation, even though at the beginning of the year it is already known that on such-and-such a day there is an opportunity to farbreng. Past years have already demonstrated just how necessary preparation is. The same applies to other village matters, such as the issue of names, loans, etc., where only after reality forces the matter onto the agenda—and someone wants to take crooked paths—do we find it necessary to fix the situation, etc., and then discuss it. By doing so, not only is more energy wasted than is necessary, but in the vast majority of cases, something fixed at the last minute does not turn out as well as it could.

May it be Hashem's will that, at the very least, from here on out, plans will be made well in advance.

Since we are entering the days of the month of Elul, you will surely begin discussing the month of Tishrei and its affairs immediately. You should ensure (baavarnen) that such-and-such matters do not become like "a pot belonging to partners" [i.e., neglected due to lack of individual responsibility], by appointing specific individuals responsible for specific matters. Most importantly, the person responsible must accept this responsibility upon himself. Even then, the Vaad should oversee the manner in which he fulfills his role, etc.

Your proposal regarding the twenty percent has been accepted.

With blessings for proper health for you and your family, may they live, and for success in your role for the benefit of all matters of Kfar Chabad—their true benefit, in accordance with the will of its founder, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—and with peace of mind,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**R' Dovid:** Bravman, Kfar Chabad. Further letters to him—above, Vol. 13, p. 405, and in the references noted there.

## 5,390

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Mr. Yisrael, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 19 Menachem Av, in which you write about the visit of the young men, the students of the Yeshiva, Shalom Dov Shemtov and Shmuel Pesach Bagomulsky, and about the dedication shown in fulfilling their shlichus.

My satisfaction is twofold: I am pleased not only with the news that they are performing their shlichus faithfully, but also that they have found Jews who know how to appreciate this and who respond to the call of this shlichus. This is especially true regarding the fact that it has led to matters of *maaseh b'fo'al* in daily life. I hope that, in accordance with the words of the Mishnah regarding "a good eye toward the affairs of others," you will see to it that your influence is utilized to the fullest extent throughout the entire area to spread *Toras Chaim* and *mitzvos*, regarding which the Torah says, "and he shall live by them." Through this, you will also bring about an *tosefes bracha* from Hashem Yisbarach in the area, in the things that one needs in life *k'fshuto*—children, life, and sustenance. By doing so, you will provide *chizuk* for Jews wherever they may be, whether in the Diaspora or in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days. For *kol Yisrael areivim zeh bazeh* (all of Israel are responsible for one another). It is well known that the interpretation and hint of this statement is that all Jews are *areiv* (responsible) for one another, that all Jews are *me'urav* (intermingled) with one another, and that all Jews are *areiv* (sweet) to one another. This is achieved by spreading Yiddishkeit and maintaining Yiddishkeit in ever-larger and broader circles of our people, Israel.

I conclude with my wish that you may be able to report good tidings regarding all that was mentioned above, and from time to time, add to these good tidings.

With blessing.

For the Children of Israel were commanded regarding all matters: "In all your ways, know Him"—meaning, to make them holy. And the command of the *Ribono shel Olam* is ultimately fulfilled, and "anyone who stands to be sanctified is considered as sanctified," especially since Above, the past, present, and future are as one. Consequently—*Ori V'Yishi* [my light and my salvation] in all these matters.

Awaiting good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5717

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from 17 Menachem Av was received. May it be His will that just as you bring good news regarding the improvement in your wife’s (tichye) condition, you will soon bring news that she has returned to full health, and likewise with good tidings in all the matters you write about.

Regarding what you wrote about your desire to ascend in the feeling of the light of Chassidus, etc., but that you feel far from this:

Heaven forbid to say such a thing. As is explained in Tanya, "the matter is very close to you." If this is true for everyone, then how much more so for one whom Divine Providence has placed in the beautiful portion of drawing the hearts of Bnei Yisrael to our Father in Heaven—a source of immense *nachas ruach* Above that cannot be measured. The magnitude of the blessing and success that is bestowed upon those who strive in this is understood, provided they strengthen and expand the conduit and the vessels to receive them; and this is well understood.

As for the path to become more connected to Chassidus and its matters, and to become unified with them, this has already been explained in many books, *maamarim* of *Torah Or*, and *sichos* of our holy Rebbes. You should study them, and may Hashem grant you success.

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about—please provide their names (and their mother’s names)—at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukullehah, navgam, zya*. May it be His will that you bring good news in this as well.

With blessings.

## 5717

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Many thanks for your two letters of the 15th and 17th of Tammuz. It is surprising that there has been a gap since then, but I am sure you will make up for it at the next opportunity.

Regarding what you wrote about the incident in a certain place concerning the observance of Shabbos: I believe I have already written—or perhaps it was to the administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad—that although visits to *moshavim* and *kibbutzim* that are currently not religious are necessary, as evidenced by the most sublime fruits and results of this work, it is understood that they require special caution. This is clearly seen in the aforementioned incident. Therefore, an individual should not rely on his own personal assessment, but rather consult with others who have experience in such matters. There are many members of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad who are knowledgeable in this, and "in a multitude of counselors there is salvation."

Regarding what you wrote about what your father told you, that there is gossip, etc.—without entering into a debate as to whether the gossip is justified or not, it is written, "Remove from yourself a froward mouth." It is worthwhile to endeavor that those who travel to such places be married men. Perhaps it is also generally worthwhile that on every trip, at least one person should be more mature, as this adds to the gravity of the matter.

As mentioned, the activities you have done until now, and which you will surely do in the future, are sublime, and none of us can estimate the good that will sprout in the future, in addition to what we already see. However, as with all matters of those who fear the word of Hashem, one must know that they are being watched with "seven eyes," and many are even looking for a pretext, etc. This is in addition to the well-known statement of our Sages, that if an ordinary person has a stain on his garment, it is of no consequence, whereas for a *talmid chacham*, it is different.

It is understood that all of the above is directed to all your colleagues and to all those who are involved in the aforementioned outreach. You will surely bring this to their attention, and you will discuss all of the above together.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

## 5395

B”H, 29 Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, man of many accomplishments, R’ Yehoshua, may he live.

Following a delay, your letter was received, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within it, which will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It was a pleasure for me to read that the situation in England, and in Europe in general, also proves the immense benefit of disseminating *Chassidus* in Yiddish as well. Under separate cover, I have sent you *Tanya*, Part I, which has been published in Yiddish. Also enclosed is a transcript of one of the *sichos* delivered to young *Bnei Yisrael* (from the age of five or six years old). These are fundamental concepts in the teachings of *Chassidus*—the inner dimension of Torah—except that our holy Rebbes clothed these foundations in language understandable even to young children, while simultaneously including the entire concept within them. Indeed, the *tzaddikim* are like their Creator, and as is known, the parable in the *Midrash* regarding "small mirrors" and "large mirrors" explains the *Tzimtzum* of the *Ein Sof, Baruch Hu*. This very example proves that **everything** that is seen in the large mirrors is also seen in the small mirrors; nothing is missing. The same applies to the aforementioned and similar matters. May it be the will of Hashem that knowledge increase in *Yisrael*, and may we merit, in the immediate future, the fulfillment of the prophecy, "For they shall all know Me, from the smallest of them to the greatest of them."

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

## 5796

By the Grace of Hashem,
Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, R’ A. Shklavsky, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

I confirm receipt of your letter in which you write the main points regarding the Chabad shul and the difficulties concerning the minyan, etc., and that one is in need of abundant mercies (*rachamim rabim*).

It is clear that the matter of *rachamim rabim* exists, as we say in our davening every day, "In Your abundant mercies, have mercy upon us." One must only strengthen the *tzinor* (conduit) and the *keilim* (vessels) to receive them in practical matters down here. And what is a better *kli* than a shul where one learns Torah, which unites Torah and tefillah? It follows, then, that this depends only on the *askanim* (communal activists) of the shul and beis medrash—that they, for their part, should do a little, and then the matter will be in order.

This is similar to what is told at the beginning of Midrash Shir HaShirim and Koheles regarding the bringing of a large stone to the Beis HaMikdash. It was not within the capacity of one person to bring it, yet it was required of the person to help with one finger, and the rest was already accomplished from Above through "His angels, who do His word." This is the way of things in every place and at every time, even if it is done through a different *levush* (garment). As is known, an angel does not necessarily have to be something that arrives with two white wings; it can also be an *malach*—in the literal sense, a *shaliach* (messenger)—and "the Omnipresent has many messengers." This is especially true in a good cause upon which the merit of the many depends.

Since you have merited to be among the leading *askanim* of this shul and beis medrash, it is certain that not only will you yourself act in this, but you will also ensure that all who are able to act in this matter will do so. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success.

I await good news regarding all that has been mentioned, and with blessings for a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*.

## 5717

B"H, 1 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven, engaged in communal needs, R' Yaakov Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a long hiatus, I received your letter from 14 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the proposal to utilize students from the higher grades to teach students in the lower grades for several hours a day.

In general, this is a sound idea. It is evident that the very fact that trust is placed in the students of the higher grade, elevating them to the rank of teacher and mashpia—at least for a few hours—adds to their energy, persistence, and diligence in their own studies at the institution. This is in addition to deepening their hiskashrus to the institution and its affairs.

Even though there is room to argue that, being inexperienced, they might not succeed as well in the matters of instruction and education during the initial period, experience from other places in similar situations shows that the enthusiasm of such students, due to their appointment to a responsible task, compensates for what they lack in knowledge of educational and pedagogical methods.

It is understood that after all that has been said, not all students of the higher grades are suitable for this. For in addition to good conduct and a sense of responsibility, there must be some talent for maintaining discipline, etc. Likewise, one must consider the concern that they might interpret the aforementioned action as the institution wishing to exploit them for its own benefit, without considering the benefit of the students themselves. Therefore, it is necessary that all members of the administration of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Melbourne discuss this proposal in its entirety, and subsequently regarding each student in accordance with his character and the nature of his soul. But as stated above, one should endeavor to implement this, as it is of great benefit to the student—even more so than the direct benefit to the Yeshiva. It is understood that you have the permission and the right to share what is written above with the other members of the administration.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of the farbrengen and its format, it is appropriate that you speak about this face-to-face with the leaders of the farbrengens, with each one individually, without any strangers present. You should awaken them to the point you wrote about, and they should discuss it together, for the goal of each of the aforementioned individuals is uniform: to fulfill the instruction of our holy Nesi’im to spread the wellsprings outward.

Since you do not mention anything regarding your health, etc., I assume everything is in order.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned matters, as well as in your personal affairs, and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

#### ***5717***

**R' Yaakov Eliezer:** Herzog, Melbourne. Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 14, p. 450, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 5798

## 5717

B"H, 1 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 21st of Menachem Av. It is certainly regrettable, as indicated in your letter, that the director of the Reshet did not maintain contact with the Reshet students throughout the vacation period. Although one does not cry over the past, it is my hope that they will consult with one another in good time regarding how to remain in contact with them during future vacation periods. This applies not only to the long summer vacation, but also to how to influence the students during their time off from school throughout the academic year—that is, on Shabbos, Yomim Tovim, and the like.

Regarding what you wrote about having studied for the appropriate courses but not attending the examinations: even after reading the reasons you provide, your failure to attend is entirely incomprehensible. Surely there is no room for harm in doing so; it is possible you would have succeeded in some of the exams, and perhaps even all of them, as is evidently the case in many instances. As for what you write regarding your poor memory, it is understood that this is nothing more than a tactic of the *yetzer hara*, whose job it is to cause a person to fall into laziness, for which it seeks out various—and even strange—excuses. You should certainly attend the upcoming examinations, and in the meantime, do what is necessary to succeed, while completely dismissing the thought that you are incapable, that your memory is lacking, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about the affairs of the Reshet and your role there: regarding such matters it is said, "In the **multitude** of counselors there is salvation." Since a person is biased and close to his own affairs, once one has presented his own reasons and justifications, one should rely on the decision of the majority, for the welfare of the institutions is dear to them as well. Even if you are only just beginning your role, with the proper attention and contemplation of the responsibility involved, things will be rectified. It is difficult to provide guidance from a distance, especially when it is unnecessary, as mentioned above.

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your work—which is *meleches shamayim* (work of Heaven)—through which there will also be an increase in the success of your personal affairs and those of your entire household, *shichyu*. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Whoever adds, they add to him." With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.
