## 5717

B"H, 1 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a hiatus, I was pleased to receive your letter of 22 Menachem Av, and even more pleased to read in it that many details have been settled and arranged. I am certain that this in itself will further strengthen the conviction that the other details, too, have no substance; the less one thinks about them and the less attention one pays to them, the sooner they will pass. For in general, they have no reality (substance), especially since we are in the days when we recite twice daily, "Hashem is my light and my salvation; whom shall I fear?" Through strengthening one’s bitachon to the fullest extent—without any discussions, pilpulim, or explanations, but rather simply, as it is, that Hashem Yisbarach is the Master of the entire world and all things in the world depend on Him, and that He is "my light and my salvation"—it follows that "whom shall I fear?" There is nothing to be afraid of and nothing to dwell upon.

I hope that, in accordance with the ruling of the Mishnah that peace is the vessel that holds the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam, and that shalom bayis is one of the highest virtues within peace itself, your shalom bayis is also in order. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings, may it be written and sealed for a good year.

## 5717

B"H, 2 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that you are sometimes distracted by confusing thoughts during davening.

The advice for this is to daven specifically from a Siddur, and in a state of purity.

You also write regarding your hasmadah (diligence in study), which is not at its full potential.

The advice for this is to contemplate the meaning of the words of davening, at least according to their literal sense, and also to keep engraved in your memory the concept mentioned at the beginning of Chapter 41 of Tanya, that Hashem stands over him, etc., and examines his kidneys and heart, etc. And when you feel a weakness in your hasmadah, contemplate this concept once again.

Regarding what you ask about the reasons for Jewish customs and practices, which, according to your letter, people ask you about:

You should turn regarding this to the Rabbonim of anash in your vicinity, and they will instruct you. But it is understood that it is not your primary task to search for reasons and to answer questions, but rather to study with hasmadah and shekidah in the revealed Torah and Chassidus, and our Sages of blessed memory have said: "You have labored and you have found."

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

## 5743

B"H, 2 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding your question in your aforementioned letter as to whether you should write all the details... it is surprising that there is even a doubt or a question about this, for in such matters, the more one elaborates and specifies, the more praiseworthy it is. And regarding what you wrote about not "touching" anyone—I believe I have already written precisely about the statement of our Sages that the Torah speaks in clean language, the example being the account in the Ark of Noach. This is not the case, however, regarding laws and instructions; as in *Parshas Shemini*, etc., a clear statement is made: "the clean and the unclean." This, too, is an instruction for us: that in a matter concerning law and instruction, such as the case at hand, there is no issue of "touching" anyone, but rather the faithful fulfillment of one's duty. And this is understood.

Regarding what you wrote, that upon moving into your new home you have incurred debts, etc.—it is known that even the order of the Torah is itself Torah. Two statements in this regard appear in proximity in our Torah: "Whoever engages in building becomes impoverished," and together with this, on that very same page, just before it: "Any person who does not have land is not a person." The *Tosafos* there explains that this refers to building a house upon it (as is brought in *Chassidus*—"Any person who does not have a house"). That is to say, one should not be impressed by the fact that one becomes impoverished for the time being. For this is *avodah*, etc., because of the completeness and the addition that comes through this, despite the matter that is burdensome for the moment, for in the end, it will pass. May it be the will of Hashem that the matters of the completeness of the home be fulfilled in spirituality as well, as explained in the *Maamar* titled *Mizmor Shir Chanukas* in *Siddur* and in *Likutei Torah*, and with additional explanation in the *Hemshech* of 5636, and elsewhere.

With blessings for good news, detailed in all that was mentioned, and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

#### ***5743***

**I have already written:** See above, Vol. 12, Letter 4,272, and the references in the footnotes there. See above, 5,330.

## 5717

B"H, 2 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, regarding your questions:

1) Why are those who believe in Hashem, His Torah, and His mitzvos so few?

It is already stated in our holy Torah that "you are the **fewest** of all peoples." The creation of the world is according to the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam, as the Zohar states regarding the verse "Bereishis bara" — that it means "with wisdom." He, His wisdom, and His knowledge are one. It is written, "Can you find the depths of Elokus?" and this is explained at length in the Rambam and many other places. Furthermore, there is some explanation of this point in various sources, including the Rambam’s introduction to his commentary on the Mishnah, near the end of the introduction, where he writes: "There remains one question here... why did the Ribono shel Olam create all people... when we see that the majority of people..." See there.

The central point here is that quality is of greater value than quantity; that is to say, a superior quality residing in a small quantity outweighs the greatest quantity if its quality is inferior.

2) Who is the person called a rasha?

See the Tanya, beginning with Chapter 1 and onwards, as indicated in the subject index at the end of the book. It is understood that there is a rasha for that moment only, and when he does teshuvah, he rectifies it to the point that it is possible for his deliberate sins to become like merits, etc.

3) What is the emunah that a person must have?

The text of "Ani Maamin" is well known, and these matters are brought in many places, and the text is also printed in the Siddurim.

4) The proof that there is a Creator of the world is not understood.

The proof for this is very simple. It is a kal v'chomer: when a person sees a printed book with several pages, there is no doubt in his mind that it was created by an intelligent being who arranged the letters, printed them, etc., and that it did not come about by chance—that a bottle of ink was overturned on paper, and through the spilling of the ink, it happened that shapes of letters, lines, and pages were formed in a way that explains an intellectual concept. Anyone who would say that it happened by chance through the spilling of ink from a bottle is not in the category of a rational human being, not even in the category of a small child. How much more so is this true regarding the world, which possesses a wondrous order thousands upon thousands and myriads of times greater than the order of a book with several pages. It is a great wonder that you would even ask this.

May it be the will of Hashem that you abandon the path of searching and questioning, and instead study with diligence and persistence our holy Torah—Toras Chaim—which gives life even in the literal sense, as it is written, "Happy are you in this world, and it shall be good for you in the World to Come." May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you are aware of the *Chitas* (Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya) lessons; you should keep them, at the very least, from now on.

## 5717

B"H, 2 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter, in which you write that you are at a crossroads and cannot decide whether to continue in the yeshiva and live a life of hardship, etc., and you ask for my advice on this matter:

It is obvious that you must continue your studies in the yeshiva. As for your conclusion that this means a life of hardship—even if we assume you will not earn a large salary or the like—it is clear to any person of reason that happiness in life does not depend on a large salary, but rather on health, inner satisfaction, and the like. There are many people with large salaries who would gladly trade them for a bit more inner satisfaction and a bit more substance in their empty lives, as is clearly evident. Especially since it is a fundamental principle of our faith that the One who gave the Torah and commanded the mitzvos is the very same One who created the world and continues to lead it in practice even now, and He is the One who sustains and provides for all. The conclusion is therefore clear.

May it be His will that you not be enticed by the words of the *yetzer*, that you walk securely on your path—the path of the King, the King of kings—and that you study with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* both the *Torah HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*.

With the blessing of *Ksivah V'Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
You surely know of the three daily *shiurim* of *Chitas* (Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya), and you should keep them, at the very least, from this point forward.

## 5716

5716

By the Grace of Hashem, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, after midday – Parshas Ki Yeipalei Mimcha Davar, etc., "And you shall arise and go up." 5716, Brooklyn.

To all participants of the first annual convention of the
Hitachdus Talmidei Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
of the United States,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the good news regarding the first convention of the Hitachdus Talmidei Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch of the United States, and its scheduling for Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Shoftim, and the days preceding and following it.

The Gemara in Sanhedrin states that a gathering of the righteous is beneficial for them and beneficial for the world. And the verse says, "And your people are all righteous."

And even though there are those among the Jewish people who have committed sins—as the Zohar asks in Parshas Lech Lecha regarding this verse—nevertheless, every person of Israel is full of mitzvos, as Chazal have made known. And it is explained in the teachings of Chassidus that a *tzaddik* is called such on account of *tzedakah*, and all mitzvos are called *tzedakah*, as it is written, "For all Your mitzvos are *tzedek* (righteousness)."

For the essence of *tzedakah* is to revive the spirit of the lowly, the pauper who has nothing of his own.

- Similarly, the illumination of the revelation of His divinity, may He be blessed, below among the lowly—which is the concept of a "dwelling place in the lower worlds"—is *tzedakah*.

And this dwelling place in the lower worlds is created through mitzvos.

And "fortunate are the righteous, for their closeness brings peace to the world as well," and is beneficial to the world.

For the goal of a convention of those who fulfill mitzvos is to consult and assist one another in matters of Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim* upon which the world stands, and the convention and consultation regarding this is a great foundation and essential principle.

As explained by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the *maamar* beginning with the words "It is stated... he who is small is great," and how the agreement of the many carries great strength, and the connection of the many is an *is'arusa d'lesata* (an arousal from below) that reaches up to the highest of heights.

And in the language of the Alter Rebbe:

Through the inclusion and connection, there is drawn down from the most supernal place, from the place that encompasses the entire *seder hishtalshelus* equally.

Therefore, nothing will be withheld from them, and nothing will be "too wonderful" (*yeipalei*) for them—from such a convention.

For, as mentioned above, this *is'arusa d'lesata* reaches up to the highest heights, "And you shall arise and go up"—a true journey without limitation—through which one reaches the place that He will choose, the place of true choice, where there is no obstacle.

May it be the will of Hashem that the resolutions of the convention and its results will increase Torah and mitzvos in the lower worlds, both their revealed and inner dimensions, through the dissemination of the wellsprings outward.

And may each one of us, and all our families, within the entirety of the Jewish people, be written and sealed for a good and sweet year.

"For He will choose our inheritance for us, the pride of Yaakov which He loved forever."

With blessings for success in actual *avodah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5708

5708

B"H, 5 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Menachem Av, in which you write that you lack a daily routine, find yourself in a state of worry, despair, and sadness, etc., and do not know how to return to Hashem, etc.

This matter has already been addressed in many holy seforim, and in particular in the books and maamarim of Chassidus, among them the holy Tanya, as indicated in the subject index at the end of the holy Tanya. However, like other parts of Torah, it is absorbed and acquired more effectively through the bond of friends, which implies that you should learn Tanya, at the very least, with another person. There are several avreichim and elders in the holy city of Jerusalem with whom you can set a regular shiur for this purpose. They are people who can explain the difficult points in these seforim should you require it. The words of the Mitteler Rebbe, son of the Alter Rebbe, are well known: when two people speak together about matters of Torah and avodah, it is as if two nefesh elokis are working against one nefesh habahamis, and the rest is understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news of a noticeable improvement in all the aforementioned. There is nothing that can stand before one’s will, and according to the declaration of Chazal: "If you have labored and not found, do not believe."

Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim of Chitas (Chumash, Tehillim, Tanya); at the very least, you should maintain them from this point forward.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5717

5717

B"H, 5 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter of 25-27 Av, in which you write regarding the young woman... who has converted to another religion, Heaven forbid, and there are those who attribute this to witchcraft and the like, etc.

You should dismiss from your minds any explanation of such matters through witchcraft, as this weakens the *hishtadlus* required to save her. For even though a Jew has sinned, they remain a Jew, and we are obligated to do everything possible in this regard, including through natural means. Certainly, one can find natural factors that contributed to this alarming step, and once identified, it will be easier to find the remedies to combat them.

However, in addition to the above, it must be clarified whether she was born in *taharah*—that is, whether at the time her mother conceived her, she was permitted [to her husband] according to the laws of the Torah. If, Heaven forbid, there was any deficiency in this, the parents must resolve firmly that from this point forward they will be meticulous in observing and safeguarding the laws and statutes of *taharas hamishpachah* as required, and they should influence their entire environment in this matter. For influencing others serves as a partial rectification for the past. The *Ribono shel Olam*, who sees into the heart, will surely, upon seeing their resolution in this, increase His blessing so that the *hishtadlus* to save a Jewish soul will succeed. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding this.

With the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

P.S.
Surely you will also clarify whether there was not also an element of forbidden love, Heaven forbid. And may you conclude with good.

## 5717

B"H, 6 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs, R' Dovber, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

...It seems that before you traveled, we spoke with you as we did with the others traveling abroad, that it is worthwhile to inquire about precious and rare seforim located in shuls and batei medrash, and perhaps also in the possession of private individuals, which are not being studied or utilized because they are remnants from previous generations. It would be worthwhile to send them here in an appropriate manner (by exchanging them for Kehot seforim that are suitable for the shul, beis medrash, or the private individual). The benefit in this is twofold: the seforim will arrive here, where they will ultimately be put to good use, and the shul, etc., will receive Kehot seforim, such as Chassidus seforim or Siddurim with Nusach Ari, and the like. The seforim can be sent to the attention of the Library or the Secretariat, etc. Especially since, according to what is explained in the seforim, this involves the concept of *pidyon shvuyim* (redeeming captives) when the seforim are not being utilized.

With blessings for good tidings, with expanded livelihood, and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 5712

5712

By the Grace of Hashem, 6 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you ask for an explanation regarding the importance of studying Tanya every day, even though you understand the importance of the daily shiurim in Chumash and Tehillim.

The answer to this, to the extent that it can be conveyed in writing, is as follows:

Certainly, you know that there is the *nigleh* of Torah and the *nistar* of Torah, which is also called *pnimiyus haTorah*. In the language of the holy Zohar, they are referred to as the "body of the Torah" and the "soul of the Torah." Just as this is true for every person—and specifically for a Yid—even within his own *neshamah*, there is a *nigleh* part and a *nistar* part, which are called the "body of the *neshamah*" and the "soul of the *neshamah*."

This can be seen more clearly from the fact that regarding matters that touch a person deeply—and even more deeply—he speaks with a special fire and intensity. This is not how he speaks about a matter that he does only to fulfill an obligation, even if he speaks about that too with a certain liveliness; it is nothing more than fulfilling an obligation.

Since we desire the blessings of the *Ribono shel Olam* in the daily affairs of a person, and in order to receive His blessings, the holy Torah states, "If you walk in My statutes," which Rashi explains as referring to the study of Torah. And since we want these blessings to be thorough, full, and complete, one must therefore study at least a minimum amount of Torah in both the *nigleh* of Torah and the *nistar* of Torah—*pnimiyus haTorah*.

And since we are speaking of a minimum, this was established in the part of the *nigleh* of Torah and the part of *pnimiyus haTorah* that one can study even as a beginner. In the *nigleh* of Torah, this is Chumash, and in *pnimiyus haTorah*, this is Tanya.

It goes without saying that just as with Chumash—it is not the same when a child or a beginner studies it as when a great *gaon* studies it, for Chumash can be studied according to its simple meaning, and deeper and deeper—so too is it with the study of Tanya.

I hope that you will show this letter of mine to your *mashpia* of Chassidus, and he will be able to expand upon this explanation for you, which would be too lengthy to do in a letter.

The main thing is that a *bochur* who learns in a *yeshiva* must know that he needs to learn with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, fulfill *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, and not seek out difficulties. Even regarding a matter that is not yet so clear and distinct to him, he must do it anyway. In time, as he learns as he should, that which is currently not understood by him will be understood. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5715

B"H, 7 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning your wife, may she live, that the doctors attribute the current delay in conception to the observance of the laws of the Torah, etc.—presumably, you mean that the doctors you consulted claim that the most opportune time is before the conclusion of the days of the count, etc., and that is what you are referring to.

There are many doctors who generally reject the accuracy of these hypotheses, and even the foundations upon which this hypothesis is built, noting that it is only a relatively short period that they have relied on the aforementioned. Furthermore, in the vast majority of cases, according to the doctors, the difference is only a matter of one or two days. There are certain treatments that shorten the days of the *veses* and the like, and consequently, the aforementioned issue is rectified, at least for a period of time, even according to their hypothesis. While, in general, one must be cautious with any treatment that interferes with the matters of *veses*, regarding a few isolated instances, there is no room for concern if it is done by an expert doctor. In any case, it is surely unnecessary to remind someone like you that there is absolutely no room to be lenient with the laws and decrees—even those of Rabbinic origin—based on the demands of the aforementioned doctors.

It is surprising that you do not mention whether you consulted a doctor regarding yourself; surely you will provide information regarding this at the next opportunity.

In connection with the above, according to the measure of the *Ribono shel Olam*, which is "measure for measure," but many times over, the fact that one who teaches his friend’s son Torah is considered as if he had fathered him is a special *segulah* for the birth of children—in addition to your son, may he live and be well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*.

#### ***5715***

**The accuracy of these hypotheses:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 5250.

**A special segulah:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 5187.

## 5716

5716

B"H, 8 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Yosef David, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from the day that was doubled in goodness [Tuesday], in which you write that you have rented a new apartment and ask when, and what should be done there.

Your intent is not entirely clear; perhaps you mean when you should move in. It is appropriate to move in on a day that was doubled in goodness, provided it does not cause undue trouble. If it is a burden, you may move in on other days of the week as well (except for Monday and Wednesday). It is the custom of Anash to bring into a new home, first and foremost, a Siddur, Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and likewise to affix mezuzos immediately—naturally, without a bracha. On the thirtieth day, one should remove one mezuzah to have it checked, and if possible, replace it with one that is more beautiful and mehudar. When affixing it, one should recite the bracha and have in mind that the bracha covers the entire house.

I trust you are keeping the three daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, in addition to your other shiurim in Nigleh and Chassidus.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

#### ***5716***

**Rabbi Yosef David:** Leiner, Brooklyn.

**To bring into a new home:** See also above, Vol. 12, Letter 4,972, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

**To affix mezuzos immediately:** See also above, Vol. 13, Letter 4,443.

## 5717

B"H, 8 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Gavriel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning changing the order of the Chassidus shiur on Erev Shabbos, to hold it after reciting *Lechu Neranena* and before *Kegavna*:

As you yourself describe in your letter, there are positive and negative aspects to this. One side you did not mention is the principle of our Sages regarding those entering the shul, lest they say that the congregation is beginning with *Kegavna*. Therefore, one who follows one custom acts according to his practice, and one who follows the other acts according to his, and you should follow the preference of the majority of those who study.

May it be Hashem’s will that, in any case, everyone will increase and glorify Torah—both the revealed Torah and the Torah of Chassidus—the perfect Torah, which is the body and soul of the Torah.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

## 5719

5719

B"H, 9 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding the difficulties that have recently arisen in the work of your husband, may he live and be well.

As I have already written to several of the residents of Kfar Chabad, Kfar Chabad is good for each of them and their families, may they live and be well, not only in spiritual matters but also in material ones. In particular, one who has merited not only to live in Kfar Chabad but also to have the opportunity to strengthen and expand Kfar Chabad, his merit and reward are far greater. It is understood that through this work, one is doing a favor not only for one person or a few, but it is a general benefit for the Kfar, and specifically a benefit for the one who acts and works in this area. From this, it is understood that if difficulties arise in the work, or if others do not appreciate it properly, this has absolutely no connection to the idea of thinking about stopping the work, and thereby causing damage, Heaven forbid, to the community, and Heaven forbid, to oneself.

Certainly, one must ensure that the improper attitude is nullified and that the obstacles are removed. In general, through the ways of peace, one achieves much more than through other means, especially according to the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken that *Ahavas Yisrael* (loving your fellow as yourself) is a vessel for the greatest of all mitzvos.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that for the new year, and even sooner, there should be ever more peace and closeness among all the residents of Kfar Chabad—each one with the other—and may all of them together bring about a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5720

B.H., 9 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in the study of Torah and performs many deeds, etc.,
R' Menashe, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It gave me pleasure to hear of your efforts in publishing the sefer *Halachos Gedolos* by one of the *Rishonim*, with a comprehensive commentary, and that Hashem has granted you merit and success so that the book will soon appear in print.

May it be Hashem’s will that through this expansion, you may increase soldiers in Torah—in Torah in general, both the "great" and the "small," the "great matter" and the "small matter" as interpreted by our Sages (*Bava Basra* 108a), the body of Torah and the soul of Torah, as the *Zohar* (Vol. III, 152a) expresses it, a *Torah Temimah*.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

Regarding the request for an *haskamah*—it is known that this is not the custom in the house of the Rebbe. Please accept my apologies.

As a token of affection for the words of the *Rishonim* by whose merit we live, I have transcribed here a few notes on the beginning of this sefer, which you left with me.

**Mishneh Halachos, Subsection 1:** "Bar Yisrael"—it begins with "a man": "A Jewish man, etc., for the purpose of *kedushah*, etc.," similar to the language of the *Mishnah*, "The man betroths"—for such is the language of the verse: "If a man takes a wife, etc." See also the language of the Rambam at the beginning of *Hilchos Ishus*.

[Regarding why the *Mishnah* in the first chapter of *Kiddushin* changes the phrasing to "The woman is acquired"—the Gemara there provides an explanation.]

Especially here, where it continues: "He is required to betroth, etc., and to recite the blessings, etc., and to hand over the *kesubah*, etc."—all of which are the actions of the man.

It is worth noting the words of our Sages cited in Rashi (*Shmuel I* 20:30).

It should be investigated whether this is the style of the *Bahag*, "A Jewish man who wishes"—for seemingly, it is self-evident.

Further on, the *Or Zarua* cites the version: "Whoever wishes." Perhaps it was chosen because of the conclusion of the matter: "From the source of *Yisrael*."

**In the text: "And hand over the kesubah to her."** The timing of handing over the *kesubah*—there are several opinions regarding this: Rambam, *Hilchos Ishus*, Chapter 10; *Tur Shulchan Aruch Even HaEzer*, end of Section 66, and the commentaries there.

In any case, it is puzzling that the *Birkas Chasanim* (the wedding blessings) is not mentioned here, whether it is after the handing over or before it.

To my mind, it is a clear omission by the copyist or the printer.

In the *She'iltos* (*Chayei Sarah*, 16): "Whoever wishes to take a wife is required to betroth her first, and recite the *Birkas Erusin* in the presence of ten, **and the *Birkas Chasanim*** in the presence of ten, and hand over the *kesubah* to her." It should be the same way here.

This also makes the continuation of the passage consistent: "For Rav Nachman said, etc., from where do we know [the requirement] **for *Birkas Chasanim***."

In the *Emek She'eilah* on the *She'iltos* there, he emends and adds the word "in the presence of ten" to the *Bahag* here, after the words "*Birkas Erusin*," and explains that his intention is to bring proof from *Birkas Chasanim* (which is not discussed there **at all**) that ten are required for *Birkas Erusin* because ten are required [for *Birkas Chasanim*]. Aside from the fact that the *Bahag* should have stated this explicitly, the wonder remains regarding the omission of the *Birkas Chasanim* matter.

**Mishneh Halachos, Subsection 2:** Our Rebbe did not have the version "Bar Nasan." This is also not the version in the *She'iltos* there. The *Emek She'eilah* explains that it must be that the letters "B.N." in the *Shas* are a scribal error, for Rav Huna bar Nasan lived after Rav Ashi, who was born when Rava, the colleague of Rav Nachman, passed away. The *Seder HaDoros* (entry: Rav Huna bar Nasan) has already noted that we find Rav Huna bar Nasan challenging Rava (*Nedarim* 12a), and perhaps he was a very old man, etc., or perhaps there were two [people by that name].

However, in Rashi on *Nedarim* there, it is printed simply as "Rav Huna," omitting the words "bar Nasan." This requires further study in *Dikdukei Sofrim*.

**Mishneh Halachos, Subsection 3:** "Through *chupah* and *kiddushin*." Based on the words of our Sages that "the garment of the righteous is precious," I am transcribing what I wrote regarding this in a *maamar* of the Admur HaZaken (the author of the *Tanya*), in his sefer *Torah Or* (98d), which reads: "Regarding what we say, 'He sanctifies His people Yisrael through *chupah* and *kiddushin*,' they asked: Why was the order changed to place *chupah* before *kiddushin*? Rather, *chupah* is the level of *makif* (encompassing light), and it is the matter of 'He forced the mountain over them like a cask,' which is the level of the revelation of the *makif* as mentioned above. Therefore, it was necessary to place *chupah* before *kiddushin*, for in order for them to come to the acceptance of the Torah, which is the level of *kiddushin*, it must be through the drawing down of the *makif* first, through which they came to the level of *bitul* to prioritize 'we will do' [before 'we will hear'], etc. Then, the drawing down and revelation of the level of Torah can occur." End quote.

## 5721

5721

B"H, 9 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, R' Zalman, may he live,

Peace and Blessing!

I recently received an article from the periodical *Iggeret LaGolah* (in English, dated 4 Tammuz 5717), along with some drawings from it. These made an impression on me precisely because they are drawn as they are—without "tricks," and not even artistic "tricks." It would be appropriate and correct to create an entire album of Kfar Chabad in this manner—not only in its current state, but also as it was when you first arrived there. In this way, the album would also show the development of the village, as well as the benefit of the village's current layout, given the hope that it will develop even further in the near future. If this series of drawings proves successful, one should also consider printing them, whether as an album of postcards or as individual postcards. The main point, as mentioned, is that the drawings should reflect the simplicity of reality. Do not be discouraged if someone says that a photograph is more suitable for this and that a drawing is unnecessary; the difference between a photograph and a drawing made by an artist—even one done with a technique as close to reality as possible—is clearly evident.

It is understood that if there are expenses associated with the realization of these drawings, they will be covered by a special fund, which will also include compensation for labor, etc. I will await your response with good news regarding this matter.

It is unnecessary to add that my intention is not only for the houses and the like, but also, and primarily, for drawings of the life of the village—from the spiritual life within the spiritual, down to the physical life within the physical.

I trust that you have your own *shiurim* in *Nigleh* and *Chassidus*, in addition to the *shiurim* studied in public in which you participate.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* and for good news regarding the above.

**To the Avreich, R' Zalman, may he live:** Kleinman, Kfar Chabad.

## 5722

10 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter in which you write regarding [Name] and the doctor’s opinion that it would be beneficial for him to travel from his home, and you ask my opinion on this matter.

As you describe the situation in your letter, the idea is good. However, regarding the suggestion that he travel to the United States or another country: in addition to the expenses involved, the main point is that it is impossible to know in advance what kind of environment he will enter upon arriving in a new place, and how that environment will influence him, even if it is one of the better environments in the country to which he travels. Furthermore, the supervision and the necessity of reporting to someone in a new country—even if he accepts this upon himself—would be a matter of his own good will, and it is not comparable to reporting that is necessitated by a [pre-existing] relationship or by the habit of many years. And this is understood.

For the desired purpose, traveling to a different location within Eretz Yisrael itself is sufficient, as then most of the negative factors will be corrected almost entirely, or perhaps even completely.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevgam, zya*, for whatever each of them needs, in accordance with the content of your letter.

With blessings for a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

P.S.
Since he is the one requesting and writing about the aforementioned, the more he increases his involvement in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, the more the blessings of Hashem will be increased in the fulfillment of his requests in general, and regarding this matter in particular.

It is certainly superfluous to emphasize that since they wrote to me, and they will be mentioned—he and his family—at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and they are in need of a special blessing, especially during these days when we say twice each day, "**Your face**, Hashem, I seek," it necessitates that not only must **each one** of them distance themselves from the matters and the people who fight, *r'l*, openly and secretly, against the teachings of Chassidus and its affairs—against the Baal Shem Tov, the Alter Rebbe, and their students—but it is also not at all sufficient to merely strengthen oneself to stand one's ground (which is the opposite of the command to **ascend** in matters of holiness).

Rather, an increase and an ascent in all of this is required, as well as influence in this direction wherever their reach extends.

***

**5722**

**To travel from his home:** See *Iggeres* 5742 above.

## 5723

5723

By the Grace of G-d
10 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I am in receipt of your letter from the day that was doubled in goodness [Tuesday], in which you outline the events you have experienced, particularly recently, in your position at... and the difficulties therein, to the point that you felt compelled (in your opinion) to announce that you are leaving your work there. You conclude by detailing the proposals you have for the future and asking for my opinion on the matter.

It is not clear from your letter whether your departure from... is in such a state that nothing can be done about it, or if there is room for a reversal. If there is, then in my opinion, you should contemplate this deeply to see if leaving is truly worthwhile. It is possible that in this case, one could use even stronger language to question whether leaving is permitted at all. After all, according to your letter, you have succeeded in your work there, yet on the other hand, you have not finished it; there are several classes whose conduct is the opposite of what is desired, and even in your own class, you are only in the middle of the process of improvement. It is a known teaching of our Sages that a person does not learn from everyone, and who knows if someone else will succeed in influencing them in the desired direction? It is understood that your arguments for leaving the place have merit and require consideration, but in this consideration, one must take into account the perspective cited in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan: "Take this rule in your hand and remember it always: any matter that is beneficial or leads to actual *avodah*, any obstacle that may arise to this—even if the obstacle comes from a 'higher' source—is merely a tactic of the *nefesh habehamis*."

If, after reflection on the matter—and primarily after consultation with those who are not personally involved—you reach the decision that you must leave... or that the situation is such that you cannot return in a way that would allow you to continue your positive influence there, then among the proposals you mentioned, you should focus on those where the situation involves "extracting the precious from the worthless," and where there is no one else in that place or institution to do so. The great importance of a *mitzvah* that cannot be performed by others is well known, as per the ruling of our Sages in *Maseches Moed Katan* (9a, end of side A and beginning of side B).

Regarding the second point in your letter—although in essence it is not separate from the above, but rather both are one point—this concerns your relationship with *Chassidus* and the *Chassidim* of Chabad.

My view is well known: in this era of ours, a conduct appropriate to this approach is especially necessary. Since the darkness is great and continues to darken even further in these years, this necessitates a much greater addition to the side of light and holiness. This addition must not only be in the fulfillment of things and actual deeds—even though it is a teaching of the *Mishnah* that the deed is the essential thing—but also, and this is essential, in the light, vitality, warmth, and *hispaalus* that are required. Since in our time people demand an "anchor" in intellect and understanding in every matter, and when it is based on *kabbalas ol* alone, it does not endure for long, as is required and in the necessary measure, therefore the light, vitality, warmth, and the addition within them must also be connected with intellect and understanding. This is one of the matters and foundations of Chabad *Chassidus*.

In other words, and regarding yourself: since Divine Providence has gifted you with the talent to influence youth who are preparing to build homes in Israel in the coming years—meaning that influencing each one of them is an influence upon a home in Israel—you must utilize your talents in this area as much as possible. This requires utilizing them with defined vitality, warmth, and light to the maximum degree. The closest path to this, and perhaps the only one, is by "throwing yourself" (*araynvurfen*) into the matters of the *Chassidus* approach: by studying its teachings and walking in its ways regarding thought, speech, and action, and living your daily life in a manner consistent with it. Our era is not suited for arranging matters in stages—starting with a stage of study and contemplation, and only afterwards drawing conclusions from that study regarding thought, speech, and action for oneself, and only then influencing others in this. There is not enough time, especially when the matter concerns influencing youth. Therefore, one must begin all three stages at once, especially since in your case, you already possess knowledge and a grasp of all these stages to a certain degree, and there is nothing that can stand before true *ratzon*.

As it appears from the end of your letter, you are not occupied as you should be with matters of *shidduchim*; I mean that you do not even mention it. This is, of course, most surprising. Naturally, on the basis of our Sages' teaching that "one may act to the benefit of another in his absence," I will take the liberty of mentioning in the *pidyon nefesh* the matter of a good *shidduch*, both materially and spiritually, and very soon. You should certainly occupy yourself with this in the natural way as well, with the necessary vigor as required by our Torah.

May it be G-d's will that in this, too, in addition to the aforementioned matters, you will bring good news very soon, and the merit of the many whom you have influenced to bring them closer to the *Ribono shel Olam* will surely stand by you in this essential matter.

I await good news in all that has been said, and with blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 5725

B"H, 10 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the *pidyon nefesh* for your daughter, *tichyeh*. It is surprising that for a very long time there has been no news from you, and even now, you send only a *pidyon nefesh* and nothing more. Surely you will provide more details at the next opportunity, and may it be His will that you bring good news.

Regarding what you wrote about your daughter, *tichyeh*, mentioned above: based on the situation as described in your letter, many new treatments have been developed in recent years for such cases, such as pills that accelerate development, etc. It seems that in Switzerland there are great doctors who are experts in this field. It would be worthwhile for you to inquire about this in detail and act according to the information you receive.

I must comment regarding the conclusion of your letter, where you write that when Hashem helps and she is healed, you will, *bli neder*, give to Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, etc. This is not the preferred phrasing, as one should not set conditions with Hashem, stipulating that He must help first and then, etc. The *avodah* of every Jewish person is to do everything possible and everything within their ability in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—of which *tzedakah* is included, and furthermore, it is equivalent to all the *mitzvos* combined, to the point that it is called "the *mitzvah*" (see *Tanya*, Chapter 37, at length). Simultaneously, one should *daven*, request, and beseech Hashem for what one needs in terms of children, life, and ample sustenance. *V'ka'l*.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5717

5717

B"H, 12 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Elul.

1) Regarding your question as to whether to include certain stipulations in a text to which one of the parties objects, etc.

In general, one should not deviate from the standard text. On the other hand, one should not be stubborn about it if it does not touch at all upon matters of yiras shamayim. It is understood that one should inquire as to why someone objects to the standard text.

2) Regarding your request for a blessing that you remain in your state of innocence, etc.

It is understood that this depends on your own will, for the ability to do so has been granted to you. However, you must study with consistency and diligence and fulfill the mitzvos with hiddur; then, the blessing of Hashem will be added to what has been said.

3) Regarding what you wrote, that you are unable to complete the three and a half years.

It is not understood to which years you are referring. In any case, you should present your situation to the administration of the school where you study, as they desire your benefit and have no personal interest in the matter; you should act according to their instruction. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

## 5718

B"H, 12 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Thursday, in which you write regarding the difficulties you are encountering, which, according to your understanding, are connected to the fact that you study Chassidus and also influence others in this regard.

Now, **if** this is indeed true, fortunate is your portion that you have merited to disseminate the wellsprings of the hidden Torah (Chassidus) in a manner that has been felt even by the "opposing side," who now wish to hinder you. This itself should awaken in you additional strength and energy to do everything possible so that the "light within the Torah" is revealed in a manner that is ever-expanding and ever-ascending; there is nothing greater than this. And while it is understood that the activities of Bnei Yisrael must be carried out specifically in ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, this does not affect the substance of the matter, only the manner in which it is brought into action. One of the details in this is not to magnify the concealments and obstructions—neither in your own eyes nor in the eyes of others. May it be the will that all those who seem to want to conceal this will come to realize the truth: that this is not their true desire, for in the inner depths of their souls, every single one of Bnei Yisrael wants to connect to the inner dimension of the Torah, since they want to connect to the inner dimension of Hashem—**which is** the path to achieve this, as explained in the holy Zohar (Vol. III, 73a).

Since it appears from your letter that other friends of yours have also been captured by the words of the teachings of Chassidus, which is written to be "your life and the length of your days," you will surely find a way to convey the above to them as well. May it be the will that the promise "your wellsprings will spread outward" be fulfilled in our immediate time, and that which follows it—is Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

## 5719

B"H, 12 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday, in which you write regarding your son, *sheyichyeh*, and what he experienced before coming to study here in the yeshivah, and you also request a suggestion as to what to do regarding the future... Since your son, *sheyichyeh*, has been here for a relatively short time, it is difficult to decide what is best for him—whether as you suggested in your letter or in another manner—until a sufficient amount of time has passed to see the influence of the new environment upon your son, *sheyichyeh*.

Since I see in your letter that you are a doctor—and if the meaning is indeed a physician, it is certainly superfluous to remind you that with the youth, especially in our era of many changes and upheavals throughout the entire world, and consequently in the environment of every individual—a time in which, to our sorrow, we have not merited tranquility in the world or in the community—all of this requires extra caution in our relationships with the youth, so as not to diminish their peace of mind and tranquility, or to cast doubts upon their affairs. If someone among the youth feels good in an environment that is appropriate according to the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, one must be extremely careful not to disturb their peace, and as mentioned above, this is understood even more clearly by one who observes the life of the younger generation in our times.

It was pleasant for me to read at the conclusion of your letter that your son is conducting himself according to the law of the Torah, and it is possible that this is the reason and cause for your son, *sheyichyeh*, wanting to ascend further in Torah and mitzvos, and he is not satisfied with his level until now, however good it may be, since the Torah says, "We ascend in matters of holiness."

My hope is strong, based on the above, that peace will increase and your relationship with him will improve more and more, and may the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the mitzvos bless you and grant you success, with much true *nachas* from your son, *sheyichyeh*.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* and for good tidings.

## 5732

5732

B"H, 13 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs,
R' Yaakov Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 3 Elul, in which you write that you have been accepted as a *shaliach tzibbur* in the *beis knesses*, and that—following the time-honored Jewish custom—you will speak words of *hisorerus* before them during the upcoming *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*.

It is understood that you have acted correctly. Surely there will be a *minyan* there, and even more, who are *Shabbos* observers. You should endeavor to increase their number, going from strength to strength, by means of words of *hisorerus* on *Rosh Hashanah*, etc., in a formal manner, and words of *hisorerus* whenever the opportunity arises—especially throughout the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, the days and nights regarding which it is said, "Seek Hashem when He is to be found," bringing the light closer to the spark. As for what to say—the ultimate objective must be consistent with the teaching, "The deed is the essential thing." The methods for explaining this depend on the type of congregants and the nature of their souls. This includes explaining that this is a benefit not only in spiritual matters but also in material ones. And even if at times this is not fully understood by the intellect, it is natural that a limited intellect cannot grasp or comprehend something that is unlimited; this is infinitely more difficult than "passing an elephant through the eye of a needle," etc.

Regarding what you wrote—that people come to you to ask for mercy on behalf of relatives, etc., and what you should do:

On such occasions, it is understood that it is appropriate to utilize the matter to inspire them regarding an increase in *yiras shamayim*. Surely you will conduct yourself in this manner in the future as well. Suggest to them that they mention their names at the *tziyon* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh-h*, *nvg-m*, *zy-a*, and that an increase in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* will serve as a channel and vessel for the acceptance of the prayer.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the *tziyon* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that was mentioned.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5733

B”H, 13 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Elul, in which you write that your son, shlita, was successful with the consul regarding the extension of his passport, etc., and you therefore request that he take some of his time from the study of Torah to study a profession.

Surely, you yourself can see the contradiction between these two matters. The content of the first is that your son, sheyichyeh, sees with his own physical eyes the blessing of Hashem, the Giver of the Torah, in his affairs. Yet, as a result of this, there comes a request that your son reduce his Torah study to learn a profession.

My hope is that what you wrote stems from a father’s love for his son—and regarding love in general, our Sages have said, concerning every person, that sometimes it "distorts the line."

In my opinion, when taking into account the age of your son, sheyichyeh, and that these are the years most suited for the study of Torah—which is called *Toras Chaim*, encompassing life in its literal sense in this world, as it is said, "If you walk in My statutes," which Rashi explains as "that you shall be toiling in Torah," followed by "and keep My mitzvos," etc., and all the blessings stated in that parsha—he should be encouraged and strengthened to study with the greatest possible consistency and diligence. As our Sages have promised: "You have labored and found"—he will succeed in his studies, to the true *nachas* of all who love him, and first and foremost, certainly his father, sheyichyeh.

I will take this opportunity to urge him to keep the three daily *shiurim* that are incumbent upon every person, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. At the very least, he should keep them from now on, as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that they are a *segulah* for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

This is especially true when the matter at hand is something entirely new, located in a different place, and has no connection to the people here (aside, of course, from the principle that all Yisrael are responsible for one another). May it be the will of Hashem that He guide the aforementioned on the path that is truly good for him.

It is well known the ruling regarding how great the deeds of Chiyya are, even in comparison to the deeds of Rabbi Chanina (Kesuvos 103b).

This is also the reason for the revelation of the secrets of the Torah—the inner dimensions of the Torah—in abundance and in a manner of dissemination, until they reach even the "outside," as is known from the parable of our Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, regarding the king's son and the precious stone in the king’s crown (printed in *HaTamim*, issue 2, p. 49).

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

## 5737

B"H, 14 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in which you write the main points of what you have experienced over the past year, as well as regarding the state of your health concerning your skin.

It is understood that if the intent of your letter is to be taken literally—that you are choosing an ointment and a method of treatment for yourself based on the advice of friends and the like—this is not the correct path, neither according to natural reason nor according to the instruction of our Torah, which grants the physician permission to heal. Surely there are expert doctors in this field in your vicinity; at the very least, you should now ask for their guidance and act accordingly. Based on the above, it is understood that your question regarding the advice of an individual who is said to be an expert is also incorrect. You should act as stated above, and as you yourself conclude in your letter, consult with a dermatologist, etc.

May it be Hashem’s will that you increase in Torah and *mitzvos* with *mesiras nefesh*, and not according to the order you write—that if Hashem helps you, then you will awaken. The order for a Jewish person is, first and foremost, to act in practice (especially since the matter itself is of incomparable value, as the *Mishnah* states: "The reward of a *mitzvah* is the *mitzvah* itself"). May Hashem grant you success and bring you good news regarding your health, not only in physical matters but also in spiritual ones.

I trust you are participating in the activities of *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad*, in a manner that does not interfere with your study schedule.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* and for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 15 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, the month of mercy, in which you write regarding your feelings of loneliness, etc., and how you wish to live specifically in another place, even though you know that the place where you are currently located is capable of influencing Chassidus, etc.

The contradiction between the beginning and the end of your statement is understandable. For if the place is capable of influencing Chassidus, it is understood that you are not lonely there, because a vessel for receiving Chassidus is, in itself, a **Chassidic** reality—whether it is revealed to all or revealed to the eyes of those who observe them. Furthermore, what is the whole matter of loneliness, when Hashem is standing over him in that very place, looking at him and examining his kidneys and heart to see if he is serving Him as is fitting (as stated by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 41)? And the Alter Rebbe immediately provides the conclusion from this as well, stating: "Therefore, one must serve before Him, etc., and one should deepen this thought and dwell upon it at length, etc." If you will strive to contemplate this conclusion, you will immediately see that you are not lonely; on the contrary.

Even though, on the face of it, all the matters you write about correspond to reality in a general sense, it is said: "I have set before you life and the good, etc." This means that regarding all matters of *kelipas nogah*—which is the general vitality of this physical and material world (Tanya, Chapter 37; see there at length)—this intermediary between holiness, etc., must be utilized in a way that increases holiness, etc. Even the contemplation regarding the conditions of the place about which you write can be approached in two ways. In this, too, lies the proof and the touchstone of who is the one inciting this contemplation, as explained in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the conclusion of your letter regarding your preparations for the great day of Chai Elul, which is approaching for blessing, you will succeed in that place in actuality. May you succeed and accomplish there as well, in accordance with the instructions of the two great luminaries who were revealed on this bright day, both of whom emphasized the matter of *avodas Hashem* specifically with joy and goodness of heart—*avodas Hashem* in the manner of "you shall surely help with him" (as transcribed in *Hayom Yom*, 28 Shevat; see there)—and through the line of "love your fellow as yourself," which is one with "love Hashem your G-d." I look forward to hearing good news regarding all the above.

Since you do not mention anything regarding matters of health, it is surely a sign that everything is in order and in peace, and I am certain that you will explicitly confirm this as well.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* and for good news.

## 5741

B"H, 15 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 10 Elul, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the hair of the *Nukvah*, which is explained in *Chassidus*—that a woman’s hair is considered *ervah* because it provides a place for the *yinekas hachitzonim* (the nourishment of the external forces), etc. (besides the *dvar mitzvah* you cite in your letter, this is also discussed in *Likutei Torah, Devarim* 36c, and elsewhere)—you ask that based on this explanation, just as a *nazir* is warned not to shave his hair because of the increase in *kedushah* that comes through it, a woman should logically be at the opposite extreme: she should be required to shave her hair, rather than merely covering her head.

The explanation for this can be understood through the *nigleh* (revealed Torah): the law that a woman’s hair is *ervah* does not apply to unmarried women, and even regarding married women, it only applies to strangers and in situations where it is customary to cover it. This is in contrast to her husband; on the contrary, he can say, "I do not desire a shaven woman" (*Nazir* 28a). From the *nigleh*, we can also understand the matter in its *pnimiyus* (inner dimension): nourishment for the *chitzonim* can only occur when the matter reaches the state of actual nourishment, as opposed to when it is merely a state of receptivity. This is only possible if there is nothing protecting it, and it is **more** forbidden than usual. The analogy is understood. See *Likutei Torah, Vayikra* 24a, 32a, and elsewhere.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**5741**

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 348, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Yitzchak:** Dubov, Manchester. Additional letters to him appear above, 5798, and in the references noted there.

## 5717

B"H, 15 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community,
R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following the long interval, your letter from Wednesday was received. I am certain you have already received my response to your previous letter, even though you do not mention it. In it, you write that during the vacation days, Anash assisted with the educational matters in your vicinity. You surely utilized this opportunity to draw closer to them, for regarding all parts and matters of Torah and mitzvos, it is said that the benefit is the bonding of friends—and "the measure of good is greater" in that "many companions create" [a stronger bond], as this matter is explained at length in the well-known *Kuntres Hecholtzu*. The motto is found in the saying of the Mitteler Rebbe: that when two Jews speak together, it is two *nefesh elokis* against one *nefesh tiv'is*, and the rest is understood.

Regarding what you wrote about organizing a guidebook for marriage in connection with the various questions that arise in this field: this is a correct endeavor. In our time, two extremes have met: on one hand, highly complex problems and questions, and on the other hand, in this latest generation, the study of practical halachic rulings—specifically in the *poskim acharonim*—has diminished significantly. Yet, the *halacha* follows the *basra'i* (the later authorities), and in them, matters are explained more clearly, and the rest is understood. Therefore, it is understood that compilations which clarify the various sides of these questions and raise awareness of them—and how much better if they also point to the books where these questions are discussed—are among the books that this current time necessitates engagement with.

Incidentally, this was also one of the reasons for the printing of the *Sdei Chemed*, in which were gathered [rulings] from many books of the *poskim acharonim* regarding practical *halacha*. Likewise, this is also why, eventually, the necessity was recognized to publish the *Otzar HaPoskim* on *Even HaEzer*, though it is a pity that the matter is proceeding so slowly.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each one according to their needs, as appropriate to the content of your letter.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

***

**R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim:** Segal, Tel Aviv. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 14, 5025, and the references in the notes there.

**In the saying of the Mitteler Rebbe:** See also above, letter 5181, and the references in the notes there.

## 5717

By the Grace of Hashem, 17 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of a distinguished lineage, etc., R’ Shazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Following up on my previous letter in response to yours—which I trust was received in due time—I have received the news that the Jewish Agency has decided to return a significant sum to the village (in connection with the expenses incurred for electrical matters). I see this as a clear indication of success for the village’s affairs. For a long time, I have been thinking about a plan—which I have discussed and written to you about previously—that in my opinion is essential: the village must develop and expand, not only in quality but also in quantity. This is especially true since the two are interdependent, and in this context, "quantity" refers to the number of residents. Given the current state of the village, the shortage of housing—specifically suitable housing—and the lack of substantial funds, the practice has been to build house by house. We see that in such cases, there is no master plan for the houses as a whole; one house does not resemble the next, and the placement of the houses being built within the village area does not conform to a unified plan. All these shortcomings can be prevented in only one way: by approaching construction by building several houses at once. Under current conditions, this requires a significant sum of money on the spot, which until now was not possible.

When I received the aforementioned news, I immediately wrote my opinion to the Village Committee: this is the opportunity that has been presented to develop the village in a planned manner—or at least, much more planned than it would be otherwise. Therefore, they should invest the entire sum into building a housing project. Naturally, they should also seek assistance through mortgages and loans, etc., which are available in such cases, so that the number of apartments built in this project will be the maximum possible. They should also consult with experts in the field to prepare a suitable construction plan.

Knowing your interest in all the village’s affairs, and especially in this step—which in my opinion is exceptional for the benefit of the village’s expansion in both quantity and quality—I am writing this to you. I have strong confidence that this not only aligns with your own perspective, but that you will further contribute with your advice and assistance to the Village Committee to perfect the housing project plan as much as possible, as you are on the ground and familiar with the conditions.

Certainly, there are several matters in the village—some of them necessary—that require financial assistance, and there is room to argue that there will be proposals to utilize these aforementioned funds for those matters. In my opinion, however, there is no place for this at all. The aforementioned matters do not require such an exceptional event or such significant sums. Surely, in the course of time, other possibilities will arise to fulfill those needs (the proof being that those involved in them did not know in the past about the return of the funds mentioned at the beginning of the letter). Meanwhile, we see tangibly that the construction of the housing project has been delayed for some time, which has led to the undesirable phenomenon where several people have approached the Village Committee expressing their desire to settle there, only to be turned away empty-handed due to a lack of apartments and housing, and they have settled in other places. Who knows if they would want to now, or even if they did, whether they could change their residence again to settle in Kfar Chabad? Certainly, when news of the housing project becomes known, it will also become known to many others who wish to settle in the village—who are suitable for it in every respect—and only the lack of housing is preventing them from doing so.

May it be the will of Hashem that as the bright day of Chai Elul approaches—the birthday of the two great luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and our Alter Rebbe, who illuminated the world with their Torah and their deeds and established their approach upon the foundation that a faithful shepherd of Israel must engage in the spiritual and material well-being of the Jewish people simultaneously, without setting conditions, and at the same time without forgetting the truth and reality, that the true good is specifically when both are united together.

As is recounted at length regarding the Baal Shem Tov’s approach to this and his activities in the *Kuntres Chai Elul 5703*, *Sicha* 4 and elsewhere, and it is well-known among Chassidei Chabad regarding the Alter Rebbe in this regard.

May Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land be a living example of this union of the spiritual and the material—a complete and perfect union that is ever-improving and ever-increasing. From it, a Chassidic way of life will spread on weekdays, Shabbos, and Yom Tov to ever-widening circles, to the great satisfaction and the greatest merit of all those who have taken part and are taking part in the affairs of Kfar Chabad and its residents, and may this also be in a manner that is ever-growing, until it becomes very great.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all that has been mentioned, as well as what is between the lines, and I sign with the traditional formula sanctified by tens of generations of our people, the children of Israel.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, for you and all that is yours.

P.S.
Just now I received further news regarding the expansion and allocation of plots to broaden the agricultural aspect of the village, and that they are preparing to begin the actual planting of the orchard. Although I have not yet received the details, surely you are aware of them as well. May it be the will of Hashem that this expansion also continues to grow in accordance with the plan mentioned above, with success in both the material and the spiritual.

## 5745

B"H, 17 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, Branch:
May Hashem grant them life!

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive at least a brief overview of your work in the past, and I hope that more has been accomplished than what was written, and most importantly, that in the future, the work will be expanded in every possible way.

I also hope—even though you did not mention it—that among the subjects being studied, there is also the study of the laws and regulations of Taharas HaMishpacha with married women or kallahs who are about to be married, as well as the laws connected to the kashrus of food items, the latter of which can also be taught to young girls. As far as I recall, these laws are compiled in the Siddur Korban Mincha; hopefully, some of the women have such a siddur, and if not, we will send one to you.

Since we are currently in the month of Elul, which, as explained at length by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is the month of *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-searching) for the outgoing year, as well as a good preparation for the coming year—that it should be a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually—this *cheshbon* and preparation must also include the participation of **every** member of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad from every branch, as well as a firm resolution to do even more in this regard in the coming days, weeks, and months.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that in good health and high spirits, you should realize all your good resolutions to the fullest extent, and with an increase as well.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above, and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for each of the members and their families, may they live.

**Branch:** Sent to all branches. One copy, which was sent on the 26th of Elul, is printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 444.
