## 5747

5747

B.H., 15 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the communal activists, lovers of Torah, and generous benefactors,
May Hashem be with them, may they live.

Greetings and blessings!

This year, the eighteenth day (Chai) of Elul, marks sixty years since the founding of the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch by the Rebbe Rashab, the father of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe — may the merit of the righteous protect us.

The Yeshiva was established on the luminous day of Chai Elul, the birthday of the two great luminaries: the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch. Through this, the unique character of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos was also signified: to disseminate Torah Temimah—both Nigleh and Pnimiyus—imbued with Yiras Hashem and Ahavas Hashem, mesiras nefesh and Ahavas Yisrael, with an inner sense of responsibility for the collective and for the individual.

Golah after golah, one exile after another, the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos have endured—in many places throughout Russia itself, Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), Poland, and Latvia, until Divine Providence transplanted the central Yeshiva to America seventeen years ago.

But—*shem beiso* (a place is its home). Everywhere, the Tomchei Temimim "four cubits" of Torah and "four cubits" of tefillah were established. Everywhere, the Yeshiva guarded its uniqueness and fulfilled its purpose and mission with mesiras nefesh.

The deep roots it planted have brought forth fruit and fruit of the fruit, sustaining Yiddishkeit wherever they were found—in Soviet Russia as in other parts of the world. And the students of the Lubavitcher yeshivos, the "Temimim," are today among the greatest creative forces in the field of strengthening Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos in general, and in proper chinuch in particular: in America, Eretz Yisrael, Canada, Europe, Morocco, Australia, and so on.

Sadly, and to our great regret, the further development and expansion of the Lubavitcher yeshivos and their vital work is severely hampered by a burden of debts and deficits. Therefore, the administration of Tomchei Temimim turns with a call for help to our brethren, the Children of Israel, for their urgent support. Surely, the broad American Jewish public will respond warmly to this call for help, especially in these current days of mercy, and will help not only to wipe away the old deficits but also to create a financial foundation for its growing work in the future.

Great is the merit of taking part and becoming a partner in the maintenance and expansion of Tomchei Temimim, to receive the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in everything one needs, in both material and spiritual matters.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***5747***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 484.

## 5717

5717

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is understood and also simple that this does not mean that every action of any person in Israel must be justified one hundred percent simply because we know that he has done many good deeds. However, it is also understood that Heaven forbid—Heaven forbid—to nullify a good action of anyone in Israel, and especially an action done in public and for the benefit of the many in Israel, simply because a second or third action is not as it should be. And what better proof do we have than these days, the days of Elul, when our Sages **commanded** **every** person in Israel to recite twice daily, "Hashem is my light and my salvation... Hear, Hashem, my voice when I call; be gracious to me and answer me." And if many people were to gather and say that so-and-so should not say this, and use all the expressions found in your letter, my hope is that you, too, would rule that their words are null and void... And although, of course, you are not obligated to take my protest into account, since this is not my own personal protest but is based on the command of the holy Torah—especially during the days of Elul, the month of mercy, the preparation for the days of judgment and the Days of Awe, when all the creatures of the world pass before Him in judgment—and since the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," as our Sages have informed us, this strengthens my protest even further. For everyone must conduct themselves in the way they wish to be treated, and the ruling in the Torah is, "That which is hateful to you, do not do to your fellow..."

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned, and for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 5717

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

With some delay, your letter was received, in which you share the good news that you participated and succeeded in the campaign to distribute Sifrei Da"Ch, the teachings of Chassidus, and also that on your birthday you recited Da"Ch in public—a portion of the maamar *Mayim Rabim Lo Yuchlu Lechabos Es Ha'ahavah* (Many waters cannot extinguish the love).

May it be the will of Hashem that, consistent with this letter, you will also act with all your ability in your own life and affairs to establish this matter: that the "many waters"—which represent all the matters of this world, and clearly the *nefesh habahamit* among them—will not, Heaven forbid, be able to extinguish the love that exists within every single Yid, the natural love for our Father in Heaven. This love is the root for the fulfillment of the 248 *mitzvos aseh* and the mitzvah of *yirah* in its entirety, which is the root for the 365 *mitzvos lo sa'aseh*. It is this love that leads to the actual performance of the *mitzvos*, for "the matter is very close to you, in your mouth and in your heart, to do it," as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 17 and onwards. The matter depends only on one's *ratzon*. And since our Sages have said that the Yidden are the "boldest of the nations," I hope that you will utilize the strength you possess so as not to be impressed by any obstacles or delays, and that you will study with great *hasmadah* and *shekidah* and fulfill the *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5717

5717

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you are in doubt as to whether my instruction has any bearing on your question.

*Hinei*, after asking your forgiveness, I must use the same expression from your letter: it is doubtful whether this has anything to do with your question.

It is **not** a matter of whether one can know Torah Shebichtav by heart, which comes from studying it multiple times in a book.

Your question was why one should not institute the practice of learning Torah Shebichtav by heart (not necessarily from a book). To this, it was pointed out to you that there is a **psak din not** to do so. The primary source was also pointed out, but this is also a law in Shulchan Aruch (Orach Chaim, section 49).

All the examples you bring—that Tannaim and Amoraim knew pesukim from Tanach by heart—are, in truth, a waste of effort, for in every shul you will find Yidden who know Ashrei by heart, and that is not even mentioning Krias Shema, even though everyone knows that this is Torah Shebichtav. But as I said earlier, knowing something by heart is one thing, but establishing a practice of learning by heart is the essence of Torah Shebaal Peh, and **not** of Torah Shebichtav.

It is even more astonishing and strange that, according to your writing that you go through the entire Tanach every two months, how can you challenge an answer before reflecting upon it?

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Avraham HaKohen,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the eve of Friday, in which you describe the morning routine in your Agudah: studying before davening, followed by preparations, including for many of the members, *tevilah* in the *mikveh*, etc.—from which it is understood that because of this, davening begins later. Now, a suggestion has arisen to begin davening two hours earlier in the morning, which would naturally eliminate all the aforementioned activities that have taken place until now before davening. The reason given for this change is so that *tefillah* should be within the time of *Krias Shema*.

It is understood that one should by no means forgo the custom of the elder Chassidim and the *Chassidim v'anshei ma'aseh* regarding the preparations before *tefillah*. Especially since this has been your practice for a long time and it is observed by many, it acquires the sanctity and gravity of a *minhag rabbim* (a custom of the many).

But in truth, one should not have to reach that point at all, taking into account the concept of "Prepare to meet your G-d," as explained at length in the books of *mussar*, *Chassidus*, and *Kabbalah*, and it is simple.

Regarding the question of the time of *Krias Shema*: surely everyone recites *Krias Shema Ketana* at its proper time. Even though each person recites it individually, G-d forbid that one should nullify the matter of *Talmud Torah*, *da'as*, *ratzon*, and preparation for *davening* in the light of morning. For at that time, *idli yoma idli katzira*—the days are short, and the Sages are weary and ailing. Regarding every Jew, King Shlomo says, and in his name: "I am lovesick for the Holy One, Blessed be He, for His Torah, and for His *mitzvos*." As the Sages of blessed memory famously say: "Even though I am asleep in exile, my heart is awake to the Holy One, Blessed be He, to His Torah, and to His *mitzvos*."

May the Almighty help that *tefillah* be with the highest possible preparation, viewing it as the Sages of blessed memory say, that *tefillah* is in place of the *Tamid* offering, which is a *korban olah*, entirely for Hashem. As is well known, there is the scrutiny and caution required for a *korban*, especially since the Sages of blessed memory say that the *Tamid* of the morning atones for the sins of the night, and the *Tamid* of the afternoon for the sins of the day. May it be the will of Hashem that this be fulfilled as the verse says: "A burnt offering, a fire offering, a pleasing aroma to Hashem."

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for him and all his colleagues, for all who fear You and keep Your commandments.

## 5718

19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter in which you ask whether there is already an *aschalta d’geulah* (beginning of the Redemption) or not.

It is surprising that you ask about a matter that is simple and has been ruled upon in *halacha* by the great teacher, the Rambam, at the end of *Hilchos Melachim*. This ruling is based on several verses in the Torah and the Prophets, as well as the words of our Sages, that a king from the House of David will arise, who occupies himself with Torah and engages in *mitzvos*, and will compel all of Israel to walk in its ways and strengthen its breaches (and this is specifically the case), and he will gather the dispersed of Israel—see there, as well as in *Hilchos Teshuvah*, end of chapter 9. We are currently in a *galus* of double and redoubled darkness, **even more so** than the generations before us, since many of the great leaders of Israel have passed on to their rest, etc. And it is not enough that there is darkness in and of itself, but the vision has also been fulfilled: "The heavens are darkened to the light, and the light is turned to darkness."

May it be the will of Hashem that instead of asking questions about these matters, you utilize your time for *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in the study of our holy Torah, both in its revealed aspects and in *Chassidus*, and that you increase in the *hiddur* (beautification) of the performance of *mitzvos*. For every such action adds light to the world, and a little light pushes away even a great deal of darkness, and thereby brings closer the end of the bitter *galus*.

I am sure you are aware of the three daily *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, and in any event, you should observe them from here on in.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Elul, in which you write that you wish to study Nigleh and Chassidus, and that in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) you are unable to fulfill all of this to your satisfaction, and therefore you feel compelled to leave Eretz Yisrael, etc.

The contradiction between the beginning and the end of your statement is obvious. It is simple that even in Eretz Yisrael there exists the commandment of Talmud Torah, which is not dependent on time or place. Those who are there and do not study Torah do not do so because they lack the ability, but rather because of the enticements of the Yetzer Hara, which tempts a person with all sorts of schemes not to fulfill the commandments of the Creator—especially regarding Talmud Torah, which is equivalent to all other mitzvos combined, and in particular regarding the study of the Torah of Chassidus, as is explained in Kuntres Eitz Chaim. What benefit would there be in leaving Eretz Yisrael, seeing as the Yetzer Hara would leave right along with you? It is a pity to incur the expenses, in addition to the matter of leaving Eretz Yisrael, which is only permitted in exceptional circumstances.

May it be the will of Hashem that you recognize the truth as it is—namely, that you have been given the **full** ability to study with consistency and diligence. Every day that passes without this consistency and diligence is a loss that cannot be recovered. If you spend time searching for a reason for the lack of study, there is no need for this at all; the only reason is as mentioned above: the Yetzer Hara. With even a slight amount of contemplation, and for even a short moment, you will see that this is so. May it be the will of Hashem that this realization happens soon, and consequently, that your study begins soon as well.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5717

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 15 Elul, in which you write a brief *cheshbon hanefesh*—or, as you put it, an "inventory." As was also discussed at the *farbrengen* of Chai Elul, it is based on the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that from Chai Elul begin the days of *cheshbon*—one day for each month of the past year.

However, it is a well-known principle of *Chassidus*, which is also a law in the Torah, that *avodah* must be performed with *simcha* and a good heart. Since *cheshbon hanefesh* is also one of the ways of *avodas Hashem*, it too must be done with *simcha* and a good heart. The main point, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, says in the name of his father, the Rebbe, is that there is a criterion to determine from which side a matter originates, as printed in *Hayom Yom* for 23 Sivan.

Regarding specific ideas in your letter, I have enclosed the *Kovetz Lubavitch*. In several of the *mili d'meilyusa* there, you will find the answer to this. Primarily and above all, as mentioned above, any thought or matter that hinders *maaseh b'poel* does not come from the side of good, etc.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of *Yisroel* for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

With blessings for true expansion and for success in all your affairs.

## 5755

B"H, 19 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos: It is surprising that you did not confirm receipt of my letter responding to your previous one. Nevertheless, I have strong hope that you acted in accordance with the instruction of our Alter Rebbe, and that you fulfilled it completely, without being enticed by the temptations of the *kluginker* (the "clever one"). As is well known, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the father of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe), is that sometimes the *yetzer hara* dresses itself in a silk garment; see also *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan.

Regarding the question in your current letter—which is also puzzling—you ask: since there is a *mitzvah* of *yibum*, why did our Sages say that if the man is old and the woman is young, we tell him, "Go to one like yourself," thereby seemingly changing the will of Hashem?

In truth, this is not a change at all. The instruction to "go to one like yourself" is also a command from Hashem for the specific case of *yibum* when the ages are not compatible. It is as if one were to ask how a *mitzvah aseh* (positive commandment) can override a *mitzvah lo taaseh* (negative commandment), or how *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life) overrides Shabbos, thereby "changing" the command of Hashem. The examples are too numerous to count.

In any event, I am certain that from here on, you will keep up with your *Chitas* (*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, *Tanya*) studies, in addition to your regular Torah study.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5757

5757

B”H, 20 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R’ Michael Yehuda Aryeh Leib Hakohen,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month and the 14th of Elul: I was very pleased to hear that you have begun teaching in Zarnuga. It is absolutely clear that your decision to move to Zarnuga is entirely correct, both from the perspective of the collective and the individual. May it be the will of Hashem that others see your example and do the same regarding the acceptance of the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos. This also includes accepting the yoke of supporting our holy educational institutions, which were founded and are directed by our Rebbeim, the Nesi’im. You will surely succeed in Zarnuga; for the toil, there is a reward—and in the way of the Ribono shel Olam, which is measure for measure, but many times over. May you see much Chassidishe nachas together with your wife, long may she live, and all your children, long may they live.

I have not yet received reports regarding the *Kinus HaTemimim*, but it seems that this time, too, the preparation was **lacking** in advance. Due to the shortage of time, it appears that not all the details were secured (*baovarent gevoren*), especially the participation of all the *Temimim* currently in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. This is despite the fact that the time was more appropriate for this—during the days of Elul, the period marking sixty years since the founding of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. [It is worth noting the concept that "sixty is the domain of *Malchus*," and the statement of our Sages (*Bava Basra* 157b) that the cycles of the Oral Torah spanned sixty years. Similarly, although I am not certain of the accuracy of all the details in *Shivchei HaBesht*—even though, as written there, the majority is based on the words and stories of the Alter Rebbe—there is certainly a foundation for it, especially for those matters that serve as the basis for several stories, in addition to the core subject. My intention is to what is brought there, that the Baal Shem Tov said that if the *Goel Tzedek* does not come within sixty years, he must then come into this world. Further on, it is heard from others that he said explicitly that after sixty years he would come again into this world. Chassidim tell of a saying of the Mitteler Rebbe regarding this, etc. Since I did not hear this from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and in any case not from an absolute authority, I am not transcribing it; perhaps you know more details about this.] I will await detailed reports from the *Kinus*, as well as what you wrote regarding the fact that you surely gathered on Chai Elul and will gather also on *Shabbos Mevarchim*—with the help of Hashem—of the month of Tishrei and throughout the entire year.

Primarily, as I have written to several of *Anash* regarding the preparation of a detailed plan to utilize the days of the upcoming month of Tishrei, and the days before and after them, **as much as possible** within the framework of *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* and the framework of *Anash* in general. May it be the will of Hashem that the news be good, in true goodness, as the Sages say (*Kiddushin* 41a), "good to Heaven and good to people." Note also what is explained in the *Maamar* entitled *Kol HaMerachem Al HaBriyos* (Kuntres 61).

Approaching the New Year, which comes upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good news as mentioned above.

## 5717

5717

B"H, 20 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 19 Elul. At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for *menuchas hanefesh* and for the *moach shalit al halev* (the mind to rule over the heart), etc. As the Alter Rebbe writes, *moach shalit al halev* is the natural state and inherent quality of a person. Especially as I told you when we met, you have **absolutely nothing** to overthink, for the world is led by the Ribono shel Olam, who is the essence of good, and He oversees everyone with *hashgacha pratis* for their ultimate good. Therefore, it is a waste of time to debate this, for it is a clear and absolute truth, and it is explained extensively in our Torah—Toras Chaim in general—and even more emphatically in the Chassidus of the Baal Shem Tov, the Alter Rebbe, and their students and their students' students.

You should have found an opportunity to teach Torah in public, and in these days it is also important to study the *dinim* of the upcoming days of Tishrei and the like. Be happy and joyous, as we say in the *tefillah* every day: "Therefore we are obligated to thank... how fortunate are we, how good is our portion," etc. This is especially true when one also recalls the concepts of Chassidus and the light that the Rebbes have infused into them. As I mentioned above, I do not mean that you should overthink this, for this is a matter that is simple in the extreme; rather, the mere thought of this is enough for you to cease worrying entirely and to be *samayach u'vatuach* (joyful and confident) in the Creator of the world and its Guide.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 5717

B"H, 22 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the alarming event that your daughter has converted, may Hashem protect us.

At a time of favor, I will mention this at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

In many cases, such an alarming event is a result of the fact that the child was not conceived in purity—that at the time the mother conceived her, they were not careful regarding the laws and regulations of *taharas hamishpachah*. If, Heaven forbid, this is the case in your situation, then you must firmly resolve that from now on you will be careful regarding the laws and regulations of *taharas hamishpachah* as required by our Torah, the Torah of life, and also influence others to be careful in such matters, which will serve as a partial rectification for the past. May Hashem, who sees into the heart, see that you have truly resolved this and will indeed conduct yourselves accordingly, in addition to observing the *mitzvos* in general; through this, the blessing of Hashem will increase in what you need, and specifically regarding the matter of your daughter.

It is also appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to law, and remove from your home anything that has even a trace of *avodah zarah*, Heaven forbid.

It is understood that you must also investigate and inquire whether there is an overt cause for the aforementioned, such as poverty or the like, and endeavor to remove that cause. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings regarding the above.

With blessings for good news and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 5760

B"H, 23 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, in which you write regarding the lack of discipline as much as is necessary, etc.

You should certainly consult with the educators on-site, as much of this depends on the character traits of the inhabitants of each country and its youth. The common denominator in every place is to appoint mashgichim for discipline from among the students themselves—specifically from among those who are not so disciplined. If possible, [use] a method of a new *parnas* or similar, and when they themselves become interested in the discipline, it is in accordance with the words of our Sages, "From his own wood, the axe handles are made..."

And approaching the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 5761

B"H, 24 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter... in which you write regarding the matter of Rabbeinu Tam tefillin.

As explained in various places, tefillin in general represent *mochin*, and Rabbeinu Tam tefillin, in Kabbalah, represent the letters of the *mochin* of *Abba*. As is understood from other places, the *mochin* of *Abba* relates to the *pnimiyus haTorah*. From this, it is understood that the *tikkun* regarding the aforementioned should be twofold:

a) To establish a *shiur* in the *halachos* of tefillin, regarding which it is said, "Whoever engages in the Torah of [the *mitzvah*]..."

b) To establish an additional *shiur* in the study of *Toras HaChassidus*. And may *Hashem* help that both these matters should be with *hatzlachah*...

#### ***5761***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 9, p. 259.

**Rabbeinu Tam tefillin:** See also above, letter 5759, and the references in the notes there. Above, Vol. 13, letter 4808.

## 5717

B"H, 26 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Elul, the month of mercy, in which you write regarding the doctor’s opinion concerning your health, and that there are those who advise heart surgery.

It is understood that the decision in this matter depends, in general, on the level of expertise of those providing the advice. Especially in your situation, as according to the information here, great experts in cardiology from abroad also visit Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and they hold consultations together with the experts in Eretz Yisrael. It would be worthwhile for you to clarify whether such a consultation is possible in the near future. You should then ask the doctor among your acquaintances to be examined by the aforementioned experts, so that their guidance may be known. May it be the will of Hashem that they succeed in their advice for your swift recovery.

Regarding what you wrote about a shidduch and whether you need to disclose the aforementioned situation, etc., you should ask for the opinion of a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* (halachic authority) in your vicinity.

You are surely aware of the three daily study portions that are appropriate for every person—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and at the very least, you should keep up with them from now on.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

## 5764

B"H, 26 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed, regarding the shortcomings in the branch of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad... and your opinion that everything depends on having a suitable, energetic secretary, and you write that although he continues his activities, he lacks sufficient energy, etc.

Now, time is a loss that cannot be recovered. From this it is understood that even if we assume you are one hundred percent correct, you must work until you find someone better than him. Especially since there is room to say that he, too, possesses this ability and energy, and lacks only a push and experience. In such matters, even a push from within—that is, from the person himself—is sufficient, especially since in such cases, the merit of the many assists him.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that he, as well as all his colleagues *sheyichyu*, utilize these *yimei haratzon* (days of favor) in which we find ourselves, when the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, is in the field and receives every person with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, as explained in *Likutei Torah*. Following this are the days of the drawing of the *Maor* (the Luminary) to the *nitzotz* (the spark). It is explained, and we see tangibly, that these are general days; therefore, every addition during this time is multiplied many times over in the days of the coming year. And if even the head of a well is appointed from Heaven, how much more so a secretary in matters of Yiddishkeit, and at the central point, matters of *D'Chassidus*. May Hashem help him to spread light around his environment and within himself as well, in a manner of "moistening in order to moisten others," and from him and from them, the Supernal Name will be praised.

Approaching the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 5765

B"H, 26 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

***

Regarding the text of *Me'ein Shalosh*: if one should change it in Eretz Yisrael to say *pri gafnah* and *me'einasah*, etc. — see *Ketzos HaShulchan*, end of section 2 in *Badei HaShulchan* there (and according to what is written there, one should not change it close to the conclusion of the blessing, even regarding fruits. Yet he contradicts himself in what he writes at the end of Volume 6). See also the book *Eretz Yisrael* by Rabbi Tukcinsky, **and the sources cited there.** However, it requires further study (*tzarich iyun gadol*) whether the premise of what is written in *Badei HaShulchan* is correct, as it seems to me that the Alter Rebbe is sparing in bringing rulings that were not explicitly stated in the books before him (similar to the approach of the Rambam). Especially those that were not customary "in our lands" (as noted in *Ketzos HaShulchan* Vol. 6 there, regarding *Birchas HaNehenin* Chapter 6, and in the *Kuntres Acharon* to the Alter Rebbe’s *Shulchan Aruch* 507 — and perhaps for this reason he did not include the blessing for a rainbow in *Birchas HaNehenin* in that *siman*). And why should one deviate from the general custom because of a proof that is open to doubt? Perhaps there is a *kabbalah* among *anash* in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, from the early Chassidei Chabad who settled there?

Regarding the wrapping of the *tallis gadol* — I wrote in *Hayom Yom* exactly as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told me.

## 5717

B"H, First Day of Selichos, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter in which you write about your activities during the vacation period.

Naturally, you acted in accordance with my opinion, and I am one hundred percent in agreement with your decision to take upon yourself the lectures you write about, and even more so regarding your speaking with them about practical mitzvos. Furthermore, and most importantly, *yashar koach* to you for being, as you write, the connector between anash and the various groups that visit there.

Regarding what you write about the concept of "Israeli consciousness" (*toda'ah yisraelit*): I have already expressed my opinion and explained it several times. The greatest danger lies in imprecise concepts such as this, especially concepts that have only recently been introduced into the language. Since the majority of newspapers, pamphlets, and books published are in the hands of those who, for the time being, do not follow the path of Torah and mitzvos, they use these concepts to blur and confuse minds more and more. Often, they exploit them as a bridge from the right to the left, similar to the Conservative movement and, in general, movements of compromise in religion that serve as a bridge in **one** direction: on a downward slope from top to bottom and from right to left. They have not saved souls for religion and Torah—not in the slightest. As I have seen in several periodicals regarding the aforementioned concept of "Israeli consciousness," it is already being used as a substitute for all the holy things of the people of Israel. They inject into this matter vain thoughts which, not only are they of no benefit for improving the relationship between a Jewish person and the G-d of Israel, but they are not even of any benefit for improving the relationships between one Jewish person and another.

It is written in the sefarim that in the final moments of the galus, the darkness will be doubled and redoubled until the lowest level, and this itself is a sign that we have reached the lowest level and in another moment the Geulah will begin.

My intention here is regarding the well-known holy declaration that "Torah shall go forth from Tzion and the word of Hashem from Yerushalayim." Never have Tzion and Yerushalayim been used to increase the darkness and the galus as they have in recent years, and specifically in recent months. This is not merely in the sense of the place itself, but also in the sense of the concept. In New York, and according to my information in other countries abroad as well, the concepts of "Tzion and Yerushalayim" are being used to distance Bnei Yisrael even further from the matters of Torah and the word of Hashem. It appears that the fate of the concept of "Israeli consciousness" is liable to be similar, unless its content is defined decisively and unequivocally. Furthermore, one must define the boundaries: in which area will it bring benefit, to which area does it have no relevance, and in which area is it a danger to the existence of the nefesh elokis, which is the essence and vitality of every single Jewish person in all places and at all times.

It is my hope that you will not take offense at these expressions, for with even slight contemplation, one realizes that they are not at all sufficient given the seriousness of the matter. This is especially true when considering several articles that have recently appeared in print, whose intent is clear: that the matter is [only] that "the Merciful One desires the heart," and there is no need, Heaven forbid, for the Torah of Moshe given from Sinai and its instructions for human life, because there is a general concept for the people of Israel, and that in the end of days it will also be universal for all nations—and that is "Israeli consciousness." The details are vague and sealed for now, but apparently, they do not burden a person with matters of positive mitzvos or negative mitzvos, and *d'l* (a word to the wise).

However, since we are promised that in the final moments of the galus, things will be clarified, refined, and purified, etc., one must hope that this blurred concept will also be clarified and refined—and the sooner, the better.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express to you and all those associated with you my blessing: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With esteem and blessing for good tidings regarding the above.

## 5717

B.H., 27 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, etc., R' Shazar, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Following up on my last letter regarding the housing issue in Kfar Chabad, I have just learned of a new possibility which, if accurate, could resolve the housing question in the Kfar. Although I do not yet have the specific details, in general terms, it is as follows: if there are individuals willing to lend money for a period of years for the construction of apartments in housing projects, they receive a guarantee from the Treasury that the loan can be repaid in the foreign currency in which it was given. Furthermore, it seems they also receive a separate mortgage to secure the investment. As I was told, negotiations have already been conducted on this matter with Mr. Eshkol. It also appears that the terms of the Treasury’s guarantee are that the construction of the housing will be in a location chosen by the lender or his representative, and the repayment will be in that same location and in the currency from which the loan originated—that is to say, in New York and in dollars, if the loan is from here.

Now, if the above information is accurate, then despite the difficulties involved, it is possible that I could find specific lenders under these terms for housing in Kfar Chabad. Naturally, the residents of this housing project, in addition to vacating their previous apartments, would need to pay for their new apartments—or at least a large portion of their cost—though they would receive concessions regarding the repayment terms over a period of years.

It goes without saying that I do not wish to trouble you to provide me with all the details regarding this possibility, as that can be done by others. However, I would like to hear your opinion on the matter in general, and whether you find it favorable in principle. If your outlook on this is positive, I will request that the members of the Village Committee visit you at a time and place convenient for you, so that you can instruct them on what they must do regarding the technical side of this matter.

You are surely familiar with the story of two people from the Pale of Settlement who visited Paris and were asked what they saw there. One related that the city, G-d save us, was full of places of impurity, etc., at every step. The second related with excitement that even there, one encounters our brethren, the Children of Israel, at every step, hears words of Torah, and seizes blessings and holiness, etc. Both spoke the truth; the difference lies in what one is looking for, for that is what one finds.

I have accustomed myself to look for the matter of Hashgacha Pratis in everything, as is well known—the emphasis of the teachings of Chassidus on this point is that Hashgacha Pratis exists even in the minute details of the inanimate, the vegetative, and the animal, and all the more so among human beings and significant events. And now, thank G-d, good tidings have reached me one after another: the news that a significant sum is being returned to the Kfar all at once, and subsequently, a personal message from our friend, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and energetic man of noble character, etc., R' P. Althaus, may he live, who met with you and heard your positive opinion regarding the housing project. It appears this was even before my letter was received, and on that very day, I also received the aforementioned news regarding loans for the stated purpose. And thus, "by three testimonies shall the matter be established."

And from one subject to another: in addition to giving thanks for the personal message—first through Rabbi Nachum Rabinovich, may he live, and now through R' P. Althaus, may he live—I offer special thanks for your attention and your most important gift, the manuscript. Although I have not yet had the time to examine it properly and compare it to the printed manuscripts, it appears to be the Siddur of the Arizal. It is especially timely, for the month of Elul’s motto is, "Seek My face; Your face, Hashem, I will seek." At a time when a person searches for his own inwardness, the path to this is to consider not only the Elokus that is revealed—which is manifested through His actions and conduct in the world—but also "Your face, Hashem," the inwardness from Above, before which the world and all that fills it is considered as nothing. Through this, the inwardness within the world is also revealed, which, even in relation to it, the world and all that fills it—as perceived in its externality—is also considered as nothing. And precisely there is a world that is entirely good and beautiful. Only through this does one find peace of mind—not the peace of mind of the people of India, if one may make the distinction, which is a cessation and a standstill, but the rest to which the Children of Israel aspire, which is an ascent "from strength to strength," toward the perfection of good and beauty.

I will conclude with a blessing for the year, as we approach the new year that is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing: a blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing.

## 5717

B"H, 28 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of silences, your letter of 23 Elul was received, along with the enclosure. In it, you ask about what we discussed when you were here some time ago: when a person is stirred from Above with a thought of teshuvah toward Torah and mitzvos, how must one anchor this awakening so that it remains lasting, and how is this anchoring achieved?

The matters mentioned are based on what our Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, writes in his book Likutei Torah, Vayikra 2, 3. Please study it there. It is understood that the anchoring must be through a matter of the lower realm—that is, through the actual practice of Torah and mitzvos. It is also understood that the more prolonged and stronger the connection, the greater and more sustained the effect of the awakening will be. Furthermore, it is understood that the "old and foolish king" does not cease his war, even during such a time of awakening. He has various methods of seduction, both by inflating a person's ego and by demeaning him—telling him, "Who are you, and what good will your efforts do?" and so on, as is clearly evident. Knowing that these arguments come from him can add to one’s resolve not to listen to these enticements, and not to waste time debating with him.

It is surprising that you do not mention your order of study in Torah in general, and in Chassidus in particular; surely you will fill this in at the next opportunity.

The *pidyon nefesh* enclosed in your letter will be read at a time of favor at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that was mentioned.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*, and for the study of the revealed and hidden Torah with *yiras shamayim*.

## 5771

B"H, Selichos Days, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Standing on the threshold of the new year, in these days of *cheshbon hanefesh*—for the individual as an individual, and as a part of the collective—contemplating the concept of *olam katan zeh ha'adam* (man is a microcosm) can shed much light on the purpose and goal of man in the *olam gadol* (the macrocosm).

In the human body, there are shared functions that involve the participation of many organs, as well as specialized functions for each organ individually. Naturally, the specific task of an organ requires a special exertion, whereas the shared functions are carried out much more easily.

What would happen if an organ ceased to function as an individual unit and instead directed all its energy toward working in partnership with other organs?

At first glance, it might seem that this would be a gain—both for the organ in question, by saving special effort, and for the body, as the organ would be able to increase its share in the collective work and not be separated from the other organs.

In reality, however, this would be catastrophic for both: the organ that stops performing its unique function loses its entire essence, which is bound specifically to that unique task. Furthermore, ceasing its normal function weakens the organ until it becomes entirely useless—not only for performing its own functions but even for contributing to the body as a whole. The deficiency in the organ in question must inevitably affect and damage the entire body, and the results can be very serious if the organ in question is a vital one.

What has been said regarding the organs of the body is also true regarding the situation of every individual within his group; a group within a nation; and a nation within humanity at large. This is certainly true in our case, in connection with a Jew, a Jewish community, and *Klal Yisrael* among the nations of the world.

The Jewish people, who have long been characterized as "the fewest of all peoples," are a small minority among the nations. The Jew, as an individual, is a minority in his environment; unfortunately, even among his own brothers, it happens that a Jew who lives as a Jew ought to live—that is, in accordance with the Torah and *mitzvos*—is also, to our regret and sorrow, not in the majority, because the majority has not yet oriented itself as to what its true task is.

It is naturally easier to determine the specific function of an organ in the body than that of a nation among nations. But in the case of our people, Israel, this is not difficult at all, taking into account that Jews are unique in the world with their diverse, extreme experiences and multi-millennial history. Through simple observation, one can quite easily find the *tzad hashaveh* (common denominator), the characteristic trait that has always been present among Jews throughout the various eras and experiences, to which the very essence and existence of our people is bound.

An objective overview, without prejudice, of the long Jewish history must lead to the conclusion that the existence of our people is certainly not connected with material well-being or physical power. Even in the best of times, under the unified kingdom of King Solomon, the Jewish people and kingdom—politically and economically—were small in comparison to the world empires of that time: Egypt, Assyria, and Babylon. It is also clear that neither statehood nor geographical territory has secured our existence, for our history as a people with a state on its own land is very short in comparison to our history in *galus*, without a kingdom and without a land. Likewise, language cannot be considered a vital element of our existence, for even in ancient times, Aramaic occupied the place of the national language; parts of *Tanach*, almost the entire *Talmud Bavli*, the *Zohar*, and so on, were written in the Aramaic language. In the times of Rav Saadia Gaon and the *Rambam*, Arabic was the language of the greatest Jewish masses, and later, Yiddish and other languages. Nor can it be said that a certain general culture or science has secured the existence of our people, for that has changed radically from one era to the next.

There remains only one thing that is a *tzad hashaveh* for all times, all countries, and all circumstances of our history—the Torah and *mitzvos*, which Jews have guarded in their daily lives with the greatest *mesiras nefesh*.

Certainly, there have been, from time to time, individuals or groups who have deviated from the path of Torah and *mitzvos*. In the times of the First Temple, there were the idolaters of Baal, etc.; in the time of the Second Temple—the *misyavnim* (Hellenists), the assimilators of Alexandria, the Karaites, and so on. But all of these have disappeared entirely from the life of the Jewish people (after causing pain and suffering not only to themselves but also to *Klal Yisrael*). Only the golden chain of Torah and *mitzvos* has not been broken, and with Torah and *mitzvos*, our people have traversed the long road from Mount Sinai to this very day. Anyone with *seichel yashar* (common sense) who admits the truth must come to the conclusion that the existence and very essence of our people is bound to a life of Torah and *mitzvos*, for "they are our life and the length of our days."

From this comes the logical conclusion:

The ideology of *nihiyeh k'chol hagoyim* (to be like all the nations) not only cannot help secure our existence, but it actually places the very existence of *Am Yisrael* in danger, *chas v'shalom*. By imitating the non-Jewish world, one will not purchase their friendship; on the contrary, one will only increase their hatred.

Likewise, those Jews or Jewish circles who seek to find favor in the eyes of the *chofshim* (the secular) through compromises and concessions in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—not only do they weaken their own positions and strengthen the forces of the *chofshim*, placing the very existence of *Klal Yisrael* in danger, *chas v'shalom*, but even the expected "gains" are nothing more than illusions and self-deception. For instead of closeness and respect, such an approach evokes only contempt and mockery—and rightly so. For a small compromise today leads to a larger compromise tomorrow, and a compromise today in *mitzvos* that are *bein adam lamakom* (between man and Hashem) leads to a compromise tomorrow in *mitzvos* that are *bein adam lachaveiro* (between man and his fellow). Firmness in accepting "I am Hashem your G-d" and "Remember the Shabbos day to keep it holy" also maintains the observance of "Do not murder" and "Do not steal."

In this current time of *cheshbon hanefesh*, surely our brethren, the children of Israel, wherever they may be, may Hashem preserve them and grant them life—both individuals and groups and movements (and the larger the group, the greater its possibilities and, simultaneously, its responsibility)—will reflect seriously and make a *cheshbon-tzedek* (an honest accounting), with the full recognition of reality and the absolute truth:

That the existence of our people depends entirely and only on the observance of Torah and *mitzvos* in daily life, by the individual and by the community.

The secret of our existence as a people is "a people that dwells alone"—that every individual, man, woman, and child, serves only Hashem Echad, according to our *Torah Achas*, which is eternal and cannot be changed, *chas v'shalom*. Our "otherness" is not our weakness, but our strength. Only through the path of Torah and *mitzvos* can we fulfill our primary and essential task, which is, according to the command of the Creator of the entire world, to be a "kingdom of priests and a holy nation," and through this, also a "treasure" for all of humanity.

With a heartfelt wish for a *kesiva v'chasima tova* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

**Menachem Schneerson**

**M. Schneerson**

The letters from the 16th and 22nd of Elul, as well as the book *Sippurei Chassidim*, Vol. 2, were received. Many thanks, many thanks.

By the way: The version that is widespread, that the interlocutor of the Alter Rebbe regarding the Napoleonic wars was the holy Rav, etc., Maharash of Karlin, is also copied in the aforementioned book.

This is incorrect, according to what is brought in *Seder HaDoros*, that the aforementioned was killed *al kiddush Hashem* **many** years before that war.

I believe I saw some time ago in a certain book that pointed this out. Some say that the interlocutor was the Maggid of Kozhnitz.

Regarding the book *Archei Kabbalah* — it is surprising that he did not also include the book *Pri Etz Chaim*. It would be appropriate to complete it now, at any rate.

Between us: The author employs a strange "caution." For example, *Abba* is arranged after... *Aba*! Apparently, this is because in most printings it is printed as an acronym. *Nekud*, *nekudah*, *nekudos* — arranged in three separate entries! And so on. Nevertheless, due to the scarcity of books of this type regarding Kabbalah, it would be worthwhile to publish it if the means for doing so can be easily found, even if only as an additional reminder regarding the subject of *pnimiyus haTorah*.

#### ***5772***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 26, p. 520, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**Regarding the book *Archei Kabbalah*:** In manuscript, which was authored by one of the residents of Jerusalem, and sent to the Rebbe by R' S.Y. Zevin.

## 5717

Regarding your question on how to conduct yourself with those who disparage matters of Yiddishkeit: It is appropriate not to enter into a *shakla-vetarya* or *pilpul*. Since the majority of those who act as mentioned do so because of the *midos* in their heart and not because of the *sechel* in their mind, in the vast majority of cases this is a result of disappointment and dissatisfaction with the order of their lives. Therefore, after they finish speaking, you should say to them calmly that even for the sake of a *safek* or a *safek-sfeika*, it is worthwhile for them to conduct themselves according to the traditional way of life. For it is obvious that this does not go against the conscience of one who says with his mouth that he does not believe, yet nevertheless puts on tefillin, eats kosher, and so on. And regarding the *yetzer hara’s* claim that such conduct is hypocrisy, the answer for them is that they are not deceiving their surroundings for some material gain, since, unfortunately, the observance of *mitzvos* does not always bring additional honor from one’s surroundings. And even according to his own opinion, it is worth doing for the sake of a *safek*, and there is truly no hypocrisy in this at all. For in essence, a Jewish person wants to fulfill all the *mitzvos*, and it is only that his *yetzer* has coerced him (Rambam, *Hilchos Geirushin*, end of chapter 2). When he fulfills them in practice, he is actually performing an act that he yearns for with every point of his soul—the inner depths of the heart—and *kal v’chomer* (it is understood).

## 5717

1. The mind (of the Shulchan Aruch) is not at all comfortable with the concealment of excess weight when traveling by airplane—that is to say, avoiding payment for it. This constitutes receiving a service (unlike the concealment of customs duties, which is also a matter requiring further study), and it is certainly not permitted.

2. It is surprising that you mention only one blessing, etc., even though several blessings are enumerated in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, section 561.

And now it is even more relevant—to refute the opinion of those who say that the U.N. resolution in 1948 nullified these blessings.

(You surely saw other cities of Judea before you saw Jerusalem, unlike what is mentioned in section 3 above. In general, the aforementioned section 3 refers to the **Old** City of Jerusalem, and that is only seen when ascending Mount Zion; regarding the New City, it is a subject of dispute.

The places where the cities of Judea were previously located, many of which are certainly situated between Lod and Jerusalem.)

3. It is also surprising that you apparently did not take the opportunity to recite the blessing for the separation of Terumos and Ma'asros.

4. It is not mentioned whether you increased your involvement in Torah and Mitzvos each day during your stay there. When one is elevated by the holiness of a place, one must increase the holiness of one's conduct for as long as one remains in that place.

5. May it be the will of Hashem that the love for the Holy Land with which you conclude will arouse you to your mission within Klal Yisrael: to "make this place Eretz Yisrael" **in your own location**, as per the well-known instruction of the Tzemach Tzedek.

## 509

[5717?]

I was alarmed yesterday when his brother told me during our conversation that his father, may he be well, is purchasing a ticket for him on a ship where the entire crew are Bnei Yisrael, and which will be underway during Shabbos Kodesh—meaning, a public chillul Shabbos Kodesh by hundreds of Yidden, Rachmana litzlan. Furthermore, there is also the matter of chillul Hashem in the name of Klal Yisrael, since they proclaim that the ship and its revenue—which includes the pounds his father paid—benefit Klal Yisrael, and these pounds are paid for melachos d’oraisa that are forbidden on Shabbos and are performed on the ship’s engines by Bnei Yisrael, Rachmana litzlan, and are done openly for all to see [except that there are those who have no knowledge of the ship’s engines as they actually function **now**, and they state the **opposite** of the reality that is **tangibly** visible, claiming that there is no melacha that desecrates the Shabbos on ships that are underway during the day of Shabbos].

It is understood that I said all of the above to his brother, may he be well—although I did not see any benefit in emphasizing to him the fault of the father who sent him the ticket. However, since he is with his father and is obligated in his honor, he is also obligated for this reason [in a manner of honor according to the command of our Torah] to explain the aforementioned to him and to prevent him from such an action in the future.

It is simple that I am aware that they quote such-and-such a Rav as having permitted this matter. But the words of the Rosh (Bava Kamma, Chapter 4, Section 4) are already known, that the halacha follows Rav in matters of prohibitions and Shmuel in matters of monetary law, because since Shmuel dealt with monetary laws more than Rav, the halacha follows him in that field. And all those in whose name they say they permit the aforementioned—well, (with apologies and their honor remaining in its place), it seems they have **no** knowledge at all of the operation of the engines in the current state, and they are relying on testimony, while we see tangibly the corruption that has been caused by this.

#### ***509***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 16, p. 641.

**On a ship... Bnei Yisrael:** See also above, Letter 534, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 5716

[Elul 5717?]

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the Torah reading during Mincha on Taanis Tzibur — see what is written on this in the supplement at the end of the *Reshimos* on *Eicha*.

There are several customs regarding the reading of the *Tochachah* (see *Shaarei Ephraim*, Gate 8, Section 23, **and the sources cited there**).

In the *beis medrash* here, the custom is that the *baal korei* goes up on his own (without being called by name) and recites the blessings before and after.
